brown_stock_escoffier.txt - Brown Stock Escoffier Style

Objectives

  • Learn to make a traditional French brown stock from scratch.
  • Understand the layering of flavors in Escoffier's method.
  • Explore the differences between bone broth and brown stock.

Ingredients

  • 1 kg beef bones
  • 150 g carrots, diced
  • 150 g onions, diced
  • 1 bouquet garni (parsley, thyme, bay leaf)
  • 1 garlic clove
  • 2 liters water
  • 500 g veal shanks
  • 500 g chuck beef
  • 200 g pork belly
  • 100 g pork rind
  • Butter or oil

Instructions

  1. Preheat oven to 220°C.
  2. Place beef bones in a roasting tray and roast until lightly browned. Turn bones occasionally for even browning.
  3. While bones are roasting, prepare the aromatics: dice carrots and onions, and create a bouquet garni with parsley, thyme, and bay leaf.
  4. Once bones are browned, add the diced carrots and onions to the roasting tray and toss with a bit of oil. Roast for 5 minutes.
  5. Transfer roasted bones, carrots, and onions to a stockpot.
  6. Deglaze the roasting tray with a little water, scraping up any browned bits, and add this liquid to the stockpot.
  7. Add enough water to the stockpot to just cover the bones.
  8. Add the bouquet garni and garlic clove to the stockpot.
  9. Bring the stock to a simmer and cook for 5-6 hours.
  10. After 5-6 hours, remove the bones and strain the stock through a fine mesh strainer. Discard the bones.
  11. Brown the veal shanks, chuck beef, pork belly, and pork rind in a pan with butter or oil.
  12. Pour the bone broth over the browned meats, ensuring they are covered.
  13. Bring the broth to a boil and reduce to a glaze. Repeat this process two times.
  14. After the second glazing, add the remaining bone broth to the pan.
  15. Simmer the stock for 1 hour.
  16. Remove the meats and strain the stock through a fine mesh strainer. Discard the meats.
  17. The resulting liquid is your Escoffier brown stock.
  18. The stock can be frozen for up to 6 months.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=QxvQMHf_SKw

brunoise_cut.txt - Brunoise Cut

Objectives

  • Learn the brunoise cut, a basic vegetable cut.
  • Understand the importance of precise measurements in the brunoise cut.
  • Understand the differences between brunoise, macedoine, and mirepoix.

Instructions

  1. Prepare a carrot by removing the top and bottom ends.
  2. Cut the carrot into chunks roughly 6-7 cm in length.
  3. Cut the carrot into a square shape.
  4. Slice the carrot into thin pieces, aiming for 2 mm thick slices.
  5. Cut the slices into 2 mm cubes.
  6. Repeat steps 4 and 5 to create a batch of brunoise.
  7. Compare the brunoise cut to the macedoine cut (4 mm cubes) and mirepoix cut (roughly chopped).

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=PemR7OvwilM

bush_eleven.txt - Bush Eleven

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a classic French dish called Bush Eleven.
  • Understand the steps involved in preparing the consomme and veloute.
  • Learn to assemble the dish with a puff pastry casing and a rich chicken and mushroom sauce.

Ingredients

  • 1 whole chicken
  • 1 large piece of string
  • 1 lemon
  • 1 bouquet garni (bay leaf, thyme, celery stalk, parsley stalks)
  • 1 onion
  • 2 carrots
  • 2 leeks
  • 2 celery stalks
  • 2 cloves
  • 10 juniper berries
  • 1 tablespoon black peppercorns
  • 1 package of puff pastry
  • 1 package of mushrooms
  • 40 grams butter
  • 40 grams flour
  • 2 egg yolks
  • 2 tablespoons cream
  • 1 tablespoon cognac
  • 1 tablespoon chopped parsley
  • Salt to taste

Instructions

  1. Truss the chicken using a piece of string to secure the legs and wings.
  2. Rub the chicken with lemon juice to maintain its white color.
  3. Create a bed of vegetables in a large pot: carrots, leeks, celery stalks, onion, cloves, juniper berries, and peppercorns.
  4. Place the trussed chicken on top of the vegetables.
  5. Add enough water to cover the chicken.
  6. Bring the pot to a boil over high heat.
  7. Reduce heat to low and simmer for 40 minutes with the lid on.
  8. While the chicken is cooking, prepare the garnish.
  9. Cut the mushrooms into small cubes.
  10. Roughly chop any leftover mushroom pieces and set aside.
  11. White cook the diced mushrooms by simmering them in water, lemon juice, and a few dashes of butter for 3-4 minutes.
  12. Make a roux by melting butter and whisking in flour. Cook over low heat for 2 minutes, stirring constantly.
  13. Set the roux aside to cool.
  14. Once the chicken is cooked, remove it from the pot and set aside to cool.
  15. Strain the chicken broth through a fine-mesh sieve, discarding the vegetables.
  16. Remove any excess fat from the broth using a kitchen towel.
  17. Heat the chicken broth and reduce it slightly to concentrate the flavor.
  18. Remove the skin and cut the chicken breast into small cubes.
  19. To make the veloute, pour the hot chicken broth into the cooled roux, whisking constantly.
  20. Add the white cooked mushrooms, their juice, morels, diced chicken, cream, and salt.
  21. Simmer the veloute for 20-25 minutes, stirring occasionally, until it thickens.
  22. Stir in cognac and chopped parsley.
  23. Off the heat, whisk in one egg yolk at a time, blending well after each addition.
  24. To assemble the Bush Eleven, warm up the puff pastry casing.
  25. Cut off the top of the casing and empty the inside.
  26. Place a few cubes of chicken at the bottom of the casing.
  27. Pour in the veloute, filling the casing generously with a mixture of mushrooms, chicken, and sauce.
  28. Garnish with the top of the puff pastry casing and serve immediately.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2RDrBZDspXk

button_mushroom_cut.txt - Cutting Button Mushrooms

Objectives

  • Learn four different ways to cut button mushrooms for French cooking
  • Understand the importance of properly washing mushrooms
  • Explore how different cuts affect the flavor and texture of mushrooms in dishes

Ingredients

  • Button mushrooms

Instructions

  1. Wash the mushrooms thoroughly under running water, ensuring to remove any dirt or debris.
  2. Cut off the stems of the mushrooms.
  3. Quartered Mushrooms: Place the mushroom flat on a chopping board and cut it into quarters.
  4. Scalloped Mushrooms: Place the mushroom flat on a chopping board and make a diagonal incision on one side. Turn the mushroom 90 degrees and repeat the process. This cut is best suited for larger mushrooms.
  5. Sliced Mushrooms: Slice the mushroom into thin pieces, aiming to get slices of the white part of the mushroom. This cut is best suited for larger mushrooms.
  6. Dice Mushrooms: Cut the mushroom into small cubes. This cut is best for soups and decorations.

cabbage_soup.txt - Soup au Chou

Objectives

  • Learn to make a classic French cabbage soup, "Soup au Chou"
  • Understand the importance of blanching cabbage for cleanliness and tenderness
  • Discover the traditional method of serving with toasted bread soaked in the soup

Ingredients

  • 1 large head of Savoy cabbage (curly cabbage)
  • 1 large head of white cabbage (cannonball cabbage)
  • 1 large carrot
  • 1 onion
  • 1/2 smoked pork belly
  • Chicken stock (about 2 liters)
  • Butter
  • Salt
  • Pepper
  • Country-style bread

Instructions

  1. Trim off the outer leaves of both cabbages and discard them.
  2. Rinse the cabbages under cold running water.
  3. Cut both cabbages into quarters.
  4. Blanch the cabbage quarters in boiling water with a pinch of salt for a few minutes.
  5. Drain the blanched cabbage and rinse under cold water.
  6. Remove the hard section from the center of each cabbage quarter and discard.
  7. Cut the cabbage quarters into strips of desired width.
  8. Melt butter in a cast iron pot over medium heat.
  9. Add the chopped carrots and half an onion to the pot and sauté for 10-20 seconds.
  10. Add half of the chopped cabbage to the pot and stir.
  11. Layer the smoked pork belly on top of the cabbage.
  12. Add the remaining half of the cabbage and the onion cloves to the pot.
  13. Pour in the chicken stock.
  14. Season with pepper (optional).
  15. Cover the pot and simmer for 1-1.5 hours.
  16. While the soup is simmering, slice country-style bread into chunks and toast in the oven.
  17. Once the soup is cooked, ladle it into bowls.
  18. Place the toasted bread chunks in the soup.
  19. Optionally, add a piece or two of the cooked pork belly to the soup.
  20. Optionally, add a sprinkle of cheese to the bread.
  21. Enjoy the soup with the soaked bread.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=kbDjjS6H9cM

Objectives

  • Explore the pros and cons of using a DSLR vs. a camcorder for a cooking channel.
  • Discuss the features and benefits of a specific camcorder model.

Instructions

  1. Start with an iPhone 6 Plus for the first year of shooting videos.

  3. Transition to a Canon HD XF4 camcorder, specifically designed for video recording, for improved video quality and ease of use.

canadian_leek_bacon_pie.txt - Canadian Leek and Bacon Pie

Objectives

  • Celebrate Thanksgiving in Canada with a delicious and easy-to-make leek and bacon pie.
  • Learn how to make a classic French pie with a shortcrust pastry and savory filling.
  • Enjoy a family-friendly recipe that involves making the dough and filling together.

Ingredients

Pastry: - 2 cups all-purpose flour - 1 teaspoon salt - 1 cup (2 sticks) unsalted butter, chilled and cubed - 1/2 cup ice water

Filling: - 2 tablespoons unsalted butter - 1 medium shallot, finely sliced - 2 leeks, white and light green parts only, thinly sliced - 1/2 cup water - 1/4 cup all-purpose flour - 1 cup heavy cream - 1/2 cup milk - 1/4 teaspoon ground nutmeg - 1/8 teaspoon cayenne pepper - 6 slices bacon, cooked and crumbled - 1 large egg, beaten

Instructions

  1. Preheat oven to 410 degrees Fahrenheit (210 degrees Celsius).
  2. Prepare the pie filling:
  3. Melt butter in a cast iron pan over medium heat.
  4. Add shallots and sauté until translucent, about 2 minutes.
  5. Add half of the leeks and cook until softened, about 5 minutes.
  6. Add the remaining leeks and cook for another 5 minutes.
  7. Add water and bring to a simmer.
  8. Reduce heat to low, cover, and simmer for 30 minutes.
  9. Stir in flour, cream, milk, nutmeg, and cayenne pepper.
  10. Cover and simmer for 10 minutes.
  11. Stir in bacon.
  12. Remove from heat and let cool.
  13. While the leeks are simmering, cook the bacon until crispy and set aside.
  14. Prepare the pie crust:
  15. Roll out the dough into a large disc, about 1/4 inch thick.
  16. Cut the dough in half, one piece for the bottom crust and one for the top crust.
  17. Place the bottom crust in a pie dish and press into the edges.
  18. Trim any excess dough.
  19. Prick the bottom crust with a fork.
  20. Pour the cooled leek and bacon filling into the pie crust.
  21. Roll out the top crust and place it over the filling.
  22. Trim the edges of the top crust and crimp them with the bottom crust.
  23. Make a small vent in the center of the top crust.
  24. Brush the top crust with egg wash.
  25. Bake for 30-40 minutes, or until the crust is golden brown and the filling is set.
  26. Let cool slightly before serving.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=bOLTROXdlVc

caramelized_apple_tart.txt - Caramelized Apple Tart

Objectives

  • Learn a unique, caramelized apple tart recipe from Normandy, France.
  • Discover a "lazy" method of preparing apples for a tart.
  • Explore the origins and history of this regional recipe.

Ingredients

  • 1 kilo apples (about 2.2 lbs)
  • 200g sugar (adjust to taste)
  • 1 lemon (juice and zest)
  • 1 vanilla pod
  • 1 teaspoon cinnamon
  • 25 ml rum (or more to taste)
  • 1 sheet of pre-made puff pastry
  • Water

Instructions

  1. Halve the apples, remove the core, and place them in a bowl of water with lemon juice to prevent browning.
  2. Preheat oven to 180°C (355°F).
  3. Prepare the puff pastry by placing it in a tart pan with high edges. Prick the bottom with a fork to prevent it from puffing too much.
  4. In a saucepan, combine sugar and a small amount of water. Heat over medium heat, stirring constantly, until the sugar melts and begins to caramelize.
  5. Remove the apples from the lemon water and pat them dry.
  6. Add the apples to the caramelized sugar mixture.
  7. Add the vanilla seeds, vanilla pod, cinnamon, and rum. Toss to coat the apples.
  8. Cook the apples over low heat for 10-15 minutes, stirring occasionally, until they soften and release their juices.
  9. Pour the caramelized apples into the prepared tart pan, making sure to include the caramel sauce.
  10. Bake for 35-40 minutes, or until the pastry is golden brown and the apples are tender.
  11. Let the tart cool slightly before serving.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=siL_pp71XY8

caramelized_onions.txt - Caramelized Onions

Objectives

  • Learn how to glaze or caramelize vegetables, specifically onions.
  • Understand the technique for creating glazed and caramelized onions.
  • Discover the versatility of glazed and caramelized onions in French cuisine.

Ingredients

  • Pickling onions
  • Water
  • 20g butter
  • 20g sugar

Instructions

  1. Peel and trim onions to a uniform size, about the size of a small marble.
  2. Place the prepared onions in a small pan.
  3. Add water to the pan, ensuring the water level is just below the top of the onions.
  4. Add 20g of butter to the pan.
  5. Add 20g of sugar to the pan.
  6. Turn the heat to high and bring the mixture to a boil.
  7. Reduce the heat to low and simmer until all the water has evaporated.
  8. Once the water has evaporated, the onions will be glazed.
  9. Continue cooking for a few more minutes to caramelize the onions.
  10. As the onions begin to brown, gently toss them in the pan to coat them in the caramel.
  11. Continue cooking until the onions are a nice brown color, but be careful not to burn them.
  12. Once the onions are caramelized, remove them from the heat and store them in a container.

carbonate_flamand.txt - Carbonnade Flamande

Objectives

  • Learn to make a slow-cooked beef stew with a Belgian twist.
  • Understand the importance of using a dark Belgian beer.
  • Master the layering technique for a flavorful and visually appealing dish.

Ingredients

  • 1 kg chuck steak
  • 4 onions, thinly sliced
  • Parsley, chopped
  • Chives, chopped
  • Tarragon, chopped
  • 1 tablespoon sugar
  • 1 tablespoon vinegar
  • Capers
  • Toasted flour
  • 1 tablespoon butter
  • 1 tablespoon grapeseed oil
  • Salt and pepper
  • 1 bay leaf
  • 400 ml dark Belgian beer (e.g., Chimay)
  • Water

Instructions

  1. Trim excess fat from the chuck steak and cut into slices about half an inch thick.
  2. Season the meat with salt and pepper.
  3. Heat a large pan over high heat and add grapeseed oil.
  4. Sear the meat on both sides until nicely browned.
  5. Remove the meat from the pan and set aside.
  6. Add butter to the pan and sauté the onions for 15 minutes, or until softened and slightly caramelized.
  7. Preheat the oven to 150 degrees Celsius.
  8. While the onions are cooking, toast the flour in a separate pan until lightly browned.
  9. Once the onions are cooked, transfer them to a bowl.
  10. Add the seared meat back to the pan and toss with the toasted flour to coat all sides.
  11. Transfer half of the meat to a large Dutch oven or oven-safe pot.
  12. Layer the caramelized onions over the meat.
  13. Add a layer of chopped herbs (parsley, chives, and tarragon).
  14. Repeat layers with the remaining meat, onions, and herbs.
  15. Sprinkle sugar and vinegar over the top.
  16. Add the bay leaf and capers.
  17. Pour the dark Belgian beer over the ingredients.
  18. Top up with water just enough to barely cover the meat.
  19. Cover the pot and place in the preheated oven.
  20. Cook for 2-3 hours, or until the meat is very tender and falls apart easily.
  21. Once cooked, remove the lid and let the sauce reduce slightly.
  22. Serve the Carbonnade Flamande hot, garnished with additional capers, herbs, and a splash of beer if desired.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-73VoD-9hoY

carrot_soup_escoffier.txt - Potage Purée Crissy à la Briarde

Objectives

  • Learn to make a classic French carrot soup
  • Understand the importance of using high-quality ingredients
  • Master the technique of creating a smooth, velvety puree

Ingredients

  • 4 cups (1 liter) of water
  • 1 tablespoon butter
  • 1 tablespoon oil
  • 1/2 cup onion, thinly sliced
  • 2 carrots, thinly sliced
  • 1/2 cup potato, cubed
  • 1/4 cup bread, cubed
  • 1/2 teaspoon salt
  • 1/4 teaspoon sugar
  • 2 tablespoons creme fraiche
  • Fresh coriander leaves (for garnish)

Instructions

  1. Melt the butter in a saucepan over medium heat.
  2. Add the onion and carrots and cook for 5 minutes, covered, until softened.
  3. Add the water, potatoes, and salt. Bring to a simmer and cook for 15 minutes, or until the vegetables are tender.
  4. While the soup is cooking, heat the oil and butter in a separate pan. Add the bread and cook until golden brown. Drain on paper towels.
  5. Use a stick blender to puree the soup until smooth.
  6. Stir in the creme fraiche, a little at a time, until the desired consistency is reached.
  7. Pass the soup through a fine-mesh sieve to remove any lumps.
  8. Add a knob of butter to the soup and stir to combine.
  9. Serve the soup hot, garnished with croutons and coriander leaves.

carrot_vinaigrette.txt - Carrot Vinaigrette

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a classic French carrot salad.
  • Understand the importance of using fresh ingredients.
  • Master the art of creating simple but delicious dressings.

Ingredients

  • Carrots
  • Parsley
  • Lemon
  • Salt flakes
  • Black pepper
  • Olive oil
  • Red wine vinegar

Instructions

  1. Grate carrots using a food processor with a fine grating blade.
  2. Chop parsley using a food processor.
  3. Make the lemon dressing:
  4. Combine salt, pepper, and the juice of half a lemon in a glass jar.
  5. Add 3 tablespoons of olive oil.
  6. Shake the jar vigorously to emulsify the dressing.
  7. Make the vinegar dressing:
  8. Combine salt, pepper, and 1 tablespoon of red wine vinegar in a glass jar.
  9. Add 3 tablespoons of olive oil.
  10. Shake the jar vigorously to emulsify the dressing.
  11. Toss grated carrots with the lemon dressing.
  12. Refrigerate the carrots until ready to serve.
  13. To serve, place a portion of the carrot salad on a plate.
  14. Season with salt, pepper, a drizzle of lemon juice, and a dash of olive oil.
  15. Garnish with a sprinkle of chopped parsley.
  16. Enjoy!

cassoulet.txt - Cassoulet

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a traditional French Cassoulet dish.
  • Understand the importance of pre-cooking the beans and sausage.
  • Assemble the cassoulet with pre-cooked ingredients for a flavorful and satisfying meal.

Ingredients

  • 10 broad white beans
  • 2 duck confit
  • 1 goose confit
  • 4 eggs
  • 1 sausage de Toulouse
  • 1 pork sausage
  • 1 tablespoon of vinegar

Instructions

  1. Preheat the oven to 220 degrees Celsius (428 degrees Fahrenheit).
  2. Pre-cook the broad white beans in a pot of boiling water for 10 minutes.
  3. Preheat the duck and goose confit.
  4. Pre-cook the Toulouse sausage and pork sausage in the oven for 15 minutes.
  5. Once the sausage is cooked, remove from the oven and set aside.
  6. Add the pre-cooked beans, duck confit, goose confit, and sausage to a large casserole dish.
  7. Pour 1 tablespoon of vinegar into the casserole dish.
  8. Crack 4 eggs into the casserole dish.
  9. Bake the cassoulet in the preheated oven for 15 minutes.
  10. Serve the cassoulet hot and enjoy!

cauliflower_cheesy_gratin.txt - Cauliflower Cheesy Gratin

Objectives

  • Learn to make a simple and delicious cauliflower gratin.
  • Master the technique of making a classic French bechamel sauce.
  • Discover how to infuse flavors into milk for a richer bechamel.

Ingredients

  • 1 head of cauliflower
  • 1/2 onion
  • 1 bay leaf
  • 1/2 teaspoon nutmeg
  • 4 cloves
  • Salt
  • White pepper
  • Cayenne pepper
  • 1 tablespoon butter
  • 2 tablespoons flour
  • 1 cup milk
  • Grated cheese (amount to taste)

Instructions

  1. Wash and cut the cauliflower into florets.
  2. Boil a pot of salted water and add the cauliflower florets.
  3. Cook the cauliflower until tender, about 15-20 minutes.
  4. While the cauliflower is cooking, prepare the bechamel sauce.
  5. Warm the milk in a saucepan over low heat.
  6. Add the onion, bay leaf, nutmeg, cloves, salt, and white pepper to the milk.
  7. Allow the milk to infuse with the flavors for about 5 minutes.
  8. In a separate saucepan, melt the butter over low heat.
  9. Whisk in the flour and cook for 1 minute, stirring constantly.
  10. Gradually whisk the infused milk into the roux, stirring continuously.
  11. Cook the sauce over low heat, stirring constantly, until it thickens.
  12. Remove the saucepan from the heat and stir in a pinch of cayenne pepper.
  13. Drain the cauliflower and rinse with cold water to stop the cooking.
  14. Preheat oven to 180 degrees Celsius (356 degrees Fahrenheit).
  15. In a baking dish, spread a thin layer of bechamel sauce.
  16. Add the cauliflower florets, season with salt and pepper.
  17. Pour the remaining bechamel sauce over the cauliflower.
  18. Sprinkle generously with grated cheese.
  19. Bake for 30 minutes, or until the cheese is melted and golden brown.
  20. Serve hot and enjoy!

cauliflower_prep.txt - How to Prepare a Cauliflower

Objectives

  • Learn to properly prepare a cauliflower from scratch.
  • Understand the importance of removing excess leaves and the root.
  • Learn how to detach cauliflower florets for cooking.

Instructions

  1. Remove excess leaves from the cauliflower by breaking them off.
  2. Cut off the root of the cauliflower using a knife.
  3. Detach the cauliflower florets by carving them off one by one.
  4. Wash the florets in a basin of water to remove any sand or debris.
  5. Store the prepared florets in a clean container for cooking.

champagne_sabayon.txt - Champagne Sabayon

Objectives

  • Learn to make a classic Italian dessert, Champagne Sabayon.
  • Understand the importance of whisking and incorporating air for a light, foamy texture.
  • Discover how to create a beautiful and elegant presentation with a brûlée topping.

Ingredients

  • 125 ml Champagne (sweet or dry)
  • 75 grams Sugar
  • 3 Egg yolks
  • Raspberries
  • Blueberries
  • Lemon zest (optional)

Instructions

  1. Prepare a bain-marie (double boiler) by filling a saucepan with a small amount of simmering water.
  2. In a heatproof bowl, whisk together the egg yolks and sugar until light and frothy.
  3. Add a pinch of lemon zest for extra flavor (optional).
  4. Slowly pour in the champagne while whisking constantly.
  5. Place the bowl over the simmering water and continue whisking vigorously for about 5-10 minutes, until the mixture has tripled in volume and becomes thick and creamy.
  6. Remove the bowl from the heat and place it in a bowl of ice water to stop the cooking process.
  7. Arrange raspberries and blueberries in a shallow dish or cocktail glass.
  8. Pour the Sabayon over the berries, covering them completely.
  9. Use a kitchen torch to brûlée the top of the Sabayon, creating a beautiful caramelized crust.
  10. Serve immediately and enjoy!

cheap_meat_ragout.txt - Cheap Meat Ragout

Objectives

  • Learn to prepare affordable cuts of meat for a delicious ragout.
  • Master the basic ragout technique for future variations.
  • Create a budget-friendly meal for the whole family.

Ingredients

  • 1 onion, roughly chopped
  • 1 celery stalk, roughly chopped
  • 2 carrots, roughly chopped
  • 2 garlic cloves, bruised
  • 1-2 lbs cheap beef cuts (e.g., chuck, brisket, short ribs)
  • Salt and pepper to taste
  • 2 tbsp oil
  • 1 tbsp flour
  • 1 tbsp tomato paste
  • 1 cup red wine
  • 1 cup beef stock
  • 1 tsp honey

Instructions

  1. Roughly chop the onion, celery, and carrots.
  2. Bruise the garlic cloves.
  3. Season the meat with salt and pepper.
  4. Heat the oil in a cast iron pan over high heat.
  5. Brown the meat in batches, ensuring each piece develops a crust.
  6. Add the chopped vegetables and cook for 10 seconds.
  7. Sprinkle flour over the meat and vegetables and cook for 10 seconds.
  8. Add the tomato paste and cook for a few seconds.
  9. Deglaze the pan with red wine, reducing it until almost dry.
  10. Add the beef stock, garlic, and honey.
  11. Transfer the pan to a preheated oven at 170°C (338°F) and cook for 1.5-2 hours, or until the meat is tender.
  12. Once cooked, remove the meat from the pan and strain the sauce through a fine-mesh sieve.
  13. To create variations, add additional ingredients to the sauce, such as tomatoes, rosemary, or mushrooms.
  14. Serve the ragout with the meat, enjoying the tender, flavorful result.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=__9a-lfeGaw

cheese_fondue.txt - Cheese Fondue

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a classic French cheese fondue
  • Understand the importance of using different cheeses for flavor and melting properties
  • Explore the different ways to serve and enjoy cheese fondue

Ingredients

  • 300 grams Gruyere cheese, cubed
  • 300 grams Comté cheese, cubed
  • 300 grams Beaufort cheese, cubed
  • 1 clove garlic, crushed
  • 150 ml dry white wine (such as Sauvignon Blanc)
  • Bread, cubed
  • Optional: cured meats, such as ham or sausage

Instructions

  1. Crush a clove of garlic and rub it inside a cast iron pot.
  2. Pour 100 ml of dry white wine into the pot and heat over medium heat.
  3. Once the wine is warm, start adding the cubed Gruyere cheese, stirring constantly until it melts.
  4. Add the Comté cheese and stir until melted.
  5. Add the Beaufort cheese and stir until melted.
  6. Continue adding cheese in batches, stirring constantly until the fondue is thick and creamy.
  7. If needed, add more wine a little at a time to adjust the consistency.
  8. Serve the fondue immediately with bread cubes and optional cured meats.
  9. Dip the bread cubes into the fondue, using a long skewer or fork.
  10. Enjoy!

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=XX4G7i7YECg

chef_knife_handling.txt - Chef's Knife Handling

Objectives

  • Learn proper and safe handling of a chef's knife.
  • Understand the importance of finger placement and control.
  • Master basic chopping and slicing techniques.

Instructions

  1. Hold the knife with your dominant hand, wrapping your fingers around the handle and placing your thumb on the back of the blade.
  2. Keep your fingers behind the blade at all times, never allowing them to go past the bolster.
  3. Use a rolling motion when chopping, keeping the point of the blade in contact with the cutting board.
  4. Use your non-dominant hand to guide the food, keeping your fingers tucked inwards to avoid injury.
  5. When chopping smaller items like parsley, hold the food in your non-dominant hand and release small pieces as you chop.
  6. For finer chopping, use the tip of the knife and keep your non-dominant hand on top of the blade for control.
  7. When slicing, use a paring knife and make thin incisions along the length of the food.
  8. Clean up any loose pieces of food as you go.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=TGuoE7EBEHU

chicken_and_rice_supreme_escoffier_style.txt - Chicken and Rice Supreme Escoffier Style

Objectives

  • Learn to prepare a classic French chicken and rice dish.
  • Understand the importance of using a homemade chicken stock.
  • Create a rich and flavorful supreme sauce.

Ingredients

  • 1.5 kg whole chicken (approx. 3.3 lbs)
  • 4 cups homemade chicken stock
  • 2 cups jasmine rice
  • 1 cup unsalted butter
  • 2 onions
  • 2 cloves
  • 1/2 cup curly parsley
  • 1/2 cup button mushrooms
  • 1/2 cup heavy whipping cream
  • 1/4 cup chicken essence (concentrated chicken stock)
  • Salt and pepper to taste
  • Bouquet garni
  • Lemon

Instructions

  1. Prepare the chicken by rubbing it with salt, pepper, parsley, and a bouquet garni.
  2. Truss the chicken with kitchen twine.
  3. Rub the chicken with lemon juice.
  4. Place the onions and bouquet garni in a 10-liter stockpot.
  5. Place the chicken on top of the onions.
  6. Pour the chicken stock into the pot, ensuring the chicken is submerged.
  7. Bring the stock to a boil over high heat.
  8. Blanch the chicken wings in boiling water for 1-2 minutes.
  9. Rinse the chicken wings and add them to the stockpot.
  10. Cover the pot and simmer for 45 minutes.
  11. While the chicken simmers, prepare the mushrooms by cooking them in boiling water until they soften.
  12. After 10 minutes, remove the mushrooms from the heat and let them cool.
  13. Prepare the roux by melting butter in a saucepan and whisking in flour.
  14. Cook the roux over low heat for 2-2.5 minutes to remove the raw flour taste.
  15. Set the roux aside to cool completely.
  16. Preheat the oven to 200°C (396°F).
  17. Prepare the rice by combining rice and chicken stock in a saucepan.
  18. Melt butter in a separate pan and sauté onions until translucent.
  19. Add the rice to the onions and coat with butter.
  20. Pour the chicken stock over the rice.
  21. Cover the pan with parchment paper and a lid.
  22. Bake the rice for 20 minutes.
  23. After 45 minutes, remove the chicken from the stockpot and place it on a tray.
  24. Cover the chicken with foil and let it rest.
  25. Strain the chicken stock through a sieve and pour it into a saucepan.
  26. Reduce the chicken stock to 2 cups.
  27. Remove the rice from the oven and fluff with a fork.
  28. Add a knob of butter to the rice and stir to incorporate.
  29. To make the sauce, whisk the cold roux into the hot reduced chicken stock.
  30. Bring the sauce to a boil and simmer for 10 minutes.
  31. Add the concentrated mushroom juice to the sauce and continue to simmer.
  32. Reduce the chicken essence to a tablespoon and add it to the sauce.
  33. Add 2 tablespoons of cream to the sauce and continue to simmer.
  34. Add a few mushrooms to the sauce.
  35. Season the sauce with salt to taste.
  36. Carve the chicken and arrange it on a plate with the rice.
  37. Drizzle the sauce over the chicken and rice.
  38. Garnish with parsley.
  39. Serve immediately.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=s-RirdGBA4g

chicken_bake.txt - Chicken Bake

Objectives

  • Learn a Michelin-star chef's simple chicken bake recipe.
  • Understand how to build layers of flavor in a dish.
  • Master the art of making a bechamel sauce.

Ingredients

  • 1 chicken breast
  • 1 onion
  • Butter
  • Flour
  • Mushrooms
  • Fresh sage
  • Fresh thyme
  • Port wine
  • Milk
  • Cheese
  • Cream (optional)
  • Carrots (optional)

Instructions

  1. Heat butter and oil in a pan over medium-high heat.
  2. Season chicken pieces with salt and pepper.
  3. Sear chicken pieces in the pan until lightly browned on both sides.
  4. Remove chicken from the pan and set aside.
  5. Add onions to the pan and cook over medium-high heat for about 10 minutes, until caramelized.
  6. Remove onions from the pan and set aside.
  7. Add butter and olive oil to the pan and heat over medium heat.
  8. Add sliced mushrooms to the pan, season with salt and pepper, and add fresh thyme and sage leaves.
  9. Cook mushrooms until they release their moisture and are cooked through.
  10. Return caramelized onions to the pan with the mushrooms.
  11. Add port wine to the pan and deglaze, scraping up any browned bits.
  12. Remove pan from heat and set aside.
  13. Make the Bechamel Sauce:
  14. Melt butter in a saucepan over medium heat.
  15. Whisk in flour and cook for 3 minutes until blonde in color.
  16. Gradually whisk in a small amount of cold milk, scraping the bottom of the pan to prevent clumps.
  17. Add remaining milk and bring to a boil.
  18. Simmer for 2 minutes, stirring constantly.
  19. Remove from heat.
  20. Pour the Bechamel sauce over the mushroom, onion, and port mixture.
  21. Stir to combine and add a few tablespoons of cream for a smoother consistency.
  22. Transfer the mixture to a baking dish.
  23. Top with cheese.
  24. Bake in a preheated oven at 350°F (175°C) for 20 minutes.
  25. Broil for 2-4 minutes to crisp the cheese.
  26. Serve immediately.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=xOuQ-3i2KXk

chicken_bery.txt - Chicken Bery

Objectives

  • Learn to make a classic French brown sauce called Sauce Bery.
  • Understand the importance of deglazing in sauce making.
  • Master the technique of sauteing chicken to achieve a beautiful color.

Ingredients

  • 4 chicken thighs
  • 50 grams shallots, finely chopped
  • 100 ml wine (red or white)
  • 400 ml homemade demiglace (or 2 cups store-bought stock)
  • 1 tablespoon parsley, chopped
  • 1 tablespoon oil
  • 20 grams butter
  • 1 1/2 tablespoons arrowroot
  • Salt and pepper to taste

Instructions

  1. Before starting, prepare all ingredients: finely chop the shallots, chop the parsley, and have the stock ready.
  2. Season the chicken thighs with salt and pepper.
  3. Heat a tablespoon of oil and 20 grams of butter in a sauté pan over medium heat.
  4. Add the chicken thighs skin-side down and cook for 5-10 minutes until nicely browned.
  5. While the chicken cooks, reduce the stock by half in a separate pan.
  6. Turn the chicken thighs and continue cooking for another 15-20 minutes, ensuring an internal temperature of at least 75°C.
  7. Remove the chicken from the pan and keep warm in a preheated oven at 50°C.
  8. Add the chopped shallots to the pan and cook over medium heat for 3-4 minutes, or until softened.
  9. Increase the heat to high and deglaze the pan with the wine, scraping up the caramelized bits from the bottom.
  10. Reduce the wine for a minute or two.
  11. Add the reduced stock to the pan, bring to a boil, and reduce for a few minutes.
  12. In a small bowl, mix 1 1/2 tablespoons of arrowroot with a little water to form a paste.
  13. Add the arrowroot paste to the sauce and stir until thickened.
  14. Remove from heat and whisk in 10-20 grams of butter until melted and glossy.
  15. Season the sauce with salt and pepper to taste.
  16. Strain the sauce through a sieve if desired to remove the shallots.
  17. Spoon the sauce over the chicken thighs and garnish with chopped parsley.
  18. Serve immediately.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Ze7LyJVhexE

chicken_breast_papillot.txt - Chicken Breast Papillot

Objectives

  • Learn a simple French recipe for chicken breast.
  • Create a delicious and impressive meal for guests.
  • Explore the versatility of papillot cooking technique.

Ingredients

  • 4 chicken breasts
  • Dijon mustard
  • Crème fraîche (or double cream)
  • Fresh thyme
  • Peppercorns
  • 1 tablespoon olive oil
  • 1 shallot (optional)
  • Parsley (optional)
  • Lemon juice (optional)
  • Olive oil (optional)
  • Salt
  • Pepper
  • 4 squares of parchment paper

Instructions

  1. Preheat oven to 180 degrees Celsius with fan force.
  2. Lightly sear chicken breasts in a frying pan with olive oil for about 5 minutes on each side. This is optional, but adds color and flavor.
  3. While the chicken is searing, prepare the cream and mustard mixture:
  4. Combine crème fraîche, mustard, peppercorns, and salt in a bowl.
  5. Whisk until well combined.
  6. (Optional) Sauté a shallot in the same pan used to sear the chicken. This will capture the fat and meat juices.
  7. Place a piece of parchment paper on a flat surface.
  8. Spread a generous amount of the cream and mustard mixture on one side of each chicken breast.
  9. (Optional) Add a few sprigs of thyme, parsley, and a pinch of salt and pepper to the parchment paper.
  10. (Optional) Drizzle a little lemon juice and olive oil over the herbs.
  11. Place the chicken breast on top of the herbs.
  12. Fold the parchment paper over the chicken, creating a sealed pouch.
  13. Repeat steps 5-10 for the remaining chicken breasts.
  14. Place the sealed pouches in the oven and cook for 20 minutes.
  15. Check the internal temperature of the chicken with a food thermometer to ensure it reaches at least 65 degrees Celsius.
  16. Let the chicken rest for a few minutes before serving.
  17. Cut open the pouches and enjoy the juicy and flavorful chicken.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=f6w04fmbEXQ

chicken_chasseur.txt - Chicken Chasseur

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a classic French chicken stew.
  • Understand the importance of preparing ingredients in advance.
  • Master the techniques of browning chicken, making a brown stock, and thickening a sauce.

Ingredients

  • 4 pieces of chicken
  • 1 tablespoon of oil
  • 1/2 cup of flour
  • 50g onion
  • 50g carrot
  • 2 cloves of garlic
  • 1 tablespoon of tomato paste
  • 1 cup of beef stock
  • 1 tablespoon of butter
  • 1/2 cup of mushrooms
  • 1/2 cup of shallots
  • 1 tablespoon of Cognac
  • 1/2 cup of white wine
  • 1/4 cup of parsley
  • 1/4 cup of tarragon
  • Salt and pepper to taste

Instructions

  1. Prepare all ingredients. Finely slice shallots, roughly chop carrots, remove germ from garlic, trim mushrooms, debone chicken, and chop parsley and tarragon.
  2. Make the stock: Heat oil in a stock pot over high heat. Add the chicken bones and brown them until they are a deep brown color.
  3. Add the onion and carrot to the pot and sweat for 10 minutes.
  4. Deglaze the pot with beef stock and bring to a boil.
  5. Add garlic, bay leaf, mushroom trimmings, and tomato paste.
  6. Cover and simmer for 30 minutes.
  7. While the stock simmers, season the chicken with salt and pepper and dredge in flour.
  8. Heat oil in a cast iron pan over high heat. Brown the chicken on all sides, about 2-3 minutes per side.
  9. Preheat oven to 180°C (350°F).
  10. Transfer the chicken to a baking tray, cover with foil, and bake for 15 minutes.
  11. Remove the bones from the stock and strain the stock through a sieve into a clean pan.
  12. Thicken the stock with a beurre manié (equal parts butter and flour) until it coats the back of a spoon.
  13. In the same pan used to cook the chicken, sauté the mushrooms over medium-high heat for 3-5 minutes.
  14. Add the shallots and cook for 1 minute.
  15. Deglaze the pan with Cognac and ignite it carefully.
  16. Add the white wine and reduce until almost dry.
  17. Add the thickened stock and simmer for 3-4 minutes.
  18. Stir in the parsley and tarragon.
  19. Finish the sauce with a knob of butter and whisk to combine.
  20. Serve the chicken with the sauce, garnished with fresh herbs.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=8HUlxam6X5Q

chicken_fricassee_one_pot.txt - One-Pot Chicken Fricassee

Objectives

  • Simplify a complex French recipe into a one-pot dish
  • Create a subtle chicken flavor profile with a creamy sauce
  • Use a unique technique to mimic traditional roux and stock

Ingredients

  • 5-6 mushrooms
  • A few pickling onions
  • 1 small bunch of thyme
  • 1 carrot
  • 1 egg
  • 50-100 ml cream
  • 100 ml white wine
  • 1 whole chicken, cut into 4 pieces
  • Butter
  • Flour
  • Salt
  • Pepper
  • Water

Instructions

  1. Season chicken pieces with salt and pepper on both sides.
  2. Generously sprinkle flour on each chicken piece.
  3. Melt butter in a cast iron pot over medium heat.
  4. Add chicken pieces skin-side down and cook until lightly browned.
  5. Add butter to the pot and sauté onions and mushrooms until softened.
  6. Return chicken to the pot.
  7. Add another tablespoon of flour and stir to coat the chicken.
  8. Deglaze the pot with white wine.
  9. Add remaining chicken pieces, onions, and mushrooms.
  10. Top with water, ensuring the chicken is barely covered.
  11. Bring to a simmer and add bouquet garni, bay leaf, and sliced carrots.
  12. Simmer for 35 minutes, removing chicken breasts after 15-20 minutes.
  13. Remove chicken legs, neck, and wings and discard.
  14. Discard bouquet garni.
  15. Place chicken pieces in a bowl and drizzle with some of the sauce to keep them moist.
  16. Bring the sauce to a boil to concentrate the flavor.
  17. Stir in cream.
  18. Reduce the sauce for 5-10 minutes, until it coats the back of a spoon.
  19. Whisk an egg yolk with some of the warm sauce.
  20. Turn off the heat and slowly stir the egg yolk mixture into the sauce.
  21. Transfer the sauce to a serving dish and arrange the chicken pieces on top.
  22. Serve with rice.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=bibGnLNYtDQ

chicken_in_beer.txt - Chicken in Beer

Objectives

  • Explore the unique culinary traditions of Northern France.
  • Learn how to make a flavorful and comforting chicken dish using beer instead of wine.
  • Discover the "Pibus" technique for enhancing chicken flavor.

Ingredients

  • 2 kg chicken (or 3 kg rooster if you can find it)
  • 1 liter good quality Belgian beer (Trappist beer recommended)
  • 100g fatty bacon (or lard)
  • 200g mushrooms, roughly sliced
  • 1 large shallot
  • 2 tbsp flour
  • 1 tbsp cream
  • 1-2 tbsp Geneva (or cognac or gin)
  • 3-4 cloves
  • 1 tsp juniper berries
  • 1-2 bay leaves
  • 1 tbsp brown sugar
  • Salt and pepper to taste
  • Parsley for garnish

Instructions

  1. Cut the bacon into chunky pieces.
  2. Heat a large pot over medium heat and add the bacon. Render the fat, then remove the bacon and set aside.
  3. Brown the chicken carcass in the rendered bacon fat.
  4. Remove the carcass and set aside.
  5. Season the chicken pieces with salt, pepper, and flour.
  6. Brown the chicken pieces in the pot, about 5 minutes per side.
  7. Discard any excess fat from the pot.
  8. Add the shallots to the pot and cook for a minute or two.
  9. Deglaze the pot with cognac or Geneva.
  10. Add half of the bacon and the mushrooms to the pot. Cook for a few minutes.
  11. Layer the chicken in the pot, starting with the tougher pieces (carcass, thighs, legs) at the bottom and the breasts on top.
  12. Sprinkle with flour, mixing well.
  13. Add the beer to the pot.
  14. Add the cloves, juniper berries, bay leaves, and brown sugar.
  15. Bring to a boil, then reduce heat and simmer for 15 minutes.
  16. Remove the chicken breasts and transfer to a baking sheet.
  17. Continue simmering the remaining chicken and sauce for another 30-40 minutes.
  18. Remove the chicken from the pot and place in a tray.
  19. Discard the carcass.
  20. Bring the sauce to a boil and add a tablespoon of cream. Reduce the sauce to a desired consistency.
  21. Briefly grill the chicken breasts skin-side up to achieve a crispy skin.
  22. Pan-fry the remaining bacon and mushrooms.
  23. Serve the chicken with the sauce, garnished with pan-fried bacon, mushrooms, and parsley.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=89k6t8oGLqw

chicken_in_cream.txt - Chicken in Cream

Objectives

  • Learn a simple, efficient technique for cooking chicken in cream.
  • Understand the importance of using high-quality ingredients.
  • Discover how to create a rich, flavorful sauce without using traditional stock.

Ingredients

  • 1 whole chicken, cut into 6 pieces
  • 1 tbsp. butter
  • Salt and pepper
  • 1 carrot, halved
  • 1-2 shallots
  • 1 bulb of garlic, unpeeled
  • 250 ml white wine
  • 250 ml water
  • 400 ml heavy cream
  • 2 egg yolks

Instructions

  1. Season chicken pieces generously with salt and pepper.
  2. Heat butter in a large pan over medium-high heat.
  3. Sear chicken pieces for 2-3 minutes on each side, until lightly browned.
  4. Remove chicken pieces from the pan and set aside.
  5. Add chicken carcasses and offcuts to the pan and cook for a few minutes, browning slightly.
  6. Return chicken pieces to the pan and add halved carrot, shallots, and unpeeled garlic bulb.
  7. Pour in white wine and water.
  8. Bring to a simmer, cover, and cook for 20-25 minutes.
  9. Remove chicken pieces and transfer to a serving dish.
  10. Discard garlic bulb and any other aromatics that are too soft.
  11. Increase heat to high and reduce the remaining liquid until thickened.
  12. Whisk 2 egg yolks with a small amount of the reduced sauce.
  13. Remove the pan from heat and whisk the egg yolk mixture into the sauce.
  14. Strain the sauce through a fine-mesh sieve, pressing on the solids to extract all the juices.
  15. Pour the sauce over the chicken and serve immediately.

chicken_in_hay.txt - Chicken Cooked in Hay

Objectives

  • Learn an old-fashioned technique for cooking chicken in a pot with hay.
  • Understand the importance of using the right type of grass for flavor.
  • Discover a unique and flavorful way to cook chicken.

Ingredients

  • 1 chicken (about 1.5 kg)
  • 1 handful of untreated, unsprayed grass
  • 300 grams of flour
  • 150 ml of water
  • Black pepper
  • Rock salt or salt flakes
  • Salted butter

Instructions

  1. Preheat oven to 190 degrees Celsius.
  2. Place a layer of grass in the bottom of a cast iron pot, creating a nest-like shape.
  3. Place the chicken in the nest, ensuring it is touching the grass on all sides.
  4. Make sure the chicken is untrussed so the flesh is exposed to the grass.
  5. Cut away any excess grass with scissors.
  6. Create a dough by combining flour and water, kneading it slightly.
  7. Roll the dough into a long rope, about the length needed to go around the rim of the pot.
  8. Place the dough around the rim of the pot, sealing the top of the pot tightly.
  9. Place the pot in the oven on the middle shelf and bake for 50-55 minutes, or until the dough is golden brown and a hay smell emanates from the oven.
  10. Allow the chicken to rest for 20-40 minutes after removing from the oven.
  11. Carefully break open the dough seal.
  12. Gently remove the chicken from the pot.
  13. If desired, place the chicken under a grill to brown the skin.
  14. Season the chicken with black pepper, rock salt or salt flakes, and melted salted butter.
  15. Carve the chicken and enjoy.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=o5PmxCR-vfQ

chicken_liver_salad.txt - Chicken Liver Salad

Objectives

  • Learn to make a classic French chicken liver salad.
  • Master the art of cooking chicken livers to perfection.
  • Discover the flavor combination of raspberry vinegar and chicken livers.

Ingredients

  • Chicken livers (cleaned)
  • Mushrooms (quartered)
  • Tomatoes (sliced)
  • Shallots (finely sliced)
  • Boiled potatoes (diced)
  • Croutons
  • Salad leaves
  • Garlic (1 clove)
  • Butter
  • Oil
  • Raspberry vinegar
  • Dijon mustard
  • Sunflower oil
  • Salt
  • Black pepper

Instructions

  1. Prepare the ingredients: Cut mushrooms into quarters, slice tomatoes, finely slice shallots, and dice boiled potatoes. Wash salad leaves.
  2. Cook the mushrooms and shallots: Melt butter and oil in a pan over medium heat. Add mushrooms and cook until they get a bit of color. Add shallots, salt, and pepper. Cook until mushrooms are a nice chestnut color, then remove from heat and reserve in a bowl.
  3. Cook the chicken livers: In the same pan, melt butter and add a clove of garlic. Cook for 30 seconds. Add chicken livers and cook for 10 minutes on low heat, turning occasionally. Check for doneness by cutting one open; it should have a rosy color inside.
  4. Deglaze the pan: Turn heat to high and add a small amount of raspberry vinegar. Reduce the vinegar until it's almost gone, then turn off the heat and set aside.
  5. Make the dressing: In a jar, combine salt, pepper, 1 tablespoon raspberry vinegar, and 1 teaspoon Dijon mustard. Shake well. Add 3 tablespoons sunflower oil and shake again.
  6. Assemble the salad: Place a bed of salad leaves in a bowl. Arrange chicken livers in the center, creating a mound. Add some tomatoes, potatoes, and mushrooms.
  7. Dress the salad: Drizzle the dressing over the salad and chicken livers.
  8. Serve and enjoy.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=r4lZsZxrjzo

chicken_mushroom_pie.txt - Chicken and Mushroom Pie

Objectives

  • Learn to make a chicken and mushroom pie using a special pie crust
  • Make mini pies in a muffin tray for easy portioning
  • Understand the importance of proper dough handling and filling techniques

Ingredients

Crust: - 250g plain flour - 125g unsalted butter, cubed - 1/2 teaspoon salt - 1/4 teaspoon sugar - 100ml milk - 1 egg

Filling: - 1 tablespoon oil - 1/2 onion, chopped - 1 clove garlic, minced - 250g mushrooms, sliced - 200g chicken, diced - 1/2 teaspoon salt - 1/4 teaspoon black pepper - 1 tablespoon flour - 1/2 cup chicken broth - 1/4 cup port wine - 1/4 cup heavy cream - 1/4 teaspoon thyme - 1/4 teaspoon parsley

Egg wash: - 1 egg - 1 tablespoon water

Instructions

  1. Make the pie crust:
  2. Combine flour, butter, salt, and sugar in a food processor.
  3. Pulse until the mixture resembles coarse crumbs.
  4. In a separate bowl, whisk together milk, egg, salt, and sugar.
  5. Add the wet ingredients to the dry ingredients in the food processor and pulse until a dough forms.
  6. Wrap the dough in plastic wrap and refrigerate for at least one hour.
  7. Prepare the filling:
  8. Heat oil in a pan over medium heat.
  9. Add onion and garlic and cook until softened.
  10. Add mushrooms and cook until softened and browned.
  11. Add chicken, salt, pepper, and flour. Cook until chicken is browned.
  12. Deglaze the pan with chicken broth and port wine, scraping up any browned bits.
  13. Add cream, thyme, and parsley. Simmer until the sauce thickens.
  14. Assemble the pies:
  15. Preheat oven to 170 degrees Celsius (340 degrees Fahrenheit).
  16. Roll out the dough to a thickness of about 3-4 millimeters (less than a quarter-inch).
  17. Using a large cookie cutter, cut out circles for the pie bases.
  18. Press the circles into the muffin tray, ensuring they reach the bottom.
  19. Fill each pie base with the chicken and mushroom mixture, pressing down to ensure a full filling.
  20. Roll out the remaining dough and cut out circles for the lids.
  21. Brush the edges of the pie bases with egg wash.
  22. Place the lids on top of the filled bases and press down firmly to seal.
  23. Use a fork to crimp the edges of the pies.
  24. Make a small hole in the center of each lid for steam to escape.
  25. Brush the tops of the pies with egg wash.
  26. Bake the pies:
  27. Bake for 45-50 minutes, or until the crust is golden brown and the filling is bubbling.
  28. Allow the pies to cool for 15 minutes before serving.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=79glUAJ3Dz0

chicken_pojarsky.txt - Chicken Pojarsky

Objectives

  • Learn to make a traditional Russian chicken recipe, popular in France.
  • Understand the historical significance of the Chicken Pojarsky dish.
  • Discover a versatile recipe that can be made with veal or fish.

Ingredients

  • 1 chicken breast
  • 50g butter
  • 100ml cream or milk
  • 1 slice white bread
  • Salt
  • Pepper
  • Nutmeg (optional)

Instructions

  1. Cut the chicken breast into large cubes.
  2. Cut the butter into cubes.
  3. Soak the white bread in cream or milk for a few minutes.
  4. Drain the excess liquid from the soaked bread.
  5. Combine the chicken, butter, soaked bread, salt, pepper, and optional nutmeg in a food processor.
  6. Pulse the mixture in the food processor until it is finely ground.
  7. Transfer the mixture to a bowl and refrigerate for 15 minutes.
  8. Shape the mixture into patties.
  9. Roll the patties in breadcrumbs.
  10. Heat clarified butter or neutral oil in a frying pan over medium heat.
  11. Fry the patties for 10-15 minutes, turning them over halfway through, until golden brown and cooked through.
  12. Serve immediately.

chicken_riesling_sauce.txt - Chicken with Riesling Sauce

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a classic Alsatian chicken recipe with a sweet riesling sauce.
  • Understand the importance of using a sweet riesling and cognac for the sauce.
  • Master the technique of pan-frying mushrooms and chicken for optimal flavor.

Ingredients

  • 1 whole chicken, cut into pieces
  • 1 tbsp grapeseed oil
  • 1 tbsp butter
  • 1 medium shallot, sliced
  • 1 branch of thyme
  • 1 clove garlic, germ removed
  • 1 cup sliced mushrooms
  • Salt and pepper
  • 1 tbsp cognac
  • 1/2 cup homemade chicken bouillon
  • 1/2 cup sweet riesling
  • 1/2 cup heavy cream

Instructions

  1. Pan-fry the mushrooms with salt and pepper until lightly browned. Set aside.
  2. Heat grapeseed oil and butter in a pan over medium heat.
  3. Lightly brown the chicken pieces on all sides, ensuring they are just slightly blonde in color.
  4. Remove chicken from the pan and set aside.
  5. Add sliced shallots and thyme to the pan and cook until softened and fragrant.
  6. Deglaze the pan with cognac, raising the heat to evaporate the alcohol.
  7. Add the mushrooms back to the pan and stir to combine.
  8. Reduce heat and add the chicken pieces back to the pan.
  9. Pour in the chicken bouillon and riesling, bring to a boil, and then reduce heat and simmer for 30 minutes, partially covered.
  10. After 15 minutes, remove the chicken breasts and keep warm in the oven at 60°C. Continue cooking the chicken legs for the remaining time.
  11. Once the chicken is cooked, remove it from the pan and keep warm.
  12. Reduce the cooking juices in the pan over high heat for 4 minutes to concentrate the flavors.
  13. Add the cream to the pan and stir to combine.
  14. Reduce the sauce over low heat until it reaches a spoon-coating consistency.
  15. Gently coat the chicken pieces in the sauce and serve immediately.

  • French bread (for the French Torching)
  • Pasta (for the Pasta Toss)

  3. Find decent pieces of shredded chicken.

chicken_stock_recipe.txt - Chicken Stock Recipe

Objectives

  • Learn how to cut a whole chicken into four pieces.
  • Understand the importance of using the chicken carcass to make fresh stock.
  • Learn how to make a quick and flavorful chicken stock.

Ingredients

1 whole chicken 1 onion 1 bouquet garni (bay leaf, thyme, parsley) 1 mix of vegetables (carrots, celery, parsnips) Cold water Salt (to taste)

Instructions

  1. Cut the chicken into four pieces: two legs and two breasts.
  2. To remove the wings, locate the joint and cut through it.
  3. To remove the legs, stretch the skin and cut along it, following the joint.
  4. To remove the breasts, locate the bone in the middle of the chicken and cut along it, detaching the flesh.
  5. Save the chicken carcass for stock.
  6. Trim any remaining pieces of flesh from the carcass.
  7. Cut the end of the chicken bottom, as it can be bitter.
  8. Cut the carcass into smaller pieces.
  9. Prepare the stock.
  10. Fill a stock pot with cold water.
  11. Add the chicken bones, onion, bouquet garni, and vegetables.
  12. Bring the mixture to a boil.
  13. Reduce heat and simmer for 30 minutes.
  14. Strain the stock.
  15. Remove the bones and garnish from the stock.
  16. Strain the stock through a sieve into a clean container.
  17. Enjoy your fresh chicken stock.
  18. The stock can be used in soups, sauces, and other dishes.
  19. The stock can be stored in the refrigerator for up to 5 days or frozen for up to 3 months.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=JpkiURuIRhA

chicken_stock.txt - Chicken Stock

Objectives

  • Learn to make professional-grade chicken stock from scratch
  • Understand the importance of blanching and skimming impurities
  • Master the art of creating a flavorful and clear chicken stock

Ingredients

  • Organic chicken carcass
  • 1 onion
  • 2 carrots
  • 1 bouquet garni
  • 1 clove of garlic
  • Salt and pepper (to taste)
  • Water

Instructions

  1. Blanch the chicken carcass in cold water.
  2. Chop the chicken carcass into smaller pieces.
  3. Bring the cold water to a boil with the chicken carcass.
  4. Skim off any white foam that forms on the surface.
  5. Remove the chicken carcass from the boiling water and discard the water.
  6. Clean the stockpot and refill it with fresh cold water.
  7. Return the chicken carcass to the stockpot.
  8. Bring the water to a boil.
  9. Add the bouquet garni, carrots, and onion to the boiling water.
  10. Reduce the heat to a simmer and cook for 45 minutes to an hour.
  11. Skim off any impurities that appear on the surface of the stock.
  12. Strain the stock through a fine-mesh sieve.
  13. Season the stock with salt and pepper to taste.
  14. Serve the stock hot or store it in the refrigerator for later use.

chicken_stuffed_morels_champagne_sauce.txt - Chicken Stuffed with Morels, Champagne Sauce

Objectives

  • Cook a classic pot-roasted chicken filled with morels
  • Prepare a rich champagne sauce infused with morel flavors
  • Make a flavorful chicken rice to complement the dish

Ingredients

Chicken - 1 whole chicken - 40 grams morel mushrooms (dried) - 200 grams clarified butter - 100 grams onion - 50 grams celery - 50 grams carrots - Salt and pepper

Sauce Base - Chicken carcasses - Vegetable stock - 1 tablespoon oil - 1 tablespoon flour - 1/2 cup champagne - Salt and pepper - Morel mushroom soaking liquid

Sauce - Morel mushroom soaking liquid - Remaining clarified butter from chicken cooking - Champagne - Heavy cream

Chicken Rice - 40-50 grams butter - 1 onion - Rice - White chicken stock - Bay leaf - Salt and pepper

Instructions

  1. Rehydrate the morel mushrooms by covering them with boiling water and letting them soak for 30-40 minutes.
  2. Brown the chicken carcasses in a pot over medium-high heat with 1 tablespoon of oil.
  3. Add chopped onions, carrots, and celery to the pot and cook for a few minutes.
  4. Deglaze the pot with 1/2 cup of champagne, scraping the bottom to capture the juices.
  5. Add 1 tablespoon of flour and mix well.
  6. Pour in vegetable stock, bring to a boil, and season with salt and pepper.
  7. Add the morel soaking liquid to the sauce base and simmer for 15-20 minutes.
  8. While the sauce base is simmering, rinse the rehydrated morels thoroughly to remove any grit.
  9. Sauté the morels in 20-30 grams of butter with shallots, garlic, salt, and pepper for a few minutes.
  10. Stuff the chicken cavity with the sautéed morels.
  11. Season the chicken generously with salt and pepper.
  12. Heat clarified butter in the pot over medium-high heat.
  13. Color the chicken on all sides in the hot butter, ensuring a nice golden brown color.
  14. Remove the chicken from the pot and set aside.
  15. Add the chopped onions, carrots, and celery to the pot and cook until softened.
  16. Place the chicken on top of the vegetables in the pot.
  17. Pour the remaining clarified butter over the chicken.
  18. Cover the pot and bake in a preheated oven at 190 degrees Celsius for approximately 1.5 hours.
  19. During the baking process, check on the chicken every 30 minutes and baste with clarified butter to keep it moist.
  20. 10-15 minutes before the chicken is finished cooking, brush the top with clarified butter and remove the lid to allow the skin to brown.
  21. Remove the chicken from the oven and let it rest for 20 minutes before carving.
  22. While the chicken is resting, melt 40-50 grams of butter in a saucepan.
  23. Sauté the onions in the melted butter for 5 minutes.
  24. Add the rice and cook until translucent.
  25. Pour in the white chicken stock, add a bay leaf, and season with salt and pepper.
  26. Cover the rice with a parchment paper circle (cartouche) and a lid.
  27. Bake the rice in the oven at 190 degrees Celsius for 17 minutes.
  28. To make the sauce, heat the remaining clarified butter from the chicken cooking in the pot.
  29. Add the morels and sauté for a few minutes.
  30. Deglaze the pot with a little more champagne.
  31. Add the sauce base to the pot and bring to a boil.
  32. Reduce the sauce for 5 minutes.
  33. Stir in the chicken juices and bring to a boil again.
  34. Reduce the sauce for another 5 minutes.
  35. Stir in heavy cream and simmer for a few minutes until the sauce reaches the desired consistency.
  36. Remove the chicken rice from the oven and fluff with a fork.
  37. Serve the chicken, rice, and sauce together.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mV1Iqk8fgOQ

chicken_tarragon_sauce.txt - Poulet a la sauce tarragon (Chicken in Tarragon Sauce)

Objectives

  • Learn to make a classic French one-pot chicken dish.
  • Master the art of infusing tarragon flavor into the sauce.
  • Discover techniques for maximizing tarragon flavor in a dish.

Ingredients

  • Whole chicken, cut into pieces
  • 2 tablespoons oil
  • 1 small mirepoix (carrots, celery, shallots)
  • Salt and pepper
  • Flour
  • Dry white wine
  • Cognac
  • Homemade stock
  • Heavy cream
  • Fresh tarragon sprigs
  • Fresh tarragon leaves

Instructions

  1. Prepare the ingredients. Cut the chicken into pieces, season with salt and pepper, and dust with flour. Prepare the mirepoix by chopping carrots, celery, and shallots.
  2. Sear the chicken. Heat oil in a cast iron pan over medium heat. Sear the chicken skin-side down for 4-5 minutes per side, ensuring a good brown color.
  3. Sweat the vegetables. Remove the chicken from the pan and set aside. Add the mirepoix to the pan and cook over medium-low heat for 2 minutes, allowing them to release their flavors.
  4. Deglaze the pan. Add cognac to the pan and deglaze, scraping up any browned bits from the bottom. Reduce the cognac until almost dry.
  5. Add the wine. Pour in the white wine and reduce until almost dry, concentrating the flavors.
  6. Add the stock. Add the homemade stock, cover the pan halfway, and bring to a simmer.
  7. Infuse the tarragon. Tie the tarragon stems together with string and submerge them in the sauce.
  8. Cook the chicken. Add the seared chicken back to the pan and cook for 20-25 minutes, ensuring the breast pieces are removed after 10-15 minutes to avoid overcooking.
  9. Reduce the cream. In a separate saucepan, reduce heavy cream over low heat. Add the tarragon leaves and infuse the cream with flavor.
  10. Finish the sauce. Remove the tarragon stems from the sauce. Reduce the sauce until it reaches the desired consistency.
  11. Assemble the dish. Add the chopped tarragon leaves to the sauce. Warm the chicken in the sauce.
  12. Serve. Plate the chicken and pour the sauce over it. Garnish with additional chopped tarragon leaves.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=dj4v0-2t4yg

chicken_vol_sauce.txt - Chicken Velouté Sauce

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a classic French Velouté sauce
  • Understand the basics of white sauces and their variations
  • Discover a simple and delicious recipe for a chicken velouté

Ingredients

  • 50g unsalted butter
  • 50g all-purpose flour
  • 500ml chicken stock (homemade is best)
  • 100ml heavy cream
  • 100g mushrooms, sliced
  • Salt and pepper to taste
  • 1/4 teaspoon grated nutmeg
  • Pinch of cayenne pepper
  • 1 tablespoon lemon juice
  • 1 tablespoon unsalted butter (for finishing)
  • Fresh parsley, chopped (optional)

Instructions

  1. Melt the butter in a medium saucepan over medium heat.
  2. Whisk in the flour and cook for 3 minutes, stirring constantly, until the mixture is a light golden brown color.
  3. Remove the pan from the heat and let the roux cool completely.
  4. While the roux is cooling, prepare the mushrooms by sautéing them in a separate pan with olive oil and butter until golden brown.
  5. Bring the chicken stock to a boil in a saucepan.
  6. Gradually whisk the cooled roux into the boiling stock, making sure to incorporate all of the roux.
  7. Reduce the heat to low and simmer for 8-10 minutes, stirring occasionally, until the sauce thickens.
  8. Add the sautéed mushrooms, cream, nutmeg, cayenne pepper, and lemon juice to the sauce.
  9. Stir to combine and cook for 2-3 minutes, or until the sauce is heated through.
  10. Season with salt and pepper to taste.
  11. Stir in the remaining tablespoon of butter and garnish with fresh parsley, if desired.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=xVUwCl-VplY

chocola_custard.txt - Chocola Custard

Objectives

  • Learn to make a classic vanilla custard from scratch.
  • Transform vanilla custard into a decadent chocolate dessert.
  • Master the art of whipping cream to perfection.

Ingredients

  • 300 ml milk
  • 200 ml cream
  • 1 vanilla bean
  • 6 egg yolks
  • 100 g sugar
  • 200 g dark chocolate, chopped
  • 20 g icing sugar

Instructions

  1. Combine 300 ml milk and 200 ml cream in a saucepan.
  2. Split a vanilla bean in half, scrape the seeds, and add both seeds and pod to the saucepan.
  3. Heat the milk mixture over medium heat, gently warming it without bringing it to a boil.
  4. In a separate bowl, whisk together 6 egg yolks and 100 g sugar until pale and slightly thickened.
  5. Gradually pour a small amount of the warm milk mixture into the egg yolk mixture, whisking constantly to temper the eggs.
  6. Pour the tempered egg mixture back into the saucepan with the remaining milk mixture.
  7. Cook the custard over medium-low heat, stirring constantly, until it reaches 80°C. You can use a food thermometer or watch for the foam on the surface to disappear.
  8. Remove the custard from heat and immediately stir in 200 g chopped dark chocolate until melted and smooth.
  9. Pour the chocolate custard into a container and cover with plastic wrap. Refrigerate for at least 3 hours, or up to 24 hours.
  10. To serve, pipe the chilled chocolate custard into glasses.
  11. Whip cold heavy cream in a chilled bowl with 20 g icing sugar until soft peaks form.
  12. Pipe whipped cream on top of the chocolate custard and garnish with roasted peanuts, chocolate shavings, or other desired toppings.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=t7fOxVxpUtA

chocolate_ganache_tart.txt - Chocolate Ganache Tart

Objectives

  • Learn to make a simple and delicious chocolate ganache tart.
  • Understand the importance of using good quality dark chocolate.
  • Create a festive Easter treat for friends and family.

Ingredients

  • 100g plain biscuits (any type)
  • 50g unsalted butter, melted
  • 200ml heavy cream (at least 35% fat)
  • 200g dark chocolate (at least 70% cocoa)
  • 1 tart ring

Instructions

  1. Crush biscuits into a fine powder using a food processor or by hand.
  2. Melt butter in a saucepan over low heat.
  3. Combine crushed biscuits and melted butter in a bowl and mix until well combined.
  4. Press the biscuit mixture into the bottom of the tart ring, ensuring it is evenly distributed and compact.
  5. Refrigerate the tart base for at least 10-15 minutes until the butter hardens.
  6. Pour heavy cream into a saucepan and bring to a boil over medium heat.
  7. Remove the cream from the heat immediately and add the chopped dark chocolate.
  8. Stir until the chocolate is completely melted and the mixture is smooth.
  9. Pour the ganache mixture over the chilled tart base.
  10. Refrigerate the tart for at least 20 minutes to set.
  11. Decorate with Easter-themed decorations, if desired.
  12. Serve chilled and enjoy!

chocolate_types_handling.txt - Chocolate: Types, Origins, and Handling

Objectives

  • Understand the origin and production of chocolate from cocoa beans
  • Learn about different types of chocolate: white, milk, and dark
  • Discover the importance of temperature control when handling chocolate for desserts

Instructions

  1. Chocolate is derived from cocoa beans, which are fruits growing on tree trunks.
  2. The beans are fermented and processed into cocoa nibs, the raw ingredient for chocolate.
  3. Cocoa nibs are pressed to extract cocoa butter, a fat, and cocoa powder, a dry product.
  4. Combining cocoa butter, cocoa powder, sugar, and milk creates different types of chocolate:
    • White chocolate: cocoa butter, sugar, milk
    • Milk chocolate: cocoa butter, cocoa powder, sugar, milk
    • Dark chocolate: cocoa butter, cocoa powder, sugar (with varying cocoa content)
  5. Dark chocolate is often categorized by its percentage of cocoa butter, indicating its bitterness level.
  6. When handling chocolate for desserts, remember that its melting point is lower than body temperature, around 32 degrees Celsius.
  7. Avoid heating chocolate above 42 degrees Celsius, as this can lead to grainy texture.
  8. Use a double boiler or a low-temperature heat source for melting chocolate.
  9. To ensure a smooth, silky chocolate sauce, monitor the temperature and avoid exceeding 40 degrees Celsius.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=LVzqQnwfTjk

choux_pastry.txt - Choux Pastry

Objectives

  • Learn to make classic French choux pastry.
  • Understand the importance of each step in the process.
  • Master the techniques for piping and baking choux pastry.

Ingredients

  • 1 cup water
  • 1/2 cup sugar
  • 1/4 teaspoon salt
  • 1/2 cup butter
  • 1 cup all-purpose flour
  • 4 eggs

Instructions

  1. Combine water, sugar, and salt in a saucepan over medium heat.
  2. Bring the mixture to a boil.
  3. Add the butter and stir until completely melted.
  4. Remove the pan from heat and immediately add the flour.
  5. Stir vigorously until the mixture forms a smooth ball.
  6. Return the pan to low heat and cook for 1-2 minutes, stirring constantly, to dry out the dough.
  7. Transfer the dough to a bowl and let it cool slightly.
  8. Add eggs one at a time, beating well after each addition.
  9. Once the dough is smooth and glossy, transfer it to a piping bag fitted with a round tip.
  10. Pipe the dough onto a baking sheet lined with parchment paper.
  11. Use a fork to flatten the tops of the choux pastry.
  12. Brush the choux pastry with egg wash.
  13. Preheat oven to 400 degrees Fahrenheit (200 degrees Celsius).
  14. Bake for 15 minutes, then reduce heat to 375 degrees Fahrenheit (190 degrees Celsius) and bake for an additional 10-15 minutes, or until golden brown.
  15. Let the choux pastry cool completely before filling and decorating.

cinderella_potatoes.txt - Cinderella Potatoes

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a unique and elegant take on mashed potatoes.
  • Master the art of preparing potatoes for a fluffy and flavorful puree.
  • Discover a simple yet impressive recipe that elevates a classic dish.

Ingredients

  • 2-4 Floury Potatoes (suitable for mashing)
  • 2 tbsp Cream
  • 1 tbsp Butter
  • Salt and Pepper
  • Grated Nutmeg
  • 1 tbsp Grated Cheese (such as Gruyere or Emmental)
  • 1/2 Egg Yolk
  • Fresh Herbs (such as parsley and chives)

Instructions

  1. Preheat oven to 200 degrees Celsius (400 degrees Fahrenheit).
  2. Place whole, unpeeled potatoes in a cold oven and cook for 45 minutes to an hour, depending on size.
  3. Check potatoes with a knife to ensure they are cooked through.
  4. While potatoes are cooking, prepare ingredients: grate cheese, chop herbs, and have cream, butter, egg yolk, and seasonings ready.
  5. Once potatoes are cooked, cut a small opening in the top of each potato, being careful not to break the skin.
  6. Carefully scoop out the potato flesh with a small spoon, leaving a thin layer of potato against the skin to maintain the shape.
  7. Add the scooped potato flesh to a bowl, along with an optional extra potato if you didn't scoop out much.
  8. In a small saucepan, combine the cream and butter over very low heat.
  9. Gently stir until butter melts and the mixture is smooth.
  10. Add the scooped potato flesh to the saucepan and mash with a fork until smooth.
  11. Season with salt, pepper, and a pinch of nutmeg.
  12. In a small bowl, whisk together the cream, egg yolk, and cheese.
  13. Once the potato puree is ready, stir in chopped herbs.
  14. Fill the empty potato shells with the herb-infused puree using a spoon.
  15. Make a small dent in the center of each filled potato shell to accommodate the custard.
  16. Pour the cheese custard into the dent, spreading it around to avoid overflow.
  17. To finish, you have two options:
    • Option 1: Place the filled potatoes under a preheated grill for 5 minutes to achieve a golden brown crust and cook the custard.
    • Option 2: Bake the filled potatoes in the oven at 200 degrees Celsius (400 degrees Fahrenheit) for 10 minutes to warm them through and create a crispy crust.
  18. Serve immediately, garnished with additional fresh herbs if desired.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZRQxbM95VUQ

clarified_butter.txt - Clarified Butter

Objectives

  • Learn how to make clarified butter, a key ingredient in many classic French sauces.
  • Understand the importance of using high-quality butter and controlling the melting process.
  • Discover how to separate the butter fat from the milk solids for a pure and flavorful clarified butter.

Ingredients

  • 1 stick (113 grams) of organic butter

Instructions

  1. Preheat oven to 60-70 degrees Celsius (140-160 degrees Fahrenheit) in convection mode only.
  2. Place the butter in an oven-proof glass container.
  3. Put the container in the preheated oven.
  4. Monitor the butter as it melts, checking every few minutes.
  5. Once the butter is mostly melted, remove it from the oven.
  6. Carefully skim off the white, foamy layer that forms on top of the melted butter using a spoon.
  7. Using a ladle or spoon, gently scoop out the clear, golden butter fat from the top, leaving the white milk solids at the bottom.
  8. Discard the milk solids.
  9. The collected clarified butter is ready to use in sauces like hollandaise or béarnaise.

cloud_egg.txt - Cloud Egg

Objectives

  • Learn to make a revisited version of the classic French cloud egg recipe.
  • Understand the importance of using high-quality ingredients and proper techniques.
  • Explore the versatility of this dish by incorporating different flavor combinations.

Ingredients

  • 1 egg
  • 2-3 tablespoons of heavy cream
  • 1/2 teaspoon of salt
  • 1/4 teaspoon of black pepper
  • 1/4 cup of grated parmesan cheese
  • 1 drop of lemon juice

Instructions

  1. Preheat the oven to 180°C (355°F).
  2. Separate the egg yolk from the egg white.
  3. In a small saucepan, heat the cream over medium heat until it comes to a simmer.
  4. Add the grated cheese to the cream and stir until it is melted and combined.
  5. Remove the cream from the heat and set aside.
  6. In a clean bowl, add the egg white, salt, and a drop of lemon juice.
  7. Beat the egg white using an electric mixer on high speed until stiff peaks form. This should take about 4 minutes.
  8. Fold in the grated parmesan cheese and black pepper.
  9. Gently spoon the egg white mixture into a small ramekin or baking dish, creating a slight indentation in the center.
  10. Pour the warm cream mixture into the bottom of the ramekin.
  11. Carefully place the egg yolk into the indentation in the egg white.
  12. Bake in the preheated oven for 5 minutes.
  13. Remove from the oven and serve immediately.

cocoa_recipe.txt - Cocoa Recipe

Objectives

  • Learn to make a traditional French dish with chicken braised in red wine and cognac sauce.
  • Understand the importance of marinating the chicken overnight and preparing a stock beforehand.
  • Master the technique of reducing the sauce and thickening the stock.

Ingredients

  • Chicken (already marinated)
  • Stock (already prepared)
  • Cognac (Courvoisier)
  • Pancetta or Bacon
  • Pearl Onions
  • Mushrooms
  • Parsley
  • Carrots
  • Shallot
  • Onion
  • Bouquet Garni
  • Butter
  • Oil
  • Sugar
  • Water
  • Flour
  • Red Wine
  • Salt
  • Pepper
  • Croutons (optional)

Instructions

  1. Filter the stock: Pass the cold stock through a sieve to remove chicken bones.
  2. Reduce the stock: Place the filtered stock on low heat and allow it to reduce.
  3. Dry the marinated chicken: Remove the chicken from the marinade and pat dry with kitchen towels.
  4. Filter the marinade: Remove the bouquet garni from the marinade and pass it through a sieve.
  5. Reduce the marinade: Place the filtered marinade on low heat and allow it to reduce.
  6. Clean the marinade: Remove any scum that appears on the surface of the marinade as it boils.
  7. Thicken the stock: Add a small amount of beurre manié (equal parts butter and flour) to the reduced stock, whisking until it reaches the desired thickness.
  8. Preheat the oven: Set the oven to 200 degrees Celsius (392 Fahrenheit).
  9. Brown the chicken: Heat butter and oil in a cast iron pan. Brown the chicken on all sides, reserving the browned pieces on a tray.
  10. Brown the garnish: Brown the dried garnish in the same pan.
  11. Flambe the chicken: Return the chicken to the pan and add a splash of cognac. Carefully ignite the cognac and let it burn off.
  12. Add the reduced wine: Pour the reduced wine into the pan and let it reduce slightly.
  13. Add the thickened stock: Top up the pan with the thickened stock.
  14. Add the bouquet garni: Place the bouquet garni in the pan.
  15. Bake the cocoa: Cover the pan and bake for 30 minutes at 200 degrees Celsius.
  16. Caramelize the onions: Heat butter, sugar, and a small amount of water in a pan. Cook the onions until caramelized.
  17. Fry the pancetta: Flash fry the pancetta in a pan with oil until it's nicely browned.
  18. Fry the mushrooms: Fry the mushrooms in the same pan until golden brown.
  19. Combine the pancetta and mushrooms: Add the cooked pancetta back to the pan with the mushrooms.
  20. Fry croutons (optional): Fry croutons in a pan with oil for decoration.
  21. Remove the cocoa from the oven: Remove the cocoa from the oven and let it rest for 5 minutes.
  22. Separate the meat and sauce: Remove the chicken and bouquet garni from the pan. Strain the sauce through a sieve into a separate container.
  23. Adjust the sauce: Taste the sauce and adjust the seasoning with salt and pepper.
  24. Thicken the sauce: Add a small amount of beurre manié to the sauce and whisk until it reaches the desired thickness.
  25. Add the garnish: Mix half of the caramelized onions, pancetta, and mushrooms into the sauce.
  26. Add cognac: Add a dash of cognac to the sauce.
  27. Dress the cocoa: Serve the chicken with the sauce and remaining garnish.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_ise46LADBs

coconut_boulders.txt - Coconut Boulders

Objectives

  • Learn how to make coconut boulders, a sweet treat popular in France.
  • Understand the importance of carefully melting sugar into egg whites.
  • Learn how to properly bake coconut boulders for a perfect texture and color.

Ingredients

  • 3 egg whites
  • 100g granulated sugar
  • 100g grated coconut
  • 1/2 teaspoon vanilla extract
  • Pinch of salt

Instructions

  1. Preheat oven to 210 degrees Celsius (410 degrees Fahrenheit).
  2. Fill a saucepan with a small amount of water and bring to a simmer.
  3. Place a heat-proof bowl on top of the saucepan, ensuring the bowl does not touch the water.
  4. Add the egg whites and a pinch of salt to the bowl.
  5. Whisk the egg whites continuously until they reach 50 degrees Celsius (122 degrees Fahrenheit).
  6. Gradually add the granulated sugar while whisking constantly until the sugar is completely dissolved.
  7. Remove the bowl from the heat and add the grated coconut.
  8. Stir until the coconut is evenly distributed.
  9. Add the vanilla extract and stir again.
  10. Using your hands, form the mixture into small, round boulders.
  11. Place the coconut boulders on a baking sheet lined with parchment paper.
  12. Bake for 5 minutes with the oven fan on.
  13. Turn off the fan and continue baking for another 5 minutes.
  14. Allow the coconut boulders to cool completely before serving.
