cold_oven_roast_chicken.txt - Cold Oven Roast Chicken

Objectives

  • Learn a simple method for roasting chicken in a cold oven.
  • Achieve crispy skin and juicy meat without any special equipment or techniques.
  • Understand the importance of resting the chicken after cooking.

Ingredients

  • 1 whole chicken of any size
  • Salt and pepper
  • Butter (4 small pieces)
  • Sunflower oil (1-2 tablespoons)
  • Coarse salt and peppercorns (optional, for seasoning the cavity)

Instructions

  1. Season the inside of the chicken with salt and pepper.
  2. Season the outside of the chicken generously with salt and pepper.
  3. Place 1-2 tablespoons of sunflower oil in a baking dish or roasting pan.
  4. Place the chicken in the baking dish.
  5. Massage the chicken with a little extra oil, if desired.
  6. Tuck 4 small pieces of butter under the skin of the chicken.
  7. Place the chicken in a cold oven that is turned off.
  8. Turn the oven on to 200°C (400°F) with fan force.
  9. Set a timer for 70 minutes and let the chicken cook undisturbed.
  10. After the timer goes off, remove the chicken from the oven and let it rest on a rack covered with foil or parchment paper for at least 20 minutes.
  11. Carve the chicken and serve.

consomme_with_yl.txt - Consommé with Yl (Savory Custard)

Objectives

  • Learn to clarify a beef broth into a consommé using the traditional egg raft method.
  • Create a savory custard garnish called Yl, a classic Escoffier recipe.
  • Explore the history and techniques behind consommé and Yl.

Ingredients

Consommé:

  • 2 liters beef broth (from previous video)
  • 1 celery stalk, finely chopped
  • 1 tomato, finely chopped
  • 1 carrot, finely chopped
  • 1 leek, green part only, finely chopped
  • 1 tablespoon coriander, finely chopped
  • 2 egg whites
  • 1 tablespoon beef (optional)

Yl (Savory Custard):

  • 3 egg yolks
  • 1 whole egg
  • 100 ml heavy cream
  • 100 ml consommé
  • 1/4 teaspoon white pepper
  • 1/4 teaspoon nutmeg (optional)

Instructions

  1. Prepare the egg raft: Finely chop all the vegetables (celery, tomato, carrot, leek, coriander). Combine the chopped vegetables, egg whites, and optional beef in a large pan.
  2. Remove fat from broth: Chill the beef broth and skim off any solidified fat.
  3. Combine broth and raft: Pour the chilled broth into the pan with the vegetable and egg white mixture.
  4. Heat and simmer: Turn the heat to medium and gently stir the mixture, ensuring the egg whites are evenly dispersed. Once the broth begins to warm, reduce heat to a simmer and do not stir again.
  5. Simmer for 45 minutes: Allow the mixture to simmer for 45 minutes without stirring. The egg whites will solidify and form a "raft" on top of the broth.
  6. Filter the consommé: After 45 minutes, carefully ladle the consommé through a fine-mesh strainer lined with cheesecloth or coffee filters.
  7. Make the Yl (Savory Custard): In a bowl, whisk together the egg yolks, whole egg, heavy cream, and consommé. Season with white pepper and nutmeg (optional).
  8. Strain the custard: Strain the custard mixture through a fine-mesh sieve to remove any lumps or bits of egg.
  9. Cook the custard: Pour the custard into individual molds and place them in a bain-marie (water bath). Bake in a preheated oven at 120°C (250°F) for 30-45 minutes, or until set.
  10. Chill the custard: Refrigerate the Yl until completely chilled and firm.
  11. Unmold and serve: Run a knife around the edge of the mold to loosen the Yl. Carefully invert the mold onto a plate to unmold. Cut the Yl into desired shapes and serve alongside the consommé.

cooking_tips_for_beginners.txt - Cooking Tips for Beginners

Objectives

  • Learn essential ingredients and condiments for French cooking
  • Understand the importance of proper salt and pepper usage
  • Discover different oil and vinegar options for enhanced flavor
  • Explore the fat content of cream, milk, and butter
  • Understand the role of basic alcohols in French cooking
  • Learn the benefits of fresh herbs and how to grow them
  • Emphasize the importance of good quality cookware and knives
  • Understand the importance of culinary techniques and basics
  • Discover how to replace store-bought ingredients with homemade versions
  • Learn the essential kitchen tools for elevating cooking
  • Discover the importance of using stock instead of water
  • Learn the importance of clean water for cooking

Instructions

  1. Start with basic ingredients and condiments like salt, pepper, mustard, and dairy products.
  2. Add salt towards the end of cooking, as most ingredients already contain salt.
  3. Use different types of salt, including table salt, salt flakes, and Himalayan rock salt, for varying tastes and textures.
  4. Experiment with various pepper types, including white, black, coarse, and mixed berries, for different dishes.
  5. Use a variety of oils like peanut, grapeseed, sunflower, olive, macadamia, walnut, and avocado oil for dressings and cooking.
  6. Explore flavored vinegars, such as tarragon-infused or shallot-infused, for added flavor.
  7. Use cream with a fat content of 32-35%, essential for sauces, desserts, and whipping.
  8. Use full-cream milk with its full fat content for French cooking.
  9. Use butter with an 85% fat content for optimal results in sauces and roux.
  10. Explore basic alcohols like Madera wine, Port wine, and white vermouth for pan sauces and fish dishes.
  11. Grow fresh herbs like coriander, basil, and parsley at home for maximum flavor.
  12. Invest in a mid-range cookware set with a non-stick pan and stainless steel options.
  13. Choose an ergonomic knife set from a reputable brand like Mercer Culinary.
  14. Replace store-bought ingredients like French dressing, mayonnaise, and short crust with homemade versions.
  15. Master basic culinary techniques like breading and sauce making.
  16. Invest in a kitchen scale, food and oven thermometer, and an electronic timer for accurate measurements and cooking.
  17. Learn how to make stock and use it in soups, sauces, and dishes.
  18. Use clean, filtered water for cooking, especially for soups and stocks.

cookware_buying_guide.txt - Cookware Buying Guide

Objectives

  • Identify the right questions to ask yourself when buying cookware.
  • Understand the importance of considering your budget, cooking style, and lifestyle.
  • Learn how to choose cookware that fits your specific needs and preferences.

Instructions

  1. Determine if you need a set or individual pans:
  2. If you're new to cooking, a cookware set is recommended.
  3. If you have a complete set and need an additional pan, buy it individually.
  4. If you're an experienced cook and know your needs, buy individual pans.
  5. Define your budget:
  6. Low-end cookware is not a good investment as it won't last long.
  7. Mid-range and high-end cookware offer better quality and durability.
  8. Consider the number of people you cook for:
  9. Choose a cookware set with pans that are appropriate for your household size.
  10. Ensure the pans are large enough to accommodate your cooking needs.
  11. Identify your most common cooking methods:
  12. If you frequently cook soups, stews, or pasta, prioritize saucepans and stockpots.
  13. If you primarily sauté or pan-fry, focus on frying pans and skillets.
  14. Evaluate your lifestyle and maintenance preferences:
  15. Consider the amount of maintenance you're willing to do.
  16. Choose pans that are dishwasher safe if you prefer convenience.
  17. Opt for pans that require hand washing if you enjoy the ritual of caring for them.
  18. Determine your expectations from cookware:
  19. Decide if you want a nonstick coating for easy cooking or stainless steel for searing.
  20. Consider the desired outcome of your cooking and choose pans that will help you achieve it.

cordon_bleu.txt - Cordon Bleu

Objectives

  • Make a homemade cordon bleu from scratch.
  • Use unique ingredients like specialty ham, pancetta, veal, and blue cheese.
  • Learn how to flatten meat effectively for cordon bleu.
  • Create homemade breadcrumbs from dry biscuits.
  • Cook cordon bleu in a pan and finish in the oven.
  • Make homemade potato chips in the oven.

Ingredients

Chicken: - 1 piece of chicken breast - Herb-infused ham - Gruyere cheese - Blue cheese - Dry biscuits for breadcrumbs - Flour - Eggs - Salt - Butter - Oil

Veal: - 1 piece of veal - Pancetta - Gruyere cheese - Blue cheese - Dry biscuits for breadcrumbs - Flour - Eggs - Salt - Butter - Oil

Potato Chips: - Potatoes - Oil - Salt (optional) - Other seasonings (optional)

Instructions

  1. Flatten the chicken breast:
    • Place chicken breast between two pieces of baking paper.
    • Add a little water to the paper to help the chicken flatten.
    • Use a heavy pan to press down on the chicken, flattening it to a thin layer.
  2. Prepare the breadcrumbs:
    • Crush dry biscuits into fine crumbs using a sieve.
  3. Assemble the chicken cordon bleu:
    • Layer the flattened chicken breast with ham, Gruyere cheese, and blue cheese.
    • Roll the chicken tightly into a roulade.
    • Refrigerate for at least 10 minutes.
  4. Flatten the veal:
    • Repeat the same process as with the chicken breast, flattening the veal to a thin layer.
  5. Assemble the veal cordon bleu:
    • Layer the flattened veal with pancetta, Gruyere cheese, and blue cheese.
    • Roll the veal tightly into a roulade.
    • Refrigerate for at least 10 minutes.
  6. Prepare the breading:
    • Roll the chicken and veal cordon bleus in flour, then dip in beaten eggs, and finally coat with breadcrumbs.
  7. Cook the cordon bleus:
    • Heat butter and oil in a pan over medium heat.
    • Sear the cordon bleus in the pan for 5 minutes, ensuring the bottom is well-sealed.
    • Transfer the pan to the oven and bake for 10-15 minutes.
    • Use a cooking thermometer to check if the internal temperature reaches 70 degrees Celsius.
  8. Serve the cordon bleus:
    • Cut the cordon bleus and serve with homemade potato chips.

corn_soup.txt - Corn Soup

Objectives

  • Learn the difference between French soup classifications
  • Understand the components of a "crème" soup
  • Learn to make a creamy corn soup with a bechamel base

Ingredients

  • 1 tablespoon butter
  • 1 tablespoon flour
  • 1/2 cup milk
  • 1/2 onion
  • Salt
  • 1 liter water
  • 2 cups corn
  • 1/4 cup heavy cream
  • Fresh corn kernels
  • Fresh oregano

Instructions

  1. Prepare a thin bechamel sauce. Melt butter in a saucepan over low heat.
  2. Whisk in flour and cook for 2.5 minutes, stirring constantly.
  3. Gradually whisk in cold milk and increase heat to medium-high.
  4. Simmer for 10 minutes, stirring occasionally.
  5. Add half an onion to the bechamel sauce.
  6. Season with salt and white pepper.
  7. Bring a pot of salted water to a boil and blanch corn for 2 minutes.
  8. Remove corn from boiling water and rinse.
  9. Remove onion from bechamel sauce and discard.
  10. Add blanched corn to the bechamel sauce.
  11. Puree the mixture using an immersion blender.
  12. Strain the mixture through a sieve to remove any lumps.
  13. Stir in heavy cream until desired consistency is reached.
  14. Warm the soup over low heat.
  15. Serve the soup garnished with fresh corn kernels and a sprig of oregano.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=CO_DOy2EqJ8

corn_volute.txt - Corn Volute

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a classic French corn volute soup.
  • Master the technique for making a thin white sauce (béchamel).
  • Understand the importance of filtering the soup for a smooth texture.

Ingredients

  • 1 tablespoon butter
  • 1 tablespoon flour
  • 1 liter milk
  • 1 bay leaf
  • 2 cloves
  • 2 garlic cloves
  • Salt (to taste)
  • 1-2 cans (400g each) sweet corn (reserve some for garnish)
  • 50-100 ml cream (optional)
  • White pepper (optional)
  • Chives (for garnish)

Instructions

  1. Melt butter in a saucepan over medium heat.
  2. Add flour and whisk to form a paste (roux).
  3. Cook the roux for 2 minutes over low heat, then remove from heat and let cool completely.
  4. In a separate saucepan, warm milk with bay leaf, cloves, garlic, and a pinch of salt.
  5. Once the milk simmers, remove from heat.
  6. Gradually whisk the cooled roux into the warm milk.
  7. Return the mixture to medium heat and bring to a boil, whisking constantly to prevent sticking.
  8. Reduce heat to low and cook for 2 minutes until the sauce thickens.
  9. Remove from heat and stir in corn.
  10. Blend the soup with an immersion blender until smooth.
  11. Strain the soup through a fine-mesh sieve to remove any corn kernels or skins.
  12. Return the strained soup to the saucepan and heat over medium heat.
  13. Stir in cream (optional) to adjust the consistency.
  14. Season with salt and white pepper (optional) to taste.
  15. Garnish with chives and reserved corn kernels.
  16. Serve warm.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=qxLH3qTEw54

corsican_beef_stew.txt - Corsican Beef Stew

Objectives

  • Learn a unique French-Italian beef stew recipe from Corsica.
  • Discover the special technique of stuffing beef with garlic and bacon.
  • Master the slow-cooking process and pasta integration for a hearty meal.

Ingredients

  • 1 kg beef, cut into large cubes
  • 150g bacon, cut into matchsticks (or thin slices)
  • 2 onions, cut in half and sliced
  • 8 cloves garlic, 4 sliced into matchsticks, 4 crushed or minced
  • 100g dried porcini mushrooms (or other dried mushrooms)
  • 2 sprigs rosemary
  • 2 bay leaves
  • 3 tablespoons tomato passata
  • 150 ml dry white wine
  • 1/2 teaspoon salt
  • 1/4 teaspoon black pepper
  • 2 tablespoons olive oil
  • 1 tablespoon cognac (optional)
  • 500g macaroni or rigatoni pasta
  • Parmesan cheese, grated

Instructions

  1. Soak dried mushrooms in 100 ml boiling water for 30 minutes.
  2. Cut a cavity in each piece of beef and stuff with one garlic matchstick and one bacon piece.
  3. Season beef with salt and pepper.
  4. Heat olive oil in a cast iron pot over medium-high heat.
  5. Brown beef on all sides, then remove and set aside.
  6. Add bacon and onion to the pot.
  7. Cook for 10 minutes, or until onions are soft.
  8. Add garlic and cook for 2 minutes.
  9. Return beef to the pot.
  10. Add bay leaves, rosemary, mushrooms (rinsed and patted dry), mushroom soaking liquid, passata, white wine, and a pinch of cinnamon.
  11. Bring to a simmer and cook for 30 minutes, partially covered.
  12. Preheat oven to 160 degrees Celsius (320 degrees Fahrenheit).
  13. Add cognac (optional) to the pot.
  14. Transfer the pot to the oven and cook for 2.5 hours, or until the meat is very tender.
  15. While the stew is cooking, bring a large pot of salted water to a boil and cook pasta according to package directions.
  16. Remove the beef from the pot and keep warm.
  17. Drain the pasta and add it to the pot with the sauce.
  18. Stir gently to coat the pasta in the sauce.
  19. Serve the beef stew over the pasta, topped with grated Parmesan cheese.

courgette_recipe.txt - Moroccan Spiced Courgettes

Objectives

  • Create a simple, flavorful side dish using courgettes.
  • Explore a fusion of French and Moroccan culinary influences.
  • Achieve a crispy texture and caramelized flavor in the courgettes.

Ingredients

  • 2 onions, thinly sliced
  • 4 garlic cloves, crushed
  • 1 teaspoon paprika
  • 1 teaspoon cumin
  • Moroccan spices (optional)
  • Salt and pepper to taste
  • 3 tablespoons olive oil
  • 3-4 tablespoons water
  • Courgettes (young ones preferred)
  • Fresh parsley or coriander (for garnish)
  • Lemon wedges (for garnish)
  • Breadcrumbs (for onion crumble)

Instructions

  1. Prepare the courgettes by removing the ends and slicing them into thin strips.
  2. Mix the onions, garlic, paprika, cumin, Moroccan spices, salt, pepper, olive oil, and water in a bowl.
  3. Massage the courgette strips with the spice mixture, ensuring they are well coated.
  4. Preheat the oven to 200 degrees Celsius (400 degrees Fahrenheit).
  5. Place the courgettes on a baking tray, leaving some space between them.
  6. Cover the tray with parchment paper and bake for 15 minutes.
  7. Remove the parchment paper and continue baking for another 10-15 minutes, or until the courgettes are tender and slightly caramelized.
  8. While the courgettes are baking, prepare the onion crumble by frying the onion bits from the baking dish with breadcrumbs until crispy.
  9. To serve, arrange the cooked courgettes on a serving dish.
  10. Garnish with fresh parsley or coriander, lemon wedges, and the onion crumble.
  11. Enjoy!

courgette_sauté.txt - Sauteed Courgette with Chorizo

Objectives

  • Learn a simple and flavorful recipe for cooking courgette
  • Avoid soggy courgette by using a high-heat sauté method
  • Create a visually appealing dish with a simple decorative technique

Ingredients

  • 1 courgette
  • 1 onion
  • Lemon zest
  • Cumin seeds
  • Olive oil
  • Hard or semi-hard chorizo
  • Salt
  • Pepper
  • Parsley or coriander (for garnish)

Instructions

  1. Prepare the courgette: Remove the ends and use a peeler to remove thin strips of skin, creating a decorative pattern. Slice the courgette into 3-4 millimeter thick rounds.
  2. Prepare the onion: Finely dice the onion.
  3. Heat a non-stick pan over medium-high heat. Add 2.5 tablespoons of olive oil and heat until sizzling.
  4. Add the cumin seeds to the hot oil and cook until they start to pop.
  5. Add the diced onion and cook for 5 minutes, stirring occasionally, until slightly browned. Set aside.
  6. Heat the same pan over high heat. Add 1 tablespoon of olive oil.
  7. Add the courgette slices to the hot pan in batches, ensuring not to overcrowd the pan.
  8. Season with salt and pepper.
  9. Sauté the courgette slices for 6-8 minutes, stirring frequently, until they develop a nice golden color.
  10. Add the cooked onion back to the pan and stir gently.
  11. Remove the pan from heat and set aside to finish cooking.
  12. In a separate pan, heat a small amount of oil over medium heat. Add the chorizo and cook for 1-2 minutes, until browned.
  13. Drain the chorizo on paper towels.
  14. Assemble the dish: Arrange the sautéed courgette on a plate. Sprinkle with the cooked chorizo and garnish with parsley or coriander.
  15. Serve immediately while still warm.

courgette_towers.txt - Courgette Towers

Objectives

  • Learn to prepare a traditional French courgette dish.
  • Understand the importance of adjusting recipes based on ingredients.
  • Discover creative solutions for overcoming culinary challenges.

Ingredients

  • 4 medium-sized courgettes
  • 1 tablespoon olive oil
  • 1 onion, roughly chopped
  • 1 shallot, roughly chopped
  • 2-3 eggs
  • Ricotta cheese
  • Walnut cheese
  • Walnuts, finely chopped or grated
  • Salt
  • Pepper
  • Garlic

Instructions

  1. Cook the onion and shallot in olive oil over medium heat for 2-3 minutes.
  2. Combine the cooked onion and shallot with walnuts, ricotta cheese, walnut cheese, and salt.
  3. Add 2 eggs to the mixture, mixing gently. Do not add the third egg.
  4. Refrigerate the stuffing mixture for a while to allow it to thicken.
  5. Cut off the ends of the courgettes.
  6. Use a channel knife to create stripes along the courgette.
  7. Use a melon baller to carefully scoop out the seeds and flesh of the courgette.
  8. Carefully fill the courgettes with the stuffing.
  9. Preheat the oven to 160 degrees Celsius (320 degrees Fahrenheit).
  10. Rub a baking dish with garlic and add a little olive oil.
  11. Arrange the courgettes in the baking dish.
  12. Season with salt and pepper.
  13. Bake for 40 minutes, turning the courgettes halfway through.
  14. If the stuffing is too runny, try using less eggs or chopping the walnuts and onion more coarsely.
  15. Serve and enjoy!

crayola_punch.txt - Crayola Punch

Objectives

  • Learn to make a traditional French Caribbean punch.
  • Understand the importance of maceration for flavor infusion.
  • Discover the key ingredients and techniques for a flavorful and visually appealing punch.

Ingredients

  • 1 large bowl
  • 1 pineapple
  • 2 mangoes
  • 1 lime
  • 1 orange
  • 4 passion fruits
  • 1 cinnamon stick
  • 1 vanilla bean
  • 1 bottle of white rum
  • 1 pomegranate liqueur (optional)
  • Guava juice
  • Orange juice
  • Tropical juice (e.g., pineapple juice)
  • Sugar cane syrup (optional)

Instructions

  1. Cut the pineapple into small cubes, removing the core.
  2. Cut the mango in half along the seed, then slice into small pieces using a criss-cross pattern.
  3. Slice the lime and orange thinly.
  4. Empty the passion fruit pulp into the bowl, saving some for decoration.
  5. Cut the passion fruit in half and quarters for decoration.
  6. Rinse the cinnamon stick.
  7. Flatten the vanilla bean with a knife, slice it open, and scrape out the seeds.
  8. Add all prepared fruits to the large bowl.
  9. Pour in guava juice, orange juice, and tropical juice.
  10. Add the rum and a dash of pomegranate liqueur (optional).
  11. Add the passion fruit seeds, orange and lime slices, cinnamon stick, and vanilla seeds to the bowl.
  12. Stir well to combine all ingredients.
  13. Cover the bowl and refrigerate for at least 12 hours.
  14. Before serving, add a few slices of lime or orange to each glass (optional).
  15. Add a few drops of sugar cane syrup to each glass (optional).
  16. Serve chilled and enjoy!

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=s9YnZ-eYb5g

creme_aniesorel.txt - Crème Aniesorel

Objectives

  • Learn to make a historical recipe called Crème Aniesorel.
  • Understand the process of making a volute soup.
  • Learn to make a chicken and mushroom julienne garnish.

Ingredients

  • 1 Chicken Breast
  • 1 cup Chicken Stock (homemade)
  • 200 grams Mushrooms (off cuts)
  • 1 Lemon
  • 2 tablespoons Butter
  • 1 leek
  • 1 tablespoon Flour
  • 100 milliliters Cream
  • Salt and pepper to taste
  • Parsley (optional)

Instructions

  1. Poach the chicken breast in chicken stock for 10-12 minutes until cooked through.
  2. Prepare the mushroom julienne by peeling the mushrooms and slicing them into matchsticks.
  3. Toss the mushroom julienne with lemon juice and set aside.
  4. Cook the mushroom julienne in butter over medium heat for 5 minutes, adding salt and water.
  5. Remove the mushroom julienne from the pan and reserve in a bowl with some chicken stock.
  6. While the chicken breast cools, make the volute.
  7. Melt butter in a saucepan and add the leek.
  8. Sweat the leek over low heat for 5 minutes.
  9. Add flour to the saucepan and cook for 3 minutes, stirring constantly.
  10. Remove the roux from the heat and allow it to cool completely.
  11. Gradually whisk in the boiling chicken stock to the roux, starting with a small amount.
  12. Once all the roux is incorporated, add the remaining chicken stock and bring to a boil.
  13. Reduce the heat to low and simmer for 25-30 minutes.
  14. Strain the volute through a sieve, pressing down on the solids to extract as much flavor as possible.
  15. Return the volute to the saucepan and bring to a boil.
  16. Add cream and bring to a boil again.
  17. Skim off any impurities that form on the surface.
  18. Simmer for 10 minutes.
  19. Adjust seasoning with salt and pepper.
  20. Serve the volute in bowls, garnished with the mushroom julienne, poached chicken, and parsley (optional).

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-8fNmJc95fA

creme_brulee.txt - Crème Brûlée

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a classic Crème Brûlée dessert.
  • Master the dry oven technique for perfect custard consistency.
  • Understand the importance of temperature control and caramelization.

Ingredients

  • 500 ml Full Cream Milk
  • 250 ml Heavy Whipping Cream
  • 4 Egg Yolks
  • 1 Vanilla Pod
  • 100 g White Sugar
  • 50 g Brown Sugar (for caramelization)

Instructions

  1. Heat a clean saucepan over low heat.
  2. Pour in the milk and cream, then add the vanilla pod (seeds removed).
  3. Bring the mixture to a boil, then immediately turn off the heat.
  4. Stir well and let cool on the stovetop for 10-15 minutes.
  5. Preheat the oven to 100°C (210°F) using a thermometer to ensure accurate temperature.
  6. In a separate bowl, whisk together the egg yolks and white sugar until pale yellow.
  7. Slowly incorporate the cooled milk mixture into the egg yolk mixture, filtering through a sieve to remove any lumps or vanilla bits.
  8. Gently pour the mixture into ramekins, filtering again to ensure a smooth finish.
  9. Bake in the preheated oven for 45 minutes, or until the edges are set and the center is slightly wobbly.
  10. Remove from the oven and let cool to room temperature for 30-40 minutes.
  11. Refrigerate for at least 2 hours, or up to 3 hours, for optimal chilling.
  12. Before serving, sprinkle a generous layer of brown sugar over the top of each ramekin.
  13. Using a blowtorch, carefully caramelize the sugar until it forms a hard, golden crust.
  14. Let the caramel cool slightly before cracking it open with a spoon and enjoying the creamy custard.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=25NHHLXwGrU

creme_caramel.txt - Crème Caramel

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a classic French crème caramel.
  • Master the caramel sauce preparation.
  • Understand the bain-marie cooking method.

Ingredients

  • 75 grams of sugar
  • 15 ml of water
  • 500 ml of full cream milk
  • 1/4 teaspoon of vanilla powder
  • 3 eggs
  • 100 grams of sugar

Instructions

  1. Prepare the caramel sauce by combining 75 grams of sugar and 15 ml of water in a saucepan over high heat.
  2. Bring the mixture to a boil and continue cooking until it turns a golden brown color.
  3. Carefully pour the hot caramel into ramekins, coating the bottom.
  4. Preheat the oven to 180 degrees Celsius (350 degrees Fahrenheit).
  5. In a saucepan, heat 500 ml of full cream milk with 1/4 teaspoon of vanilla powder until it reaches a boil.
  6. In a separate bowl, whisk together 3 eggs and 100 grams of sugar until the mixture is light and frothy.
  7. Gradually pour the hot milk into the egg mixture, whisking constantly.
  8. Strain the mixture through a sieve to remove any lumps or egg shells.
  9. Pour the custard mixture into the prepared ramekins, filling them almost to the top.
  10. Place the ramekins in a roasting tray and pour boiling water into the tray, ensuring the water level reaches halfway up the sides of the ramekins.
  11. Bake for 35 minutes, or until the custard is set.
  12. Remove the ramekins from the oven and allow them to cool completely before refrigerating for at least an hour.
  13. To serve, run a knife around the edges of the crème caramel to loosen it from the ramekin.
  14. Invert the ramekin onto a plate and gently tap the bottom to release the crème caramel.
  15. Enjoy!

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=j5AJjC4CmNg

creme_de_tomat.txt - Crème de Tomat

Objectives

  • Learn to make a classic French tomato soup using simple ingredients.
  • Master the technique of slow-cooking onions for maximum flavor.
  • Understand the importance of using fresh, ripe tomatoes for the best taste.

Ingredients

  • 1 white onion, thinly sliced
  • 2 cloves garlic, peeled
  • 1 sprig of thyme
  • 1 pound of fresh tomatoes, chopped (or 1 can of diced tomatoes)
  • 1 tablespoon of sugar
  • 1 cup (250 ml) of chicken stock
  • 2 tablespoons of butter
  • 1/2 cup of heavy cream
  • 1 egg yolk
  • Salt and pepper to taste

Instructions

  1. In a medium saucepan over medium heat, add the butter and 1-2 tablespoons of water.
  2. Add the sliced onion and cook slowly for 10-15 minutes, until soft and translucent.
  3. Add the garlic, thyme, and chopped tomatoes to the pan.
  4. Stir in the sugar and cook for another 10 minutes, until the tomatoes have softened.
  5. Pour in the chicken stock and bring to a boil.
  6. Reduce the heat to low and simmer for 2-3 minutes, stirring occasionally.
  7. Remove the thyme sprig.
  8. Using a stick blender or a food mill, blend the soup until smooth.
  9. Return the soup to the pan and bring to a simmer.
  10. In a separate bowl, whisk together the egg yolk and heavy cream until smooth.
  11. Slowly pour the hot soup into the cream mixture, whisking constantly.
  12. Return the soup to the pan and cook over low heat, stirring constantly, until slightly thickened.
  13. Season with salt and pepper to taste.
  14. Serve warm with a garnish of fresh basil or a drizzle of olive oil.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=UAYKPO7NxU4

creme_vichyssoise.txt - Crème Vichyssoise

Objectives

  • Learn the history of Crème Vichyssoise and its relationship to Potage Parmentier.
  • Understand the key differences between the two soups.
  • Master the classic French recipe for Crème Vichyssoise.

Ingredients

  • 500 grams (about 1 pound) potatoes, peeled and cubed
  • 1 pound leeks, thinly sliced (including some green and white parts)
  • 1 medium onion, chopped
  • 1 cup (250 ml) milk
  • 1 cup (250 ml) heavy cream
  • 50 grams (about 3 tablespoons) butter
  • 1 tablespoon rock salt
  • Bouquet garni (a bundle of herbs like thyme, parsley, and bay leaf)
  • Chives, for garnish (optional)
  • Whipped cream, for garnish (optional)

Instructions

  1. Melt the butter in a large saucepan over low heat.
  2. Add the onions and leeks to the pan and cook gently for 4-5 minutes, stirring occasionally.
  3. After 5 minutes, check the pan for any browning. If there are any traces of browning, reduce the heat.
  4. Continue cooking the onions and leeks over very low heat for another 10 minutes.
  5. Add the potatoes to the pan.
  6. Pour in enough water to cover the potatoes by a few centimeters (about 3-4 cups).
  7. Bring the mixture to a boil over high heat.
  8. Once boiling, reduce the heat to medium, add the salt and bouquet garni.
  9. Cook uncovered for 30 minutes, or until the potatoes are completely cooked.
  10. Remove the bouquet garni from the pan.
  11. Use a stick blender to process the soup until it is smooth and thick.
  12. Pass the soup through a fine-mesh sieve into a clean saucepan.
  13. Add the cream and half of the milk to the soup and stir to combine.
  14. Taste the soup and adjust the seasoning with additional salt if needed.
  15. Bring the soup to a boil over medium heat.
  16. Turn off the heat and let the soup cool down completely.
  17. Transfer the cooled soup to a glass bowl and chill in the refrigerator for several hours until completely cold.
  18. For serving, garnish with a dollop of whipped cream and a sprinkle of chives.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=AvJrHwG0l-o

crepe_flambe_and_crepe_suzette.txt - Crêpe Flambé & Crêpe Suzette

Objectives

  • Learn the difference between Crêpe Flambé and Crêpe Suzette
  • Master the techniques for making both classic French desserts
  • Discover the history and origins of Crêpe Suzette

Ingredients

Crêpe Flambé

  • 45 grams unsalted butter
  • 150 ml orange juice
  • 45 grams caster sugar
  • Zest of 1 orange
  • 2 tablespoons cognac
  • 3 tablespoons Grand Marnier liqueur
  • Freshly made crêpes

Crêpe Suzette

  • 100 grams caster sugar
  • 100 grams unsalted butter
  • Zest of 1 mandarin
  • 2 tablespoons Triple Sec
  • Mandarin juice
  • Freshly made crêpes

Instructions

Crêpe Flambé

  1. Heat a pan over medium heat.
  2. Add 1 tablespoon of sugar to the pan and let it melt into caramel.
  3. Add butter, lemon juice, orange juice, and orange zest to the caramel.
  4. Reduce the heat and let the mixture simmer for 4 minutes.
  5. Stir in the Grand Marnier liqueur.
  6. Dip each crêpe into the mixture, coating both sides.
  7. Arrange the crêpes in the pan.
  8. Heat the pan over high heat.
  9. Pour cognac over the crêpes and ignite.
  10. Once the flames subside, serve immediately.

Crêpe Suzette

  1. Zest one mandarin and set aside.
  2. In a bowl, combine softened butter, sugar, and mandarin zest.
  3. Gradually mix in the Triple Sec.
  4. Add mandarin juice and mix until well combined.
  5. Heat a pan over low heat.
  6. Place a crêpe in the pan and let it warm.
  7. Flip the crêpe and add a teaspoon of the Suzette butter.
  8. Coat the crêpe with the butter.
  9. Fold the crêpe in half, then in half again.
  10. Serve immediately.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=vF_zZssIl8w

croquembouche_recipe.txt - Croquembouche

Objectives

  • Learn to make a croquembouche, a classic French dessert.
  • Understand the importance of making a pastry cream that's slightly runny.
  • Learn to make a whipped cream that's thick and fluffy.

Ingredients

Pastry Cream - 1 cup pastry cream - 1 tablespoon rum - 1 cup heavy cream - 2 tablespoons sugar - 1/2 cup white chocolate - 1/2 cup dark chocolate - 1/2 cup crushed peanuts - 500 grams caster sugar - 100 grams glucose syrup - Strawberries (optional)

Instructions

  1. Warm the pastry cream in a bowl and whisk in the rum until smooth.
  2. Beat the heavy cream with the sugar until stiff peaks form.
  3. Fold the whipped cream into the pastry cream.
  4. Fill the pastry puffs with the cream mixture.
  5. Melt the white and dark chocolate separately in a double boiler.
  6. Dip the pastry puffs in the melted chocolate, allowing the excess to drip off.
  7. Optionally, sprinkle the chocolate-coated puffs with crushed peanuts.
  8. Make a dry caramel by heating the sugar and glucose syrup in a saucepan over medium heat, stirring constantly.
  9. Dip the bottom of each puff into the caramel and stick it to the base of the croquembouche.
  10. Continue building the croquembouche in layers, pressing the puffs together to create a solid structure.
  11. Decorate the top of the croquembouche with strawberries or other desired toppings.

  • Make a classic croque monsieur and croque madame with bechamel sauce

croque_monsieur_bechamel.txt - Croque Monsieur Béchamel Sauce

Objectives

  • Learn to make a perfect Béchamel sauce for a Croque Monsieur sandwich
  • Discover basic flavoring techniques for Béchamel sauce
  • Understand the importance of temperature control in Béchamel sauce making

Ingredients

  • 50g butter
  • 50g flour
  • 1 liter milk
  • Salt
  • Pepper
  • Nutmeg
  • Optional: other flavorings like garlic, herbs, or spices

Instructions

  1. Melt the butter in a saucepan over medium heat.
  2. Add the flour and whisk continuously for 1-2 minutes, until the mixture is smooth and forms a paste.
  3. Gradually whisk in the cold milk, ensuring that the mixture is well combined.
  4. Bring the mixture to a simmer, whisking constantly, until it thickens.
  5. Reduce the heat to low and simmer for 5 minutes, whisking occasionally, to cook out the flour taste.
  6. Season with salt, pepper, and nutmeg to taste.
  7. Add any desired flavorings, such as garlic, herbs, or spices, at this point.
  8. Remove from heat and use as needed.

croque_monsieur_croque_madame.txt - Croque Monsieur & Croque Madame

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a classic French Croque Monsieur and Croque Madame.
  • Master the art of making a perfect béchamel sauce.
  • Understand the importance of using quality ingredients and proper assembly techniques.

Ingredients

  • White bread (sliced, 1 cm thick)
  • Good-quality ham
  • Gruyère cheese
  • Butter
  • Béchamel sauce
  • Egg (for croque madame)
  • Salt and pepper (to taste)

Instructions

  1. Toast the bread on both sides until lightly golden brown.
  2. Prepare the béchamel sauce:
  3. Melt butter in a saucepan over medium heat.
  4. Whisk in flour and cook for 1 minute.
  5. Gradually whisk in milk, stirring constantly until smooth.
  6. Bring to a simmer and cook for 5 minutes, stirring occasionally.
  7. Season with salt, pepper, and nutmeg.
  8. Stir in grated Gruyère cheese until melted.
  9. Assemble the croque monsieur:
  10. Spread a thin layer of béchamel sauce on one slice of toasted bread.
  11. Top with a layer of ham and grated Gruyère cheese.
  12. Place the second slice of toasted bread on top.
  13. Spread another layer of béchamel sauce on the top slice.
  14. Sprinkle with additional grated Gruyère cheese.
  15. Assemble the croque madame:
  16. Follow steps 1-3 for the croque monsieur.
  17. Fry an egg to your liking and place on top of the assembled croque monsieur.
  18. Bake both sandwiches in a preheated oven at 365°F (195°C) for 5 minutes.
  19. Serve immediately and enjoy!

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=FEKohTH10HU

croque_monsieur_vegetarian.txt - Vegetarian Croque Monsieur

Objectives

  • Learn how to make two classic French croque monsieur sandwiches, one savory and one sweet.
  • Discover the secrets to achieving a perfectly toasted and melted cheese sandwich.
  • Explore creative variations using ingredients like goat cheese, honey, and banana.

Ingredients

Croque Monsieur Provençal: - 2 slices of white bread, pre-toasted - Gruyere cheese, sliced - Fresh tomato slices - Dried Provençal herbs or Italian herbs - Olive oil

Croque Monsieur with Goat Cheese and Honey: - 2 slices of white bread, pre-toasted - French goat cheese - Honey - Dried thyme - Double cream or crème fraîche

Sweet Croque Monsieur: - 2 slices of white bread (non-toasted) - Melted butter - Sugarcane sugar - Frozen bananas - Hazelnut chocolate

Instructions

Croque Monsieur Provençal:

  1. Using a basting brush, coat both slices of bread generously with olive oil.
  2. Layer one slice of bread with a generous amount of Gruyere cheese.
  3. Add tomato slices, removing the seeds to avoid excess moisture.
  4. Season with salt and pepper, then sprinkle with Provençal herbs.
  5. Layer the other slice of bread with more Gruyere cheese and a few tomato slices.
  6. Close the sandwich, press gently, and brush the top with olive oil.
  7. Bake in the oven at 185°C (365°F) with a fan, or 200°C (392°F) without a fan, for 10-12 minutes, or until the cheese is melted and the top is toasted.
  8. If the top isn't brown enough, broil for a few minutes to achieve a nice color.

Croque Monsieur with Goat Cheese and Honey:

  1. Spread double cream or crème fraîche on both slices of bread.
  2. Add a slice of French goat cheese to each slice.
  3. Sprinkle with black pepper and a touch of honey.
  4. Finish with a sprinkle of dried thyme.
  5. Close the sandwich, press gently, and brush the top with olive oil if desired.
  6. Bake in the oven at 185°C (365°F) with a fan, or 200°C (392°F) without a fan, for a shorter time than the Provençal version to prevent dryness.

Sweet Croque Monsieur:

  1. Coat both slices of white bread with a generous layer of melted butter.
  2. Sprinkle sugarcane sugar on both sides of the bread.
  3. Add frozen banana slices to each side of the bread.
  4. Top with pieces of hazelnut chocolate.
  5. Close the sandwich, press firmly, and brush the top with melted butter.
  6. Bake in the oven until the chocolate is melted and the banana is caramelized, about 15-20 minutes.
  7. If you have a sandwich press, use it for a more even cook.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=LTAsUQzqGKY

custard_basics.txt - Custard Basics: The Foundation for French Desserts

Objectives

  • Learn the basic components of custard and its variations
  • Understand the role of eggs, sugar, and milk in custard
  • Discover three main types of custard: liquid, vanilla sauce, and pastry cream

Ingredients

Liquid Custard - 250 ml whole milk - 1/2 vanilla bean - 2-3 eggs - 50 grams sugar

Vanilla Custard - 250 ml whole milk - 1/2 vanilla bean - 2 egg yolks - 50 grams sugar

Pastry Cream - 250 ml whole milk - 1/2 vanilla bean - 2 egg yolks - 50 grams sugar - 25 grams flour - 25 grams cornstarch

Instructions

Liquid Custard 1. Warm the milk with the vanilla bean in a saucepan over medium heat. 2. Beat the eggs and sugar together until light and frothy. 3. Gradually whisk the warm milk into the egg mixture, ensuring it doesn't cook the eggs. 4. Strain the mixture to remove any foam. 5. Pour into ramekins. 6. Place ramekins in a baking dish and fill with hot water halfway up the sides of the ramekins. 7. Bake at 160 degrees Celsius for 30 minutes.

Vanilla Custard 1. Warm the milk with the vanilla bean in a saucepan over medium heat. 2. Beat the egg yolks and sugar together until light and frothy. 3. Gradually whisk the warm milk into the egg mixture, ensuring it doesn't cook the eggs. 4. Strain the mixture to remove any foam. 5. Cook the custard over medium heat, stirring constantly, until it reaches 82-83 degrees Celsius. 6. Remove from heat and immediately transfer to a container. 7. Refrigerate for at least 4 hours, ideally 12 hours.

Pastry Cream 1. Warm the milk with the vanilla bean in a saucepan over medium heat. 2. Beat the egg yolks and sugar together until light and frothy. 3. Whisk in the flour and cornstarch until well combined. 4. Gradually whisk the warm milk into the egg mixture, ensuring it doesn't cook the eggs. 5. Cook the custard over medium heat, stirring constantly, until it boils. 6. Reduce heat to low and cook for 1 minute, stirring constantly. 7. Remove from heat and transfer to a container. 8. Allow to cool completely before using.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=vCaPITa8QRc

dark_chocolate_truffle.txt - Dark Chocolate Truffles

Objectives

  • Learn to make simple dark chocolate truffles.
  • Understand the importance of using the right chocolate and cream ratio.
  • Master the technique of rolling truffles in cocoa powder.

Ingredients

  • 100g dark chocolate, chopped
  • 100ml double cream
  • 25g unsalted butter, diced
  • Cocoa powder, for dusting

Instructions

  1. Chop the chocolate into small pieces.
  2. Heat the cream in a saucepan over medium heat until it comes to a boil.
  3. Remove from the heat and slowly whisk in the chopped chocolate until it is melted and smooth.
  4. Stir in the butter, whisking until it is completely melted and the ganache is smooth.
  5. Pour the ganache into a flat container lined with plastic wrap.
  6. Cover with another layer of plastic wrap and refrigerate for at least 2 hours, or until firm.
  7. Once the ganache is firm, use a sharp knife to cut it into squares or triangles.
  8. Roll the ganache pieces in cocoa powder to coat.
  9. Refrigerate the truffles for at least 30 minutes before serving.

dew_of_ham_with_gorgonzola_tarts.txt - Dew of Ham with Gorgonzola Tarts

Objectives

  • Make a savory tart with a puff pastry base and a custard filling.
  • Use a combination of cured and standard ham, gorgonzola cheese, and yogurt for a unique flavor profile.
  • Create a fast and easy recipe perfect for a quick meal.

Ingredients

  • 1 sheet of puff pastry (pre-made)
  • 4 eggs
  • 1 cup plain yogurt
  • 2 tablespoons cream
  • 1/2 cup cured ham, diced
  • 1/2 cup standard ham, diced
  • 1/4 cup gorgonzola cheese, diced
  • Salt and pepper to taste

Instructions

  1. Preheat oven to 180 degrees Celsius (355 degrees Fahrenheit).
  2. Prepare the ingredients by dicing the ham, gorgonzola cheese, and puff pastry.
  3. Place the puff pastry in a tart pan, ensuring it fits and trimming any excess.
  4. Press the pastry into the pan using a rolling pin to create a smooth surface.
  5. Refrigerate the pastry while preparing the filling.
  6. In a bowl, whisk together the eggs, yogurt, cream, salt, and pepper.
  7. Taste the custard mixture to adjust seasoning as needed.
  8. Arrange the diced ham and gorgonzola cheese evenly in the prepared pastry shell.
  9. Carefully pour the custard mixture over the ham and gorgonzola, ensuring it covers the ingredients.
  10. Place the tart on the lower rack of the oven to ensure the bottom of the pastry is crispy.
  11. Bake for approximately 30 minutes, or until the custard is set and the pastry is golden brown.
  12. Allow the tart to cool slightly before slicing and serving.

dijon_mustard.txt - Dijon Mustard

Objectives

  • Learn the history of Dijon mustard and its significance in French cuisine.
  • Understand the traditional ingredients and preparation methods for Dijon mustard.
  • Create a homemade Dijon mustard from scratch.

Ingredients

  • Mustard seeds (black are strongest)
  • Water (for soaking seeds)
  • White wine (for grinding)
  • White wine vinegar (for flavor)
  • Rock salt (for seasoning)
  • Pestle and mortar (for grinding)

Instructions

  1. Soak the mustard seeds in water for at least two hours.
  2. Drain the seeds and place them in a sieve.
  3. Grind the mustard seeds in a pestle and mortar, adding a few tablespoons of white wine as you go.
  4. Continue grinding for approximately 10 minutes, until the seeds are finely ground and a yellow paste starts to form.
  5. Add a few tablespoons of white wine vinegar and a teaspoon of rock salt to the paste.
  6. Continue grinding until the mixture is smooth and emulsified.
  7. Taste the mustard and adjust the seasoning as needed.
  8. If desired, add a small amount of sugar to reduce any bitterness.
  9. Transfer the mustard to a sieve and press it through to create a smoother consistency.
  10. Store the mustard in a sealed container in the refrigerator for at least 3-4 days to allow the flavors to mature.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=6LU02AGrsTk

dion_chicken.txt - Dijon Chicken

Objectives

  • Learn to cook a simple, delicious Dijon chicken recipe.
  • Master the art of braising chicken in a copper pan for optimal flavor and texture.
  • Create a creamy Dijon sauce using a classic French technique.

Ingredients

  • 4 pieces of chicken
  • Salt and pepper
  • Flour (optional)
  • 40g butter
  • Bay leaves
  • Thyme
  • 200ml white wine
  • 100-200ml cream
  • 2 egg yolks
  • Dijon mustard (to taste)
  • White pepper
  • Cayenne pepper (optional)

Instructions

  1. Season the chicken pieces with salt and pepper.
  2. Dust the chicken with flour if desired, to help remove excess moisture.
  3. Heat the butter in a copper pan over medium-high heat.
  4. Sear the chicken skin-side down for 5 minutes, or until golden brown.
  5. Flip the chicken and sear the other side for another 5 minutes.
  6. Add bay leaves and thyme to the pan.
  7. Deglaze the pan with white wine, scraping up any browned bits from the bottom.
  8. Add 200ml of white wine to the pan and bring to a boil.
  9. Cover the pan with a lid and braise the chicken for 20-25 minutes, or until cooked through.
  10. Remove the chicken from the pan and set aside.
  11. Remove the bay leaves and thyme from the pan.
  12. Filter the braising juices through a fine-mesh sieve into a clean container.
  13. Clean the pan and return the filtered braising juices to the pan.
  14. Bring the juices to a boil.
  15. Reduce the braising juices until they are slightly acidic and taste strongly of chicken.
  16. Add 100-200ml of cream to the pan and bring to a simmer.
  17. Reduce the cream for 1-2 minutes, or until it coats the back of a spoon.
  18. In a separate bowl, whisk together the egg yolks and a portion of the sauce.
  19. Slowly pour the egg yolk mixture into the sauce, whisking constantly.
  20. Add Dijon mustard to the sauce, starting with 1 tablespoon and adjusting to taste.
  21. Season the sauce with white pepper and cayenne pepper, if desired.
  22. Turn the heat to low and stir the sauce constantly, par-cooking the eggs to thicken the sauce.
  23. Add the chicken pieces to the sauce and stir gently.
  24. Serve the chicken with the Dijon sauce, drizzled over or alongside.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=PFnKXYKPvNc

doffinois_soup.txt - Doffinois Soup

Objectives

  • Learn to prepare a traditional Doffinois soup, a hearty French dish
  • Understand the importance of slow cooking and the unique ingredient combinations
  • Explore the use of pre-cooked white beans for a quick and flavorful soup

Ingredients

  • 1 leek, thinly sliced
  • 1 carrot, thinly sliced
  • 1 onion, thinly sliced
  • 1 can (400g) pre-cooked white beans, rinsed
  • 1 tomato, chopped
  • 500ml beef stock
  • 500ml water
  • 1 tablespoon olive oil
  • 1 tablespoon butter
  • 1 teaspoon rock salt
  • 2-3 tablespoons crème fraîche or thick cream (optional)
  • Fresh parsley, chopped (or sorrel leaves, sautéed in butter)
  • Crusty bread, for dipping

Instructions

  1. Thinly slice the leek, carrot, and onion.
  2. Rinse the pre-cooked white beans.
  3. Heat a large pot over medium heat.
  4. Add olive oil and butter to the pot and melt.
  5. Add the sliced leek, onion, and carrot to the pot.
  6. Gently cook the vegetables for 15 minutes, stirring occasionally, until softened but not browned.
  7. Add beef stock, white beans, chopped tomato, and 1 teaspoon of rock salt to the pot.
  8. Bring the soup to a simmer, then reduce heat to low and simmer gently for 30 minutes.
  9. After 30 minutes, add crème fraîche or thick cream (optional) and chopped parsley (or sautéed sorrel leaves).
  10. Simmer for an additional 5 minutes, season with pepper to taste, and serve hot.
  11. Dip crusty bread into the soup for a traditional and satisfying experience.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Rkoyt5qjdRc

duchess_potato.txt - Duchess Potatoes

Objectives

  • Learn to make Duchess Potatoes, a French variation of mashed potatoes.
  • Understand the importance of using the right type of potatoes and drying them properly.
  • Learn to pipe Duchess Potatoes into different shapes and bake them to golden perfection.

Ingredients

  • 1 kg Sebago potatoes (or similar variety suitable for boiling)
  • Unsalted butter
  • 3 egg yolks
  • Salt
  • Nutmeg
  • Black or white pepper (optional)

Instructions

  1. Peel and cut potatoes into chunks to speed up cooking.
  2. Place potatoes in a pot with cold water and add a small amount of rock salt.
  3. Bring the pot to a boil, then reduce heat and simmer for 20-25 minutes, or until potatoes are cooked through.
  4. Drain potatoes thoroughly, ensuring no excess water remains.
  5. Mash the potatoes using a potato masher or food mill.
  6. Place the mashed potatoes in a saucepan over low-medium heat and stir gently to dry out any remaining moisture.
  7. Turn off the heat and add the butter to the mashed potatoes, incorporating it gradually until melted and evenly distributed.
  8. Add the egg yolks to the potato mixture and mix gently until combined.
  9. Season the mixture with salt, nutmeg, and pepper to taste.
  10. Heat the mixture on very low heat for 1-2 minutes, stirring continuously to ensure even seasoning.
  11. Transfer the potato mixture to a piping bag.
  12. Pipe the potato mixture onto a baking sheet in desired shapes, such as crowns or nests.
  13. Bake in a preheated oven at 200°C (425°F) for 15-20 minutes, or until golden brown.
  14. Serve hot and enjoy!

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mjdzwYREr48

duck_a_l_orange.txt - Duck à L'Orange

Objectives

  • Learn how to make the classic French dish Duck à L'Orange.
  • Master the art of creating a sweet and sour orange sauce.
  • Discover the importance of reducing ingredients to a syrupy consistency.

Ingredients

  • 2 duck breasts (recipe scaled for 4 duck breasts)
  • Juice of 2 blood oranges
  • Candied orange peel
  • Cointreau (orange liqueur)
  • Duck stock (or white chicken stock)
  • Star anise
  • 25 grams of sugar
  • Vinegar
  • Lemon juice

Instructions

  1. Prepare the orange peel marinade:
  2. Cut the orange peel into thin julienne strips.
  3. Place the julienned orange peel in a bowl.
  4. Add star anise, Cointreau, and the juice of one orange.
  5. Marinate overnight.
  6. Make the sauce:
  7. Reduce duck stock in a pan until it reaches a syrupy consistency.
  8. In a separate pan, combine sugar and vinegar.
  9. Heat over medium heat, stirring constantly, until the mixture caramelizes.
  10. Add blood orange juice and bring to a boil.
  11. Reduce until the mixture reaches a syrupy consistency.
  12. This is the gastric, the base of the sauce.
  13. Carefully add a small amount of the gastric to the reduced duck stock.
  14. Add a squeeze of lemon juice to balance the sweetness.
  15. Reduce the sauce further until it reaches your desired consistency.
  16. Prepare the garnish:
  17. Peel a turnip and use a melon baller to create small balls.
  18. Place the turnip balls in a pan with water, butter, and a bay leaf.
  19. Cover with a cartouche (a piece of parchment paper) and simmer until the water evaporates.
  20. The turnip balls should be lightly caramelized.
  21. Cook the duck breasts:
  22. Heat a pan over medium-high heat.
  23. Sear the duck breasts skin-side down for 5-6 minutes, until the skin is golden brown.
  24. Remove the excess fat from the pan.
  25. Flip the duck breasts and sear for a few more minutes.
  26. Remove the duck breasts from the pan and let them rest for 5 minutes.
  27. Finish the sauce:
  28. Place the macerated orange peel in a pan and reduce until it becomes a syrup.
  29. Add the reduced orange juice to the duck à l'orange sauce.
  30. Assemble the dish:
  31. Preheat oven to 356 degrees Fahrenheit.
  32. Warm the duck breasts in the oven.
  33. Arrange the duck breasts, glazed turnips, and candied orange peel on a plate.
  34. Drizzle with the duck à l'orange sauce.
  35. Serve immediately.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=E_FHBDN_UPo

duck_breast_green_peppercorn_sauce.txt - Duck Breast in Green Peppercorn Sauce

Objectives

  • Learn to make a classic French green peppercorn sauce
  • Cook duck breast to a perfect medium-rare
  • Combine duck breast and sauce for a delicious meal

Ingredients

  • Duck Breast
  • 1/2 tablespoon of oil
  • Salt and Pepper
  • Cognac
  • White Wine
  • Green Peppercorns in brine
  • Full cream or heavy whipping cream
  • Duck stock
  • Butter
  • Flour

Instructions

  1. Preheat oven to 70 degrees Celsius (158 Fahrenheit).
  2. Reduce duck stock by half and thicken with beurre manié (equal parts butter and flour).
  3. Season duck breasts with salt and pepper on the meaty side.
  4. Score the fatty side of the duck breast in a crosshatch pattern.
  5. Heat oil in a pan over medium heat and sear duck breasts on the fatty side for 10 minutes.
  6. Remove excess fat from the pan.
  7. Turn duck breasts and cook for 5 minutes.
  8. Add cognac to the pan and flambe.
  9. Remove duck breasts and keep warm in the oven.
  10. Deglaze the pan with white wine and reduce until almost gone.
  11. Add duck stock and reduce further.
  12. Crush green peppercorns and add to the sauce.
  13. Add cream and reduce for a few minutes.
  14. Remove from heat and stir in a knob of butter to create a silky sauce.
  15. Slice duck breast and serve with the green peppercorn sauce.

duck_legs_confit.txt - Duck Legs Confit

Objectives

  • Learn to prepare classic French duck legs confit.
  • Master the two-stage curing and cooking process.
  • Understand the importance of low and slow cooking techniques.

Ingredients

  • Duck legs
  • Duck or goose fat (about 1 liter)
  • Rock salt
  • Peppercorns
  • Juniper berries
  • Thyme (about 1 teaspoon)
  • Bay leaves (3-4)
  • Garlic cloves (3)

Instructions

  1. Wash your hands thoroughly before handling raw meat.
  2. Prepare the spiced salt:
  3. Grind rock salt using a pestle and mortar until semi-coarse.
  4. Add peppercorns, juniper berries, thyme, and bay leaves.
  5. Grind all ingredients together until well combined.
  6. Cure the duck legs:
  7. Generously rub the spiced salt onto each duck leg, massaging it in thoroughly.
  8. Wrap each leg individually in plastic wrap.
  9. Refrigerate for 24 hours.
  10. Remove excess moisture and salt:
  11. Unwrap the duck legs and discard the excess salt and herbs.
  12. Use a brush or your hands to remove any remaining salt from the surface of the legs.
  13. Cook the duck legs:
  14. Preheat duck fat in a pan over low heat to 90-95 degrees Celsius (200 degrees Fahrenheit).
  15. Add garlic cloves and bay leaves to the fat.
  16. Add duck legs to the pan, skin-side down.
  17. Cover the legs with parchment paper and weigh down to ensure they are submerged in the fat.
  18. Cook for a minimum of 2 hours, or up to 3 hours, until the meat is tender and easily detaches from the bone.
  19. Serve the duck legs:
  20. Remove the legs from the fat and drain on paper towels.
  21. To crisp the skin, pan-fry or broil the legs for 5 minutes per side.
  22. Serve with a simple green salad.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=UhwKM3DzT_Q

duck_sauce.txt - Sauce Shia (Duck Sauce)

Objectives

  • Learn to make a spicy, flavorful sauce with Caribbean origins.
  • Understand the history and cultural significance of the sauce.
  • Explore the use of fresh herbs and chilies for a vibrant flavor profile.

Ingredients

  • 1-2 cloves garlic, minced
  • 1/4 cup olive oil
  • 1-2 limes, juiced and zested
  • 1/2 cup water
  • 1/4 cup spring onions, thinly chopped
  • 1/4 cup parsley, thinly chopped
  • 1-2 habanero peppers, thinly chopped (or scotch bonnet peppers)
  • Salt and pepper to taste

Instructions

  1. Mince the garlic and add it to a bowl with the olive oil. Allow the garlic to infuse in the oil.
  2. Finely chop the spring onions, parsley, and habanero peppers.
  3. Zest one or two limes, adding the zest to the bowl with the herbs and chilies.
  4. In a separate saucepan, combine the lime juice and water. Bring to a simmer over medium heat.
  5. Once the water mixture is simmering, turn off the heat and pour it into the bowl with the herbs, chilies, and garlic-infused oil.
  6. Mix the ingredients together and let them sit for a few minutes to allow the flavors to meld.
  7. Taste the sauce and adjust the seasoning with salt and pepper as needed.
  8. To create an emulsion, add olive oil to the sauce mixture in small increments, whisking continuously until the desired consistency is achieved.
  9. Transfer the sauce to a serving bowl and allow it to macerate at room temperature for 1-2 hours before serving.
  10. Serve the sauce over grilled fish, meat, chicken, or lobster.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=KPadsuLx1PM

duck_stock.txt - Duck Stock

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a brown duck stock.
  • Understand the importance of browning the bones for flavor.
  • Learn how to properly store and preserve duck stock.

Ingredients

  • duck bones
  • 1/2 tablespoon oil (peanut, grapeseed, or sunflower)
  • 1/2 cup white wine (Sauvignon Blanc)
  • 1 cup duck stock
  • 1 cup water
  • carrots
  • onion
  • juniper berries
  • black peppercorns
  • rosemary
  • bay leaves
  • sage
  • thyme
  • parsley stalks

Instructions

  1. Heat a stock pot or large pan over very high heat.
  2. Add the duck bones and cook for 10 minutes, turning occasionally to ensure even browning.
  3. Add the chopped carrots and onions to the pot and cook for 5-10 minutes on medium-low heat, until softened.
  4. Increase the heat and add the white wine.
  5. Reduce the wine until almost all liquid is evaporated.
  6. Add the duck stock and water, along with the peppercorns, juniper berries, rosemary, bay leaves, sage, thyme, and parsley stalks.
  7. Bring the mixture to a boil, then reduce heat to a gentle simmer.
  8. Cover the pot, leaving a small opening for steam to escape.
  9. Simmer for 40 minutes to an hour, or until the stock has reached desired consistency.
  10. Remove the bones and strain the stock through a sieve into a clean container.
  11. Allow the stock to cool completely.
  12. Store the stock in the refrigerator for up to 48 hours or freeze for longer storage.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Ei5Krc_wx7g

easy_cheesecake.txt - Easy Cheesecake

Objectives

  • Learn to make a simple, crustless cheesecake with orange flavor.
  • Understand the importance of preparing the baking tin properly.
  • Discover a quick and easy method for blending cheesecake ingredients.

Ingredients

  • 4 eggs
  • 500 grams of fresh cream cheese (Philadelphia Cream Cheese)
  • Orange peel (grated)
  • 2 tbsp of orange liqueur (Cointreau)
  • 250 milliliters of heavy whipping cream
  • 200 grams of sugar
  • 1 tablespoon of butter
  • 1/2 tablespoon of plain flour

Instructions

  1. Grease the inside and sides of a baking tin with butter.
  2. Line the tin with parchment paper, ensuring it adheres to the sides.
  3. Cut the cream cheese into manageable pieces and leave at room temperature.
  4. Beat the eggs in a bowl.
  5. Grate the orange peel and mix it with the orange liqueur.
  6. Combine all ingredients (except the cream cheese) in a food processor.
  7. Add the cream cheese to the food processor and blend until smooth.
  8. Pour the mixture into the prepared baking tin.
  9. Bake in a preheated oven at 200 degrees Celsius (392 Fahrenheit) for approximately 45 minutes.
  10. Let the cheesecake cool completely before serving.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VqBFPc-nmrw

easy_puff_pastry.txt - Easy Puff Pastry

Objectives

  • Learn how to make easy puff pastry using only 3 ingredients.
  • Create a versatile puff pastry for savory applications like charcuterie, pates, and small goods.
  • Understand the importance of cold butter and proper folding techniques.

Ingredients

  • 75 milliliters of water
  • 250 grams of all-purpose flour
  • 200 grams of plain unsalted butter
  • a pinch of salt

Instructions

  1. Combine the flour and salt in a large bowl.
  2. Cut the cold butter into small cubes and sprinkle them over the flour.
  3. Gently incorporate the butter into the flour using your hands, ensuring there are flakes and small balls of butter remaining.
  4. Gradually add the water, using your hands to form a dough.
  5. Shape the dough into a ball and place it on a lightly floured surface.
  6. Flatten the dough into a rectangle.
  7. Wrap the dough in plastic wrap and refrigerate for 30 minutes.
  8. Lightly flour your work surface and use a tape measure to ensure the dough is 15 centimeters wide and 45 centimeters long.
  9. Roll the dough out in one direction, extending it to the desired length.
  10. Fold the dough into thirds, like a letter.
  11. Rotate the dough 90 degrees and roll it out again to the original length.
  12. Repeat the folding process two more times.
  13. Refrigerate the dough for 15 minutes.
  14. The puff pastry is now ready to be used. Roll it out to your desired shape and bake as needed.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=CqJA8KbmqB4

easy_shortcrust_by_hand.txt - Easy Shortcrust Pastry By Hand

Objectives

  • Learn to make a simple, easy-to-roll shortcrust pastry by hand.
  • Understand the importance of cold ingredients and minimal kneading.
  • Discover a new favorite shortcrust recipe for both sweet and savory tarts.

Ingredients

  • 250g cold unsalted butter, diced
  • 375g plain flour, sifted
  • 1 egg yolk
  • 100ml whole milk
  • Pinch of salt (for savory tarts)
  • 1 teaspoon sugar (optional, for sweet tarts)

Instructions

  1. Sift flour into a large bowl.
  2. Add diced cold butter to the bowl.
  3. Use your fingertips to rub the butter into the flour, creating a sandy mixture.
  4. In a separate bowl, whisk together milk, egg yolk, salt, and sugar (if using).
  5. Pour the liquid mixture into the flour and butter mixture.
  6. Use a spatula to "hack" the dough, mixing the dry and wet ingredients until a dough forms.
  7. Remove the dough from the bowl and gather it into a ball.
  8. Knead the dough briefly on a lightly floured surface using a gentle pressing motion.
  9. Shape the dough into a disc, wrap it in plastic wrap, and refrigerate for at least one hour.
  10. Before rolling, remove the dough from the refrigerator 15-20 minutes before use to allow it to soften slightly.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=IJqZbtJel80

egg_in_a_pot.txt - Egg in a Pot (Cocotte)

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a classic French egg in a pot (cocotte).
  • Explore variations with chorizo, cheese, and other ingredients.
  • Master the quick and efficient cooking technique.

Ingredients

  • Butter
  • Salt
  • Pepper
  • Eggs
  • Chorizo (optional)
  • Cheddar cheese (optional)
  • Heavy cream
  • Nutmeg
  • Spanish paprika (optional)

Instructions

  1. Grease the inside of the ramekins with butter using a brush.
  2. Season the ramekins with salt and pepper.
  3. Crack one egg into each ramekin, ensuring the yolk is centered.
  4. For a chorizo version, add a small amount of chopped chorizo and grated cheddar cheese to the bottom of the ramekin before adding the egg.
  5. Place a piece of baking paper in the bottom of a pot to prevent the ramekins from touching the bottom.
  6. Fill the pot with 1 centimeter of water.
  7. Bring the water to a boil.
  8. Carefully place the ramekins into the boiling water.
  9. Cover the pot and cook for 2.5 minutes.
  10. Remove the ramekins from the pot and set aside.
  11. While the eggs are cooking, reduce heavy cream in a saucepan over medium heat, adding salt and nutmeg for flavor.
  12. Spoon the reduced cream over the cooked eggs.
  13. Garnish with Spanish paprika for a sweet and smoky flavor.
  14. Serve immediately.

egg_omelet.txt - Œufs en Meurette

Objectives

  • Learn to make a classic French dish called Œufs en Meurette.
  • Understand the importance of reducing wine to concentrate flavors.
  • Learn how to poach eggs in red wine for a unique taste.

Ingredients

  • 1 tablespoon butter
  • 1 onion, diced
  • 1 carrot, diced
  • 1 shallot, diced
  • 100g mushrooms, diced
  • 100g bacon, cut into matchsticks
  • 1/2 liter red wine
  • 200 ml beef stock
  • 1 sprig parsley
  • 1 sprig thyme
  • 1 bay leaf
  • 1 baguette
  • Garlic
  • 4 eggs
  • Water
  • Vinegar

Instructions

  1. Dice the onion, carrot, shallot, and mushrooms into small cubes.
  2. Cut the bacon into matchsticks.
  3. Melt the butter in a saucepan over medium heat.
  4. Add the diced vegetables and cook for 10 minutes, covered.
  5. Blanch the bacon in boiling water for a few seconds, then rinse under cold water.
  6. Add the bacon to the vegetables and mix well.
  7. Pour in the red wine and bring to a boil.
  8. Reduce the wine by half, skimming off any scum that forms on the surface.
  9. Add the beef stock, parsley, thyme, and bay leaf.
  10. Bring to a boil again and reduce by 2/3.
  11. While the sauce is reducing, prepare the croutons.
  12. Use a cookie cutter to cut out circles from the white part of the baguette.
  13. Infuse the croutons with garlic oil by brushing them with a garlic-infused oil.
  14. Fry the croutons in a non-stick pan over medium heat until golden brown.
  15. To poach the eggs, bring a pan of water, vinegar, and red wine to a simmer.
  16. Gently crack the eggs into a separate bowl and make sure the egg white is tightly attached to the yolk.
  17. Carefully slide the eggs into the simmering liquid.
  18. Allow the eggs to poach for a few minutes until the whites are set.
  19. Remove the eggs from the poaching liquid and place on a paper towel to drain.
  20. Strain the sauce through a sieve, pressing down on the solids to extract as much juice as possible.
  21. Add a tablespoon of butter to the sauce and stir until melted.
  22. Season the sauce with salt and pepper to taste.
  23. To serve, place a few croutons on a plate and drizzle with the sauce.
  24. Top with a poached egg and spoon more sauce over the top.
  25. Garnish with a sprinkle of bacon and parsley.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=XgTcxX-nw20

eggs_shimei.txt - Eggs Shimei

Objectives

  • Learn to prepare a classic French vegetarian dish, Eggs Shimei.
  • Master the techniques of making hard-boiled eggs, duxelles of mushrooms, and mornay sauce.
  • Understand the history and origins of the Eggs Shimei recipe.

Ingredients

  • Eggs
  • Mushrooms
  • Shallots
  • Parsley
  • Butter
  • Flour
  • Milk
  • Nutmeg
  • Salt
  • Cheese (Gruyère or Emmental recommended)
  • Lemon juice (optional)
  • Rock salt (optional)

Instructions

  1. Prepare the hard-boiled eggs:
    • Bring a pot of water to a boil.
    • Gently add the eggs one at a time to the boiling water.
    • Once the water returns to a boil, start timing for 10 minutes for medium-sized eggs (up to 60 grams).
    • After 10 minutes, turn off the heat and remove the eggs from the water.
    • Plunge the eggs into a bowl of cold water to stop the cooking process.
  2. Prepare the duxelles of mushrooms:
    • Melt butter in a pan over low heat.
    • Add shallots and sweat for 1 minute.
    • Add mushrooms and mix well.
    • Increase heat to medium and cook until the mushrooms release their water and the mixture is dry.
    • Add parsley and rock salt to taste.
    • Turn off the heat and set aside.
  3. Prepare the bechamel sauce:
    • Warm milk in a saucepan with trimmings from the mushrooms, shallots, a pinch of salt, and grated nutmeg.
    • Bring to a simmer and let infuse for a few minutes.
    • In a clean pan, melt butter over low heat.
    • Add flour in equal amounts to the butter and cook for 1-2 minutes to make a paste.
    • Turn off the heat and let the roux cool.
    • Strain the infused milk through a fine sieve into the roux.
    • Whisk constantly over medium heat until the sauce thickens.
    • Simmer for 1-2 minutes.
    • Turn off the heat and let the bechamel sauce cool.
  4. Prepare the mornay sauce:
    • Add an egg yolk to the cooled bechamel sauce and whisk until incorporated.
    • Add grated cheese and whisk until melted.
  5. Assemble the Eggs Shimei:
    • Peel the hard-boiled eggs and cut them in half lengthwise.
    • Carefully remove the egg yolks and reserve them.
    • Mix the egg yolks with a small amount of the duxelles of mushrooms.
    • Fill the egg whites with the mushroom mixture.
    • Place a small amount of mornay sauce in the bottom of a serving dish.
    • Arrange the filled egg halves in the dish, standing them upright.
    • Cover the eggs with mornay sauce.
    • Sprinkle with additional grated cheese.
  6. Broil the Eggs Shimei:
    • Place the dish under a preheated broiler until the cheese is melted and golden brown.
    • Serve immediately.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=RDNmiEr1hnQ

endives_gratinee.txt - Endives Gratin

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a classic French Endives Gratin
  • Discover techniques to minimize the bitterness of endives
  • Prepare and cook endives for a delicious gratin with ham, bechamel, and cheese

Ingredients

  • 5-6 endives
  • Fresh ham
  • Chicken stock
  • Butter
  • Lemon juice
  • Salt
  • Black pepper
  • Cheese (for bechamel and topping)

Instructions

  1. Prepare the endives by removing any brown outer leaves and trimming the ends.
  2. Melt butter in a pan with a thick bottom over medium heat.
  3. Sear the endives on each side for 2-3 minutes, giving them a slight coloration.
  4. Add chicken stock, a squeeze of lemon juice, and salt to the pan.
  5. Cover the pan and simmer the endives for 45 minutes on low heat, adding water if needed.
  6. While the endives cook, prepare the ham by ensuring it is large enough to wrap around each endive.
  7. Drain the cooked endives and let them rest on a kitchen towel to remove excess moisture.
  8. Wrap each endive in a slice of ham, ensuring the endive is visible.
  9. Place the ham-wrapped endives in a buttered baking dish.
  10. Prepare a bechamel sauce (refer to the cream of mushroom video for instructions).
  11. Add cheese to the bechamel sauce and melt.
  12. Pour the bechamel sauce over the endives in the baking dish.
  13. Sprinkle black pepper and cheese over the bechamel.
  14. Bake in the oven at 220 degrees Celsius (428 degrees Fahrenheit) for 15 minutes, using only the bottom element.
  15. If the gratin is not brown enough after 15 minutes, broil for an additional 5 minutes to achieve a crusty, golden cheese topping.
  16. Let the gratin cool slightly before serving.

epoch_house_wine.txt - Époques Wine

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a cold, spiced wine.
  • Discover the historical significance of spices in wine.
  • Create a festive and refreshing beverage for the holidays.

Ingredients

  • 1 bottle of red wine
  • 1/2 cup honey
  • 1 inch ginger, peeled and sliced
  • 4-5 cinnamon sticks
  • 1/4 cup cloves
  • 1/4 cup cardamom seeds, crushed
  • 1 orange, sliced
  • cheesecloth or muslin cloth

Instructions

  1. Warm the red wine in a cast-iron pan over low heat.
  2. Add the honey and stir until melted.
  3. Add the ginger, cinnamon sticks, and orange slices.
  4. Combine the crushed cloves and cardamom seeds in a cheesecloth or muslin cloth to create a spice bag.
  5. Add the spice bag to the pan.
  6. Simmer gently for 5 minutes.
  7. Remove from heat and let cool completely.
  8. Transfer the wine to a carafe and refrigerate for at least one night, up to 10 days.
  9. Serve chilled.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_qc04acHPz0

escoffier_salad_composite.txt - Escoffier Salad Composite

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a classic Escoffier salad composite.
  • Understand the six base dressings Escoffier recommends.
  • Prepare a variety of vegetables and dressings for a stunning salad platter.

Ingredients

  • Lettuce
  • Beetroot (oven cooked)
  • Celery AK (raw)
  • Tomatoes (fresh)
  • Onions (oven cooked)
  • Hard-boiled eggs (optional, for decoration)
  • Salt (rock salt recommended)
  • Pepper (black and white)
  • Egg yolks
  • Shallots
  • Onion
  • Lemon juice
  • Parsley
  • Oil (sunflower, peanut, or grapeseed)
  • Mustard
  • Red wine vinegar
  • Cream fraiche
  • Cayenne pepper (optional)

Instructions

  1. Prepare the vegetables:
  2. Boil eggs and keep them in water.
  3. Roast beetroot and onions at 180 degrees Celsius for about an hour.
  4. Wash and detail lettuce.
  5. Clean tomatoes.
  6. Make the French dressing (Vinaigrette):
  7. In a bowl, combine a pinch of salt, a pinch of pepper, and a teaspoon of mustard.
  8. Add one tablespoon of vinegar and whisk to combine.
  9. Gradually add 3 tablespoons of oil while whisking until emulsified.
  10. Reserve in the fridge.
  11. Make the sauce remoulade (mustard mayonnaise):
  12. In a bowl, combine a pinch of salt, a pinch of pepper, one egg yolk, and a teaspoon of mustard.
  13. Whisk until combined.
  14. Gradually add 200 ml of oil while whisking until emulsified.
  15. Add a squeeze of lemon juice and whisk again.
  16. Reserve in the fridge.
  17. Prepare the celery AK:
  18. Cut the celery AK in half.
  19. Peel the skin using a peeler.
  20. Immediately squeeze lemon juice over the celery AK to prevent oxidation.
  21. Grate the celery AK using a coarse grater.
  22. Assemble the celery AK salad:
  23. Combine the grated celery AK with the sauce remoulade.
  24. Add a squeeze of lemon juice and a dash of cayenne pepper (optional).
  25. Mix well until combined.
  26. Reserve in the fridge.
  27. Prepare the beetroot:
  28. Peel the beetroot and cut into small, square-shaped cubes.
  29. Prepare the onions:
  30. Finely slice the onions.
  31. Make the mustard cream dressing:
  32. In a bowl, whisk one teaspoon of mustard with 100 ml of cream until slightly thickened.
  33. Add the juice of half a lemon and whisk again.
  34. Assemble the beetroot salad:
  35. Combine the beetroot cubes and sliced onions in a bowl.
  36. Pour the mustard cream dressing over the beetroot mixture.
  37. Gently mix until coated.
  38. Prepare the tomatoes:
  39. Remove the base of the tomatoes.
  40. Slice the tomatoes as thinly as possible.
  41. Prepare the shallots:
  42. Finely slice the shallots.
  43. Assemble the salad composite:
  44. Arrange the tomatoes in a base layer on a platter.
  45. Place the celery AK salad on the side of the platter.
  46. Arrange the lettuce in the center of the platter.
  47. Arrange the beetroot salad on top of the lettuce.
  48. Sprinkle thinly sliced shallots over the tomatoes.
  49. Drizzle the French dressing over the tomatoes and other areas of the platter.
  50. Sprinkle chopped parsley over the tomatoes for color.
  51. Serve and enjoy!

far_breton.txt - Far Breton

Objectives

  • Learn to make a traditional Breton dessert called Far Breton.
  • Understand the importance of a beurre noisette for flavor.
  • Discover the versatility of this simple cake recipe.

Ingredients

  • 200g salted butter
  • 150g flour
  • 150g sugar
  • 1 vanilla bean
  • 4 eggs
  • 250ml milk
  • 1 tablespoon of rum
  • 150g prunes soaked in cognac (or water)

Instructions

  1. Melt the salted butter in a saucepan over medium heat.
  2. Continue heating until the butter foams and turns a light brown color, creating a beurre noisette.
  3. Remove from heat and set aside to cool slightly.
  4. In a large bowl, combine the flour, sugar, and vanilla seeds.
  5. Create a well in the center of the dry ingredients.
  6. Add the eggs one at a time, incorporating each egg fully before adding the next.
  7. Gradually add the milk, mixing until a smooth batter forms.
  8. Add the rum and mix well.
  9. Gently fold in the cooled beurre noisette.
  10. Place the soaked prunes (with stones removed) in the bottom of a pie dish.
  11. Pour the batter over the prunes, ensuring the prunes are fully covered.
  12. Bake in a preheated oven at 180°C (355°F) for 25-40 minutes, or until golden brown and set.
  13. Allow the Far Breton to cool slightly before serving.
  14. Serve lukewarm or at room temperature with coffee.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=u7HYdRNNoKM

fennel_prep.txt - Fennel Preparation

Objectives

  • Learn how to properly prepare a fennel bulb for cooking.
  • Understand the different uses of fennel and its properties.
  • Discover the best combinations for fennel in dishes.

Ingredients

  • 1 fennel bulb

Instructions

  1. Remove any excess stems and leaves from the fennel bulb.
  2. Cut off the bottom part of the bulb that is brown and fibrous.
  3. Carefully remove the outer layer of leaves, being careful not to damage the bulb.
  4. Wash the fennel bulb thoroughly under running water.
  5. Cut the fennel bulb in half lengthwise.
  6. Remove any tough or fibrous parts from the core of the bulb.
  7. Depending on the desired use, cut the fennel into quarters, slices, or smaller pieces.
  8. If eating raw, remove the core for a softer texture.
