french_mayonnaise.txt - French Mayonnaise

Objectives

  • Learn the simple and authentic French technique for making mayonnaise.
  • Discover the key ingredients and proportions for a perfect emulsion.
  • Understand the importance of using love and a good mood while making mayonnaise.

Ingredients

  • 1 egg yolk
  • A pinch of salt
  • A bit of pepper
  • A few drops of vinegar
  • 1 teaspoon of Dijon mustard
  • 150 ml of oil

Instructions

  1. Combine one egg yolk, a pinch of salt, a bit of pepper, a few drops of vinegar, and a generous teaspoon of Dijon mustard in a bowl.
  2. Mix the ingredients thoroughly until well blended.
  3. Start adding oil gradually, a little at a time, while whisking gently.
  4. Continue whisking and adding oil until the mixture starts to thicken.
  5. Add the remaining oil, whisking continuously, until the mayonnaise reaches your desired consistency.
  6. Transfer the mayonnaise to a container for storage or serving.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=AHGpyrRRlx0

french_meringue_dessert.txt - Vasa or Ice Cream Meringue Dessert

Objectives

  • Learn how to make French meringue.
  • Learn how to use a food ring for professional presentation.
  • Create a delicious and visually appealing Valentine's Day dessert.

Ingredients

French Meringue: - 2 egg whites - 120 grams castor sugar - 1-2 drops of vanilla extract

Raspberry Sauce: - 1 cup fresh raspberries - 1/2 cup confectionery sugar - 1/4 cup lemon juice

Whipped Cream: - 100 grams fresh mascarpone cheese - 30 grams sugar - 250 ml heavy cream

Additional: - Vanilla ice cream - Raspberry sorbet - Fresh raspberries for decoration

Instructions

  1. Prepare the French Meringue:
  2. Separate egg whites and place in a bowl with a pinch of salt.
  3. Whisk using a hand mixer until foamy.
  4. Gradually add 1/3 of the sugar and continue whisking until stiff peaks form.
  5. Transfer meringue to a clean container.
  6. Add remaining sugar and vanilla extract, folding gently with a rubber spatula until incorporated.
  7. Pipe the Meringue:
  8. Transfer meringue to a piping bag fitted with a round tip.
  9. Using a food ring lightly oiled, mark a circle on a baking sheet.
  10. Pipe the meringue in a circular pattern within the marked ring.
  11. Sprinkle with icing sugar (optional).
  12. Bake in the oven at 100 degrees Celsius (200 degrees Fahrenheit) for at least 1 hour.
  13. Make the Raspberry Sauce:
  14. Wash and set aside a few raspberries for decoration.
  15. Combine remaining raspberries, confectionery sugar, and lemon juice in a saucepan.
  16. Simmer over low heat until the raspberries break down and the sauce thickens.
  17. Strain the sauce through a fine-mesh sieve to remove seeds.
  18. Refrigerate until ready to use.
  19. Assemble the Dessert:
  20. Remove the vanilla ice cream and raspberry sorbet from the freezer a few minutes before assembling.
  21. Place a food ring on a plate.
  22. Scoop a layer of vanilla ice cream into the ring, pressing down to compact it.
  23. Top with a layer of raspberry sorbet.
  24. Repeat the layers of ice cream and sorbet.
  25. Cover the top with plastic wrap and freeze for at least 30 minutes.
  26. Make the Whipped Cream:
  27. Combine mascarpone cheese and sugar in a bowl and mix until smooth.
  28. Gradually add heavy cream and whisk until stiff peaks form.
  29. Transfer the whipped cream to a piping bag fitted with a star tip.
  30. Assemble the Final Dessert:
  31. Remove the frozen ice cream stack from the freezer.
  32. Place a meringue disc on a serving plate.
  33. Carefully remove the ice cream stack from the food ring and place it on top of the meringue.
  34. Pipe whipped cream around the edge of the ice cream stack.
  35. Garnish with fresh raspberries.
  36. Serve immediately.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=gVRZ6jOoQns

french_mussel_white_wine.txt - Moules Marinières (French Mussels in White Wine)

Objectives

  • Learn how to prepare and cook delicious French-style mussels in white wine.
  • Understand the importance of cleaning mussels before cooking.
  • Discover a simple and authentic recipe that can be easily recreated at home.

Ingredients

  • 1 kg mussels
  • 1 shallot
  • 2 garlic cloves
  • 1 celery stalk
  • 1 bay leaf
  • 1 sprig thyme
  • 200 ml dry white wine (ideally French)
  • 100 g unsalted butter
  • Fresh parsley
  • Salt and pepper to taste
  • Optional: 1 tablespoon double cream

Instructions

  1. Clean the mussels by removing any beards or barnacles. Scrub any seaweed off the shells with a knife or use scissors to cut them off.
  2. Finely chop the shallot, garlic, celery, parsley, and thyme.
  3. Combine the chopped ingredients in a blender or food processor and blend until finely chopped.
  4. Melt the butter in a large pot over low heat.
  5. Add the herb mixture to the melted butter and cook until fragrant.
  6. Add the mussels to the pot and pour in the white wine.
  7. Bring the mixture to a boil.
  8. Once boiling, give the mussels a good stir to ensure they are coated in the wine.
  9. Cover the pot and cook for 5-6 minutes, or until the mussels have opened.
  10. Remove the pot from the heat and discard any mussels that haven't opened.
  11. If desired, add a tablespoon of double cream to the sauce and stir to combine.
  12. Serve the mussels with a generous amount of the creamy sauce. Enjoy!

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=XAajvodGE48

french_omelet.txt - French Omelet

Objectives

  • Learn to make a classic French omelet using a professional technique.
  • Understand the importance of low heat and precise timing for a perfect omelet.
  • Avoid browning the omelet during cooking.

Ingredients

  • 3 eggs
  • 1 tablespoon of butter
  • 1 tablespoon of oil
  • Salt
  • White pepper

Instructions

  1. Crack 3 eggs into a bowl and whisk until well combined.
  2. Add salt and white pepper to taste.
  3. Heat a 22cm non-stick pan with an aluminum base over low heat.
  4. Add butter and oil to the pan and swirl to coat.
  5. Pour the egg mixture into the pan.
  6. Gently swirl the pan to distribute the egg evenly and create a smooth surface.
  7. Cook the omelet, constantly monitoring the heat to prevent browning.
  8. When the omelet is almost set but still slightly wet on top, fold it in half.
  9. Continue cooking until the omelet is fully set.
  10. Remove the omelet from the pan and serve immediately.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2fqahITH4Ho

french_onion_soup.txt - French Onion Soup

Objectives

  • Learn to make a classic French onion soup.
  • Create a flavorful stock base for the soup.
  • Assemble the soup with toasted bread and melted cheese.

Ingredients

  • 400 grams of sliced onion
  • 1/2 liter of water
  • 1/2 liter of beef or veal stock
  • 50 grams of butter
  • 1 bouquet garni
  • Salt and pepper
  • 1 rump steak (optional)
  • Toasted bread
  • Gruyere cheese (or similar)

Instructions

  1. Prepare the Stock:
    • Heat a pan on high heat and add a small amount of oil.
    • Sear the rump steak until well-browned on all sides.
    • Add the water and stock to the pan.
    • Bring to a boil, then reduce heat to a simmer and cook for at least 30 minutes.
  2. Caramelize the Onions:
    • Melt the butter in a cast-iron pan or a pan with a thick bottom over medium-low heat.
    • Add the sliced onions and cook slowly, stirring occasionally, until they are soft and caramelized.
    • Season with salt and pepper.
  3. Combine and Simmer:
    • Gradually add the stock to the caramelized onions, scraping up any browned bits from the bottom of the pan.
    • Add the bouquet garni.
    • Simmer for 20 minutes, covered.
  4. Assemble the Soup:
    • Remove the bouquet garni.
    • Place two pieces of toasted bread in the bottom of an oven-safe bowl.
    • Pour the soup over the bread.
    • Top with additional toasted bread.
    • Sprinkle with 100-200 grams of Gruyere cheese (or similar).
  5. Broil and Serve:
    • Place the bowl under a broiler until the cheese is melted and bubbly.
    • Serve immediately.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Co6ej47MOVE

french_pantry_live_chat.txt - The French Pantry: A Live Chat with Livia

Objectives

  • Explore the essential ingredients and staples of a French pantry
  • Understand the importance of using high-quality ingredients in French cooking
  • Gain insights into Livia's personal cooking journey and experiences

Instructions

  1. Start with the essential spices: bay leaves, onions, shallots, and garlic.
  2. Include these vegetables in your fridge: carrots, fresh parsley, leeks, and celery.
  3. Always have these staples in your pantry: salt, pepper, olive oil, red wine vinegar, and Dijon mustard.

  5. Don't forget eggs, sugar, and flour for baking and sauces.
  6. Use full cream milk (or whole milk in America) for most recipes.
  7. Incorporate butter, especially French butter, for rich flavor.
  8. Keep a dry white wine, like Chablis, for cooking and pairing with cheese.
  9. Use a good quality red wine, like Bordeaux, for sauces.
  10. Always have a baguette on hand for sandwiches and snacks.

french_pasta_salad.txt - Pasta Salad à la Française

Objectives

  • Learn a simple French pasta salad recipe.
  • Understand the importance of fresh ingredients for this dish.
  • Enjoy a light and refreshing pasta salad perfect for hot weather.

Ingredients

  • 200 grams pasta (pappardelle)
  • 2 cloves garlic, pressed
  • 1/2 lemon, juiced
  • 1/2 lemon, zested
  • Olive oil
  • Salt
  • Pepper
  • Parsley, chopped
  • Basil leaves
  • Mint leaves

Instructions

  1. Prepare the garlic oil: Combine olive oil, pressed garlic, and a pinch of salt in a small saucepan. Heat over medium heat for 20 seconds, then remove from heat.
  2. Cook the pasta: Bring a large pot of salted water to a boil. Add the pasta and cook until al dente.
  3. Drain the pasta: Drain the pasta and immediately add it to the garlic oil mixture. Toss gently to coat.
  4. Prepare the herb mixture: In a large bowl, combine chopped parsley, basil leaves, and mint leaves.
  5. Make the dressing: In a separate bowl, whisk together lemon juice, salt, pepper, and a drizzle of olive oil.
  6. Combine the pasta and dressing: Add the pasta to the herb mixture. Toss well to combine.
  7. Add the final touches: Drizzle with additional olive oil, add lemon zest, and toss again.
  8. Serve immediately: Enjoy your pasta salad!

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=5ljrBqQ3ASg

french_pepper_steak.txt - French Pepper Steak

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a classic French pepper steak with a flavorful sauce.
  • Understand the importance of using good quality ingredients and proper cooking techniques.
  • Discover the secret ingredient that gives this dish its distinctive flavor.

Ingredients

  • 1 Porterhouse steak (or any prime cut of beef)
  • Salt
  • Black pepper
  • 1 shallot, thinly diced
  • Butter
  • Cognac
  • Cream
  • Brown stock
  • White wine

Instructions

  1. Season the steak with salt and pepper on both sides. Let it sit for 10 minutes to allow the pepper flavor to infuse into the meat.
  2. Heat a cast iron pan over medium heat.
  3. Add the steak to the pan and cook for 3 minutes per side, without moving it.
  4. Once the steak is cooked, deglaze the pan with cognac. You can flambe it if you like.
  5. Remove the steak from the pan and place it in a preheated oven to keep warm.
  6. Melt butter in the pan over low heat.
  7. Add the shallots and cook for 5-10 seconds.
  8. Add the white wine and deglaze the pan, scraping up any browned bits.
  9. Reduce the wine until it is almost dry.
  10. Add the brown stock and reduce until the sauce is syrupy.
  11. Add cream to adjust the consistency and color of the sauce.
  12. Return the steak to the pan for a few seconds to warm it up and coat it with the sauce.
  13. Serve the steak with the sauce on top.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=cbGMJ1MjuI4

french_potato_salad.txt - Salade de Pommes de Terre

Objectives

  • Learn to make a classic French bistro potato salad.
  • Understand the importance of proper food preparation for salads.
  • Learn how to use food stackers to create beautiful salad presentations.

Ingredients

  • 1 yellow-fleshed potato, peeled and diced
  • 1/2 cup ham, diced
  • 1/4 cup gherkins, diced
  • 1/4 cup parsley, chopped
  • 2 hard-boiled eggs, sliced
  • 1 ripe tomato, seeded and diced
  • Homemade mayonnaise
  • Salt and pepper to taste

Instructions

  1. Peel and dice the potato into small cubes.
  2. Dice the ham into small cubes.
  3. Dice the gherkins into small cubes.
  4. Chop the parsley finely.
  5. Slice the hard-boiled eggs.
  6. Seed and dice the tomato into small cubes.
  7. Boil the potatoes in cold salted water for 15 minutes.
  8. Drain the potatoes and rinse with cold water to stop the cooking process.
  9. In a large bowl, combine the potatoes, ham, gherkins, and parsley.
  10. Add the mayonnaise and gently mix until well combined.
  11. Season with salt and pepper to taste.
  12. Gently fold in the tomatoes.
  13. Place a food stacker in the center of a plate.
  14. Fill the stacker with the potato salad mixture, pressing down to create layers.
  15. Top with sliced eggs.
  16. Gently remove the stacker to reveal the beautifully layered salad.
  17. Decorate the salad as desired.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MvMpSsSV6LI

french_ratatouille.txt - French Ratatouille

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a simple and delicious French Ratatouille.
  • Master the "one on one off" cutting technique for vegetables.
  • Discover how to create a beautiful and flavorful dish with minimal effort.

Ingredients

  • 1 large onion
  • 2 bell peppers (one red, one yellow)
  • 1 courgette (zucchini)
  • 4-5 tomatoes
  • 1 clove of garlic
  • Olive oil
  • 1 bay leaf
  • Bouquet garni (available in supermarkets)
  • Fresh thyme (optional)
  • Salt
  • Black pepper
  • Tomato sauce (optional)
  • Fennel and cumin seeds (optional)
  • French bread (optional)
  • Basil (optional)

Instructions

  1. Peel the onion and use the "one on one off" technique to cut it into rough strips.
  2. Slice the onion into 1 cm thick pieces.
  3. Cut the bell peppers into 1 cm cubes.
  4. Slice the courgette into 1 cm thick pieces.
  5. Heat a large pot over high heat and add a generous amount of olive oil.
  6. Add the onions, garlic, and bell peppers to the pot.
  7. Stir the vegetables and cook for a few minutes until they start to soften and release their aroma.
  8. Add the courgette, tomatoes, bay leaf, bouquet garni, and fresh thyme (if using).
  9. Stir well to combine all the ingredients.
  10. Season with salt and black pepper.
  11. Reduce heat to low, cover the pot with a lid, and simmer for 15 minutes.
  12. After 15 minutes, remove the lid and discard the bay leaf and bouquet garni.
  13. If desired, add a tablespoon or two of tomato sauce to enhance the tomato flavor. Stir gently.
  14. Serve the Ratatouille as a side dish with fish or white meats.
  15. For a more gourmet presentation, arrange the Ratatouille in a terracotta dish, sprinkle with fennel and cumin seeds, and serve with toasted bread and a sprig of basil.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=4L7IzA52Yj4

french_roux.txt - French Roux

Objectives

  • Understand what a French roux is and its purpose
  • Learn how to make a white, blonde, and brown roux
  • Identify the key ingredients and timing for each type of roux

Ingredients

  • 40 grams butter
  • 40 grams flour

Instructions

  1. Set the stove to low heat.
  2. Melt the butter in a rounded saute pan.
  3. Once the butter is completely melted, add the flour.
  4. Stir continuously to create a paste.
  5. For a white roux, cook for 3-4 minutes.
  6. For a blonde roux, cook for 4-6 minutes.
  7. For a brown roux, cook for 6-8 minutes.
  8. Stir constantly throughout the cooking process to prevent burning.
  9. Once the desired color is achieved, remove from heat and cool.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=UKSWqgY-Ffk

french_sauce_classification.txt - French Sauce Classification: A Modern Approach

Objectives

  • Understand the modern classification of French sauces, moving beyond the traditional "mother sauces."
  • Explore the key categories of sauces based on color, emulsification, and sweetness.
  • Learn about the importance of "ajud" in modern kitchens and its role as a replacement for the traditional "espagnole" sauce.

Ingredients

Instructions

  1. The traditional "mother sauce" classification is outdated and rarely used in modern kitchens.
  2. The modern classification is based on color, emulsification, and sweetness.
  3. White sauces: These include any sauces using a white stock, milk, or fish fumet.
  4. Brown sauces: These include any sauces using a brown stock (beef, veal, chicken, game, or crustacean), often with a tomato base.
  5. Emulsified sauces:
  6. Warm emulsified sauces: These are created by combining two ingredients that don't typically mix, such as butter and egg yolks, using vigorous whisking. Examples include béarnaise, hollandaise, and butter sauces.
  7. Cold emulsified sauces: These include vinaigrettes and mayonnaise, which are also created through emulsification.
  8. Sweet sauces: These include both cold sauces (fruit-based) and warm sauces (chocolate sauce, salted caramel sauce, etc.).
  9. The "ajud" is a modern, versatile sauce base that has replaced the traditional "espagnole" sauce in many kitchens.
  10. Ajud is made by reducing a stock (often chicken) with meat trimmings, mirepoix, tomato paste, wine, and other flavorings.
  11. The resulting sauce is thick, flavorful, and can be used as a base for a variety of dishes.
  12. The modern approach to sauce classification emphasizes flexibility and adaptability, allowing chefs to create unique and delicious sauces based on their preferences and the ingredients available.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=SkK28MEdbvg

french_sausage_meatballs.txt - French Sausage Meatballs

Objectives

  • Create party snack meatballs using iconic French sausages.
  • Transform chipolata and merguez sausages into easy-to-make meatballs.
  • Enjoy the authentic flavors of French sausage in a new format.

Ingredients

Chipolata - 1 kg pork shoulder, lean parts (pre-seasoned with salt and pepper) - 500 g pork fat (hard fat or fat back)

Merguez - 500 g lamb - 250 g beef - 1 tablespoon olive oil - 1 teaspoon cumin - 1 teaspoon paprika - 1 teaspoon cayenne pepper - 1 teaspoon marisa - 1 clove garlic, minced - 1 tablespoon mint - 1 teaspoon harissa (optional) - 50 ml water (optional)

Instructions

  1. Prepare the Meat: Wash hands thoroughly and ensure all equipment is clean.
  2. Chipolata:
  3. Grind the pre-seasoned pork shoulder through a meat grinder using a coarse grid attachment.
  4. Grind the pork fat separately.
  5. Combine the ground meat and fat using a paddle attachment, mixing until sticky and gooey.
  6. Refrigerate the mixture for at least 30 minutes.
  7. Merguez:
  8. Grind the lamb and beef through a meat grinder using a coarse grid attachment.
  9. Add all spices, olive oil, garlic, mint, and harissa (optional) to the ground meat.
  10. Mix everything together using a paddle attachment.
  11. Add water (optional) if the mixture is too dry.
  12. Refrigerate the mixture for at least 30 minutes.
  13. Form Meatballs: Roll the chilled sausage mixtures into meatballs.
  14. Bake: Preheat oven to 200°C (400°F).
  15. Cook: Place meatballs on a baking sheet and bake for 10-15 minutes, or until cooked through.
  16. Serve: Enjoy the chipolata meatballs with mustard and the merguez meatballs with a dollop of harissa.

french_savory_crepes.txt - French Savory Crepes (Crêpes au Jambon, Fromage et Champignons)

Objectives

  • Learn to make French-style savory crepes filled with ham, cheese, and mushrooms.
  • Master the art of making a classic béchamel sauce and a flavorful mushroom duxelles.
  • Recreate the taste and texture of frozen supermarket crepes from France.

Ingredients

For the Crepes: - 100g flour - 2 eggs - 250ml milk - 1 tsp salt - 1 tbsp butter, melted, plus more for cooking

For the Mushroom Duxelles: - 200g mushrooms, finely chopped - 1 shallot, finely chopped - 1/2 onion, finely chopped - 2 cloves - 1 tbsp butter - 1 tbsp lemon juice - Salt and pepper to taste - 1 tsp parsley, chopped

For the Creamy Bechamel Sauce: - 40g butter - 40g flour - 500ml milk - 1 onion, studded with cloves - 1 bay leaf - Salt to taste - 200ml double cream - 40g Gruyère cheese, grated

For the Filling: - 100g ham, finely chopped - Gruyère cheese, grated

Instructions

  1. Make the Crepe Batter:
  2. In a bowl, whisk together the flour, salt, and eggs.
  3. Gradually add the milk, whisking constantly to avoid lumps.
  4. Stir in the melted butter.
  5. Cover the bowl with plastic wrap and let the batter rest in the refrigerator for 1 hour.
  6. Prepare the Mushroom Duxelles:
  7. Melt butter in a pan over medium heat.
  8. Add the shallots and onions and cook until softened, about 2 minutes.
  9. Add the mushrooms and cook until they release their moisture.
  10. Add lemon juice, salt, and pepper.
  11. Reduce the heat to low and cook until the moisture evaporates and the mushrooms are concentrated, about 10 minutes.
  12. Stir in the parsley and set aside.
  13. Make the Creamy Bechamel Sauce:
  14. Warm the milk in a saucepan with the onion, cloves, and bay leaf.
  15. Melt the butter in a separate pan over medium heat.
  16. Whisk in the flour and cook for 2 minutes, stirring constantly.
  17. Gradually whisk in the warm milk, removing the onion, cloves, and bay leaf.
  18. Cook over low heat, stirring constantly, until the sauce thickens.
  19. Remove from heat and stir in the double cream and grated Gruyère cheese.
  20. Divide the sauce into two bowls.
  21. Prepare the Fillings:
  22. In one bowl of béchamel sauce, stir in the mushroom duxelles.
  23. In the other bowl of béchamel sauce, stir in the chopped ham and grated Gruyère cheese.
  24. Cook the Crepes:
  25. Heat a non-stick crepe pan over medium heat.
  26. Lightly brush the pan with butter.
  27. Pour a thin layer of batter into the pan, swirling it to cover the bottom evenly.
  28. Cook for 1 minute per side or until golden brown.
  29. Repeat with the remaining batter.
  30. Assemble the Crepes:
  31. Place a thin layer of the mushroom filling or the ham and cheese filling in the center of each crepe.
  32. Fold the crepes into a rectangle or roll them into a cigar shape.
  33. Freeze and Reheat:
  34. Wrap the crepes in plastic wrap and freeze for at least 24 hours.
  35. To reheat, place the frozen crepes in a pan with a knob of butter over low heat.
  36. Cook for 5 minutes per side or until heated through and crispy.
  37. Serve:
  38. Serve the crepes warm with a side salad.

Tips: - To make thinner crepes, use a smaller amount of batter per crepe. - For a richer flavor, use whole milk instead of skim milk. - You can add other fillings to the crepes, such as spinach, onions, or peppers. - To prevent the crepes from sticking, make sure the pan is hot enough before adding the batter. - If the crepes are too thick, add a little more milk to the batter. - If the crepes are too thin, add a little more flour to the batter.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=SvyuzrXwTic

french_shortcrust.txt - French Shortcrust: A Comprehensive Guide

Objectives

  • Learn the four types of French shortcrust and their distinct uses.
  • Understand the ingredients and characteristics of each type.
  • Gain knowledge to confidently choose the right shortcrust for any recipe.

Ingredients

Pâte Brisée (Savory Shortcrust)

  • Flour
  • Butter
  • Salt
  • Water

Pâte Sucrée (Sweet Shortcrust)

  • Flour
  • Butter
  • Sugar
  • Eggs

Pâte Sablée (Sandy Shortcrust)

  • Flour
  • Butter
  • Sugar
  • Eggs
  • Almond Meal (sometimes)

Pâte à Foncer (Tart Lining)

  • Flour
  • Butter
  • Sugar
  • Eggs

Instructions

  1. Pâte Brisée: The easiest shortcrust, used for savory preparations like quiches and tarts. It's made with flour, butter, salt, and water. It's easy to roll and handle, and doesn't require blind baking.

  2. Pâte à Foncer: A classic all-around sweet shortcrust, similar to Pâte Brisée but with added sugar and eggs for a richer, softer texture. It's used for sweet tarts with toppings that can be cooked in the oven, like apple or apricot tarts. No blind baking is needed.

  3. Pâte Sucrée: A sweet shortcrust designed for blind baking to create a tart shell. It's made with lots of sugar, butter, eggs, and often almond meal. It's very sticky and difficult to work with, requiring two layers of plastic wrap and chilling to handle. It's used for tarts with fillings that can't be cooked in the oven, like strawberry tarts with pastry cream.

  4. Pâte Sablée: A sandy shortcrust made with dry ingredients and butter rubbed together to create a sandy texture. It's used for biscuits, cake bases, and cheesecake crusts. It's the most fiddly to handle and cook, requiring careful handling and often needing to be cooked with a cookie cutter in place.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=PHJELMW5v5k

french_tabuli.txt - French Tabuli

Objectives

  • Learn to make a simple and delicious French tabuli.
  • Understand the importance of using fresh ingredients and proper hydration techniques.
  • Discover how to assemble and dress a tabuli for optimal flavor.

Ingredients

  • 100g bulgur
  • 2 lemons
  • 2-3 tbsp parsley
  • 2-3 tbsp mint leaves
  • 2-3 tbsp spring onion
  • 2-3 tbsp cherry tomatoes
  • 2-3 tbsp olive oil
  • salt and pepper to taste

Instructions

  1. Rinse 100g of bulgur under cold water.
  2. Place the bulgur in a bowl and cover with boiling water.
  3. Let the bulgur soak for 15 minutes.
  4. While the bulgur is soaking, thinly slice the spring onion, roughly chop the parsley and mint leaves, and halve the cherry tomatoes.
  5. Drain the bulgur and spread it on a tray lined with paper towels to dry further.
  6. Once the bulgur has cooled, transfer it to a large bowl.
  7. Add the parsley, mint leaves, spring onion, and cherry tomatoes to the bowl.
  8. Squeeze the juice of 2 lemons over the mixture.
  9. Add 2-3 tablespoons of olive oil and mix well.
  10. Season with salt and pepper to taste.
  11. Let the tabuli sit for 10-15 minutes before serving.

french_toast.txt - Pain Perdu

Objectives

  • Learn to make French toast using a traditional French recipe.
  • Understand the key ingredients and techniques for a delicious Pain Perdu.
  • Discover the origins of this classic French dessert.

Ingredients

  • Baguette (French bread)
  • Eggs
  • Milk
  • Sugar
  • Vanilla extract

Instructions

  1. Cut the baguette into thick slices.
  2. In a bowl, whisk together eggs, milk, sugar, and vanilla extract.
  3. Dip each slice of bread into the egg mixture, making sure it's fully coated.
  4. Heat a non-stick pan over medium heat.
  5. Add a small amount of butter to the pan and swirl to coat.
  6. Cook the bread slices for 2-3 minutes per side, until golden brown and cooked through.

french_tomato_sauce.txt - French Tomato Sauce

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a classic French tomato sauce.
  • Master the art of making a roux.
  • Understand the importance of simmering and straining for a smooth sauce.

Ingredients

  • 1 tablespoon butter
  • 1/2 cup diced bacon
  • 1/2 cup diced carrots
  • 1/2 cup diced onions
  • 2 tablespoons flour
  • 1/2 cup tomato puree
  • 1 cup chicken or vegetable stock
  • 1/2 cup diced tomatoes
  • 1 clove garlic, minced
  • 1 shallot, minced
  • 1/4 cup homemade bouguignon
  • Salt and pepper to taste
  • 1 tablespoon butter (for finishing)

Instructions

  1. Melt butter in a saucepan over medium heat.
  2. Add bacon and cook until lightly browned.
  3. Add carrots and onions and cook until softened, about 5 minutes.
  4. Sprinkle in flour and cook for 1 minute, stirring constantly.
  5. Add tomato puree and cook for 2 minutes, stirring constantly.
  6. Remove from heat and let cool for 15 minutes.
  7. Bring stock to a boil in a separate saucepan.
  8. Add the cooled roux to the boiling stock, stirring constantly.
  9. Add diced tomatoes, garlic, shallot, bouguignon, salt, and pepper.
  10. Bring to a boil, then reduce heat and simmer for 1 hour.
  11. Strain the sauce through a fine-mesh sieve.
  12. Return the strained sauce to the saucepan.
  13. Add a knob of butter and swirl to melt.
  14. Serve immediately or store in the refrigerator for later use.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=YK0vwL9NzPI

french_vegetable_puree.txt - French Vegetable Puree

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a simple vegetable puree.
  • Understand the different types of vegetables and their properties.
  • Master the techniques for making smooth and flavorful purees.

Ingredients

  • Potatoes (1 kg)
  • Turnips (500 g)
  • Carrots (as needed)
  • Butter (as needed)
  • Cream (as needed)
  • Milk (as needed)
  • Shallots (as needed)
  • Chicken or vegetable stock (as needed)
  • Salt (12 g per liter of water)
  • Pepper (to taste)

Instructions

  1. Cut potatoes, turnips, and carrots into uniform pieces to ensure even cooking.
  2. Potatoes: Cook in cold salted water for 20-25 minutes.
  3. Turnips: Bring water to a boil, add salt, and then add turnips. Cook for 20 minutes.
  4. Carrots: Melt butter in a pan over medium-low heat. Add shallots and cook for 1-2 minutes. Add carrots, stock, and salt. Cover with parchment paper and cook for 30 minutes.
  5. Drain the cooked turnips and set aside to cool.
  6. Drain the cooked potatoes and pass them through a food mill to create a smooth puree.
  7. Add milk and cream to the potato puree, incorporating gradually until desired consistency is reached.
  8. Finish with butter, stirring until melted.
  9. Drain the turnips and pass them through a sieve to remove fibers.
  10. Add 25% of the potato puree to the turnips, along with butter, and whisk until blended.
  11. Season with salt and pepper.
  12. Puree the cooked carrots using a stick blender.
  13. Pass the carrot puree through a sieve to remove any remaining chunks.
  14. Add cream to the carrot puree, incorporating gradually until desired consistency is reached.
  15. Warm the carrot puree gently until the cream thickens slightly.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=QzWTCH300Pw

french_vegetable_stock.txt - French Vegetable Stock (Bouillon de Légumes)

Objectives

  • Learn to make a flavorful French vegetable stock using the "cooking by expansion" method
  • Understand the importance of using less-than-perfect vegetables for a delicious stock
  • Master the technique of gently simmering the stock for optimal flavor extraction

Ingredients

  • 1 leek (roughly chopped)
  • 1 large carrot (roughly chopped)
  • 1 celery stalk (roughly chopped)
  • 1/2 onion (pricked with cloves)
  • 1/2 bunch flat leaf parsley
  • 1 bunch fresh thyme
  • 2 liters of cold water
  • 1/2 teaspoon rock salt
  • 1/4 teaspoon peppercorns

Instructions

  1. Wash, peel, and roughly chop all vegetables, except for the celery.
  2. Prepare the aromatic bunch: Combine the leek, carrot, celery, onion, parsley, and thyme.
  3. In a stock pot, combine the chopped vegetables and cold water.
  4. Add the aromatic bunch to the pot.
  5. Bring the pot to a simmer over low heat.
  6. Simmer gently for 30 minutes, then add salt and peppercorns.
  7. Continue simmering for another 30-40 minutes, or until the vegetables are fully cooked.
  8. Remove the aromatic bunch and the onion from the stock.
  9. Strain the stock through a fine-mesh sieve, pressing on the vegetables to extract as much liquid as possible.
  10. Discard the vegetable solids.

Enjoy your flavorful and clear French vegetable stock!

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Qlq3ENnRdIg

frog_legs_lyon.txt - Lyon Style Frog Legs with Garlic and Parsley

Objectives

  • Learn how to prepare and cook frog legs in the traditional Lyon style.
  • Understand the importance of proper seasoning and browning for optimal flavor.
  • Discover the unique taste and texture of frog legs, similar to a meaty fish.

Ingredients

  • Frog legs (skinned and prepared)
  • Flour
  • Salt
  • Pepper
  • Butter
  • Oil
  • Parsley
  • Garlic
  • Lemon

Instructions

  1. Remove any excess flesh from the frog legs, reserving only the legs.
  2. Rinse the frog legs thoroughly under cold water to remove any impurities.
  3. Pat the frog legs dry with a clean towel.
  4. Place the frog legs in the refrigerator while you prepare the parsley and garlic.
  5. Chop parsley and garlic finely.
  6. Season the frog legs generously with salt and pepper.
  7. Coat each frog leg in flour, tapping off any excess to create a thin coating.
  8. Heat a cast iron pan over medium-high heat.
  9. Add butter and oil to the pan, allowing the butter to foam.
  10. Arrange the frog legs in the pan with the muscle-rich, round part touching the oil.
  11. Reduce heat to medium and cook the frog legs, turning them occasionally to ensure even browning.
  12. Once the frog legs have achieved a golden-brown color, remove them from the pan and set aside.
  13. Turn off the heat and add the parsley and garlic mixture to the pan.
  14. Toss the frog legs with the parsley and garlic mixture.
  15. Serve immediately with a squeeze of fresh lemon.

garlic_cream_sauce.txt - Garlic Cream Sauce

Objectives

  • Create a simple, elegant garlic cream sauce using only two ingredients
  • Highlight the importance of using locally sourced, fresh garlic
  • Demonstrate the blanching technique to reduce the pungency of garlic

Ingredients

  • 200 ml cream (organic Shawls brand is recommended)
  • 80 grams white garlic (French style)
  • 1 liter water
  • 30 grams salt
  • 1 tablespoon water (for blending)
  • Salt and pepper to taste
  • Optional: 1 small clove fresh garlic

Instructions

  1. Peel the garlic cloves and remove the germ.
  2. Rinse the garlic under clean running water.
  3. Blanch the garlic in boiling salted water (1 liter water and 30 grams salt).
  4. Bring the water to a boil with the garlic.
  5. Turn off the heat as soon as the water boils.
  6. Drain the garlic using a paper towel.
  7. Blend the blanched garlic with 1 tablespoon of water until smooth.
  8. You can also use a food processor for easier blending.
  9. Heat the cream in a saucepan over medium-high heat.
  10. Bring the cream to a boil, then reduce the heat to low.
  11. Reduce the cream by a third, until it reaches a semi-thick consistency.
  12. Add the garlic puree to the reduced cream, stirring constantly.
  13. Season with salt and pepper to taste.
  14. Optionally, add a tiny bit of fresh garlic for a stronger garlic flavor.
  15. Serve the sauce warm over steak, fish, or vegetables.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=tUqvs4Ras0E

garlic_flan.txt - Garlic Flan

Objectives

  • Learn to make a simple garlic confit.
  • Prepare a unique garlic flan recipe.
  • Discover the subtle sweetness of pink garlic.

Ingredients

  • 1 bunch pink garlic
  • 1 sprig thyme
  • 1 bay leaf
  • 50 ml water
  • 150 ml olive oil
  • 500 ml milk
  • 250 ml heavy whipping cream
  • 2 whole eggs
  • 1 egg yolk
  • Pinch of salt
  • Pinch of pepper
  • Nutmeg (optional)
  • Butter

Instructions

  1. Detach the garlic cloves from the bunch.
  2. For the confit garlic: Place garlic cloves with skin on in a saucepan. Add thyme, bay leaf, water, and olive oil. Simmer on low heat for 45-60 minutes.
  3. For the flan: Blanch garlic cloves in boiling water for 1 minute. Rinse with cold water.
  4. In a saucepan, bring milk to a boil. Add blanched garlic cloves and reduce heat to low. Simmer for 30 minutes, reducing the milk to 250 ml.
  5. Gently crush the garlic-infused milk with a blender.
  6. Strain the milk mixture through a sieve.
  7. Add 250 ml heavy whipping cream to the strained milk.
  8. Add 2 whole eggs and 1 egg yolk to the milk and cream mixture.
  9. Season with salt, pepper, and nutmeg (optional).
  10. Preheat oven to 150 degrees Celsius (300 degrees Fahrenheit).
  11. Place a piece of baking paper at the bottom of a deep container.
  12. Butter four ramekins and place them in the container.
  13. Pour the garlic mixture into the ramekins.
  14. Pour water into the container, filling it to 3/4 of the height of the ramekins.
  15. Bake for 30 minutes, ensuring the water simmers but does not boil.
  16. To check if the flan is cooked, insert a knife into the center. If it comes out clean, the flan is done.
  17. To unmold, run a hot knife around the edges of the ramekin. Carefully invert the flan onto a plate.
  18. Garnish with confit garlic, thyme, parsley, and a pinch of paprika.
  19. Serve and enjoy!

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=QyOgRrv__QM

garlic_mousse.txt - Garlic Mousse

Objectives

  • Learn the principles of emulsification and its application in sauces.
  • Understand the difference between stable and unstable emulsions.
  • Master the technique of making a versatile garlic mousse.

Ingredients

  • 1 large garlic clove (Mexican or Russian garlic)
  • 1/2 cup neutral oil
  • 1 tablespoon lemon juice
  • Salt
  • Black pepper (optional)

Instructions

  1. In a food processor, combine the garlic and salt.
  2. Process until a paste forms.
  3. Slowly add the oil, processing until a mousse-like consistency is achieved.
  4. Add the lemon juice, processing for about 40 seconds.
  5. Taste and adjust the seasoning with additional lemon juice, salt, or pepper.
  6. Transfer the garlic mousse to a bowl.
  7. Store in an airtight container in the refrigerator for up to a week.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rh1UWHRnbl0

gateau_basque.txt - Gateau Basque

Objectives

  • Learn to make a classic Gateau Basque from the southwest of France.
  • Understand the key components: a sweet short crust and pastry cream.
  • Discover how to assemble and bake a layered cake in a tart ring.

Ingredients

Pastry - 250g plain flour - 10g baking powder - 150g caster sugar - 200g cold unsalted butter, diced - 8 egg yolks - Zest of 1 lemon (optional)

Pastry Cream - 500ml whole milk - 1 vanilla bean, seeds scraped - 100g caster sugar - 4 egg yolks - 25g plain flour - 15g cornflour - 50g unsalted butter, softened - 1 tsp rum (optional)

Instructions

  1. Sift flour and baking powder into a large bowl.
  2. Add sugar and mix well.
  3. Add diced cold butter and use your fingertips to rub it into the flour mixture until it resembles coarse breadcrumbs.
  4. Add egg yolks one at a time, mixing well after each addition.
  5. Stir in lemon zest, if using.
  6. Bring the dough together into a ball, but do not overwork it.
  7. Wrap the dough in plastic wrap and refrigerate for at least 1 hour.
  8. While the dough is chilling, prepare the pastry cream.
  9. Heat milk and vanilla bean seeds in a saucepan over medium heat.
  10. In a separate bowl, whisk together sugar, egg yolks, flour, and cornflour until smooth.
  11. Gradually whisk the hot milk into the egg yolk mixture.
  12. Return the mixture to the saucepan and cook over medium heat, whisking constantly, until thickened.
  13. Remove from heat and stir in softened butter and rum, if using.
  14. Pour the pastry cream onto a baking sheet lined with parchment paper.
  15. Cover with plastic wrap, ensuring it touches the surface of the cream to prevent a skin from forming.
  16. Refrigerate the pastry cream until completely chilled.
  17. Divide the chilled dough in half.
  18. Place one half of the dough between two sheets of plastic wrap and roll out into a 20cm diameter circle.
  19. Carefully transfer the rolled-out dough to a tart ring placed on a baking sheet lined with parchment paper.
  20. Repeat steps 18 and 19 with the other half of the dough.
  21. Brush the bottom disc of dough with egg wash.
  22. Pipe the chilled pastry cream onto the bottom disc, leaving a 3cm border around the edge.
  23. Brush the edge of the pastry cream with egg wash.
  24. Carefully place the top disc of dough over the pastry cream.
  25. Use your fingers to press the edges of the top and bottom discs together to seal.
  26. Brush the entire top of the cake with egg wash.
  27. Using the back of a fork, create decorative patterns on the top of the cake.
  28. Refrigerate the cake for at least 30 minutes before baking.
  29. Preheat oven to 180°C (350°F).
  30. Bake the cake for 45 minutes, or until golden brown.
  31. Let the cake cool slightly in the tart ring before carefully removing it.
  32. Allow the cake to cool completely on a wire rack before serving.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=EyFPTKkWptU

glazed_carrots.txt - Glazed Carrots in the Style of Joël Robuchon

Objectives

  • Learn a fine-dining technique for glazing carrots.
  • Elevate a simple carrot dish with a complex glaze.
  • Create a visually stunning and flavorful side dish.

Ingredients

  • 1 pound carrots, peeled and sliced thinly
  • 1 tablespoon cumin seeds
  • 1 tablespoon sugar
  • 2 cloves garlic, minced
  • 2 tablespoons olive oil
  • Salt to taste
  • 1 bouquet garni (thyme, parsley, bay leaf)
  • 1/2 cup water
  • 1/2 cup freshly squeezed orange juice
  • 1 tablespoon butter
  • Fresh coriander leaves for garnish

Instructions

  1. Place the sliced carrots in a large bowl.
  2. Add the cumin seeds, sugar, minced garlic, olive oil, and salt to the bowl.
  3. Mix the ingredients with your hands until the carrots are evenly coated.
  4. Heat a large saute pan over medium heat.
  5. Spread the carrots in a single layer in the pan, making sure they are flat.
  6. Place the bouquet garni in the center of the pan.
  7. Carefully add water to the pan, just enough to reach halfway up the carrots.
  8. Cover the pan with a lid and bring the water to a boil.
  9. Reduce the heat to a simmer and cook for 10-11 minutes, or until the carrots are tender.
  10. Remove the lid and carefully pour out any excess water.
  11. Add the orange juice to the pan and continue to cook, uncovered, until the liquid has reduced and the carrots are glazed.
  12. Remove the bouquet garni from the pan.
  13. Continue cooking, gently rocking the pan, until the glaze caramelizes slightly.
  14. Garnish with fresh coriander leaves and serve.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=YJDYMxMncmU

gougeres_cheese_puffs.txt - Gougeres: Cheese Puffs

Objectives

  • Learn to make classic French cheese puffs (gougeres)
  • Master the choux pastry technique for savory applications
  • Discover tips for achieving perfectly puffed and golden gougeres

Ingredients

  • 1 cup (240 ml) Water
  • 1/2 cup (1 stick) Unsalted Butter
  • 1/2 teaspoon Salt
  • 1/4 teaspoon Black Pepper
  • 1 cup (120 g) All-Purpose Flour
  • 3 Large Eggs
  • 1 cup (100 g) Grated Cheese (Cheddar, Gruyere, or similar)
  • Pinch of Nutmeg (optional)

Instructions

  1. Preheat oven to 400°F (200°C). This is crucial for puffing the gougeres.
  2. In a saucepan, combine water, butter, salt, and pepper. Bring to a simmer over medium heat.
  3. Once the butter is melted and the mixture is simmering, immediately turn off the heat.
  4. Add the flour all at once, whisking vigorously until a smooth dough forms (panada).
  5. Return the pan to the stovetop over very low heat and cook for 3 minutes, constantly stirring to dry out the dough.
  6. Transfer the dough to a large bowl and let it cool slightly.
  7. While the dough cools, beat the eggs in a separate bowl.
  8. Gradually add the beaten eggs to the cooled dough, mixing well after each addition. The consistency should be smooth and slightly runny, forming ribbons when lifted with a spoon.
  9. Stir in the grated cheese and a pinch of nutmeg, if desired.
  10. Transfer the dough to a piping bag fitted with a star tip.
  11. Pipe the dough onto a baking sheet lined with parchment paper or a silicone mat, forming small mounds.
  12. Use a wet finger to smooth out any pointy peaks on the gougeres.
  13. Bake for 20-25 minutes at 400°F (200°C) or until golden brown and puffed.
  14. Reduce the oven temperature to 300°F (150°C) and continue baking for another 10-15 minutes to dry out the inside of the gougeres. Do not open the oven door during this time.
  15. Let the gougeres cool slightly before serving. Enjoy!

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=E9pNgzsDZbo

grand_aioli.txt - Grand Aioli

Objectives

  • Learn to make a traditional French vegetable platter called "Grand Aioli"
  • Prepare aioli from scratch using a mortar and pestle
  • Cook vegetables and boiled eggs to create a colorful and delicious platter

Ingredients

English | Characters ------- | -------- 4 garlic cloves | 4瓣大蒜 2 egg yolks | 2个蛋黄 2 pinches of salt | 2小撮盐 200 ml sunflower oil | 200毫升葵花籽油 100 ml olive oil | 100毫升橄榄油 Broccoli | 西兰花 Carrot | 胡萝卜 Asparagus | 芦笋 Radishes | 小萝卜 Potatoes | 马铃薯 Boiled eggs | 煮鸡蛋

Instructions

  1. Wash, trim, and peel all vegetables.
  2. Ensure vegetables are roughly the same size for even cooking and presentation.
  3. Prepare the aioli:
  4. Remove the germ from the garlic cloves.
  5. Roughly chop the garlic cloves and crush them into a paste using a mortar and pestle.
  6. Add two egg yolks and salt to the garlic paste and mix well.
  7. Gradually add the sunflower oil, whisking constantly until the mixture thickens.
  8. Add the olive oil slowly, whisking until fully incorporated.
  9. Taste and adjust the seasoning as needed.
  10. Bring a large pot of water to a boil and add salt.
  11. Cook vegetables in boiling water, starting with white vegetables, then carrots, and finally green vegetables.
  12. Cook vegetables until they are tender but still have a slight bite.
  13. Plunge cooked vegetables into ice water to stop the cooking process and preserve their color.
  14. Boil eggs in a separate pot of boiling water for 10 minutes.
  15. Plunge boiled eggs into ice water to cool.
  16. Drain vegetables and eggs.
  17. Arrange vegetables and eggs on a platter.
  18. Serve the aioli in a bowl alongside the platter.
  19. Enjoy!

grandma_chicken.txt - Grandma Chicken

Objectives

  • Learn to cook a simple and comforting French chicken dish.
  • Master the technique of blanching bacon and caramelizing onions.
  • Understand the importance of building blocks in French cooking.

Ingredients

  • 1 whole chicken, cut into pieces
  • 1/2 glass of dried white wine
  • Button mushrooms
  • 1 onion
  • Flour
  • Butter
  • Smoked bacon
  • Parsley

Instructions

  1. Blanch the bacon by placing it in a pan with cold water, covering it with water, and bringing it to a boil.
  2. Once the water boils, immediately turn off the heat and rinse the bacon with cold water.
  3. Pat the bacon dry and flash fry it in a pan with a half tablespoon of oil.
  4. Remove the bacon and reserve the fat in the pan.
  5. Add the mushrooms to the pan and cook for 5 minutes.
  6. Add the bacon back to the pan, mix well, and reserve it on the side.
  7. Caramelize the onions by placing them in a pan with a tablespoon of butter, a teaspoon of sugar, and a little bit of water.
  8. Simmer the onions until they are caramelized.
  9. Salt and pepper the chicken pieces and brown them in a pan for 5 minutes.
  10. Add the chicken breast to the pan, skin side down, and let it brown for 10 minutes.
  11. Remove the chicken from the pan and reserve it.
  12. Discard the excess oil from the pan and caramelize the juices of the chicken.
  13. Add the white wine to the pan and deglaze it.
  14. Reduce the wine and add the chicken stock.
  15. Reduce the stock for 5 minutes.
  16. Add the beurre manié to thicken the sauce.
  17. Add the garnish (bacon, mushrooms, and caramelized onions) to the sauce.
  18. Add the chicken pieces back to the sauce and cook for 10 minutes.
  19. Serve the chicken with the sauce, caramelized onions, and parsley.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=5IxG4QkwVTs

graten_ham_sunset_sauce.txt - Gratin of Ham with Sunset Sauce

Objectives

  • Learn a simple, kid-friendly recipe for gratin of ham with sunset sauce.
  • Understand the basics of making a bechamel sauce.
  • Create a flavorful sunset sauce using tomato and cream.

Ingredients

  • Ham
  • Butter
  • Flour
  • Milk (whole)
  • Thyme
  • Bay leaf
  • Onion
  • Clove
  • Salt
  • Chicken stock cubes (organic)
  • Heavy whipping cream
  • Tomato sauce (homemade pasata)
  • Cheese (grated)

Instructions

  1. Make the roux:
  2. Melt butter in a pan over low heat.
  3. Add equal amount of flour and whisk until combined.
  4. Cook on very low heat for 3 minutes.
  5. Remove from heat and let cool completely.
  6. Prepare the flavored milk:
  7. Heat milk in a saucepan over low heat.
  8. Add thyme, bay leaf, onion with clove, and salt.
  9. Bring to a simmer.
  10. Add chicken stock cubes and stir until dissolved.
  11. Remove from heat.
  12. Make the bechamel sauce:
  13. Pour warm milk through a sieve into the cooled roux.
  14. Whisk constantly to combine.
  15. Turn heat on low and bring to a simmer, whisking continuously.
  16. Transform the bechamel into sauce crème:
  17. Add heavy whipping cream to the bechamel sauce and whisk until combined.
  18. Create the sunset sauce:
  19. Gradually add tomato sauce to the sauce crème, whisking constantly, until desired pinkish color is achieved.
  20. Assemble the gratin:
  21. Preheat oven to 200 degrees Celsius (400 degrees Fahrenheit).
  22. Grease a large baking dish with butter.
  23. Spread a thin layer of sauce in the bottom of the dish.
  24. Arrange ham slices in the dish, leaving some space between each slice.
  25. Pour remaining sauce over the ham, ensuring each slice is coated.
  26. Sprinkle grated cheese over the top.
  27. Bake the gratin:
  28. Bake in preheated oven for 15-20 minutes, or until the cheese is melted and bubbly and the ham is slightly crispy.
  29. Serve hot with pasta.

gratin_dauphinois_cheese.txt - Gratin Dauphinois with Cheese

Objectives

  • Learn the difference between Gratin Dauphinois and Gratin Dauphinois with cheese.
  • Master the technique of pre-cooking potatoes in a milk and cream mixture.
  • Create a delicious and comforting French potato gratin with cheese.

Ingredients

  • 1 kilo yellow flesh all-purpose potatoes
  • Full cream milk
  • Heavy cream
  • Pancetta
  • Garlic
  • Salt
  • Pepper
  • Nutmeg
  • Onion
  • Comté cheese
  • Gruyère cheese

Instructions

  1. Cut potatoes into thick slices.
  2. Pour cold milk and cream into a pan.
  3. Add potato slices to the milk and cream mixture immediately after cutting.
  4. Season the milk and cream mixture with salt, pepper, nutmeg, garlic, and onion.
  5. Bring the mixture to a boil over medium heat, stirring occasionally.
  6. Pre-cook the potatoes for 8-15 minutes, depending on thickness.
  7. While the potatoes pre-cook, pan-fry slices of pancetta in a separate pan.
  8. Preheat oven to 180-200 degrees Celsius (350-395 degrees Fahrenheit).
  9. In a baking dish, layer the pre-cooked potatoes, pancetta, and more potatoes.
  10. Pour the milk and cream mixture over the potatoes.
  11. Generously sprinkle Comté and Gruyère cheese over the potatoes.
  12. Bake for 30 minutes, starting at 180 degrees Celsius (350 degrees Fahrenheit) and increasing to 200 degrees Celsius (395 degrees Fahrenheit) for the last 15 minutes.
  13. Let the gratin rest for at least an hour before serving.

gratin_dauphinois.txt - Gratin Dauphinois

Objectives

  • Learn to make a classic French potato side dish, Gratin Dauphinois.
  • Understand the importance of using the right type of potato and proper techniques for slicing and layering.
  • Discover different serving options for this versatile dish.

Ingredients

  • Full cream milk
  • Heavy cream
  • Butter
  • Salt
  • Pepper
  • Nutmeg
  • Garlic
  • Gourmandine potatoes (French variety, yellow flesh, ideal for baking)

Instructions

  1. Wash and peel the potatoes.
  2. Place the potatoes in cold water while preparing the dish.
  3. Rub the inside of the dish with a piece of garlic.
  4. Generously coat the dish with butter.
  5. Slice the potatoes evenly using a food processor with a 4mm blade.
  6. Mix the cream and milk together.
  7. Pour a small amount of the cream mixture at the bottom of the dish.
  8. Start layering the sliced potatoes one by one, overlapping slightly.
  9. Season each layer with salt, pepper, and a pinch of nutmeg.
  10. Add a thin layer of cream mixture on top of each potato layer.
  11. Repeat the layering process until the dish is full.
  12. Ensure the cream mixture is just above the top layer of potatoes.
  13. Preheat oven to 150°C (300°F).
  14. Bake the gratin for 1 hour and 30 minutes.
  15. Allow the gratin to cool slightly before serving.
  16. Serve with a pizza cutter or a sharp knife.
  17. Enjoy the creamy, flavorful layers of the gratin.

greek_style_mushrooms.txt - Champignon à la Grecque (Greek Style Mushrooms)

Objectives

  • Learn to make a classic French side dish called Champignon à la Grecque (Greek Style Mushrooms)
  • Discover a simple yet flavorful way to prepare mushrooms for warmer days
  • Master the technique for infusing mushrooms with aromatic flavors

Ingredients

  • 500g button mushrooms, as white and small as possible
  • 1/2 onion, thinly diced
  • 1/2 lemon, juiced
  • 1/4 cup white wine
  • 1/4 cup olive oil
  • 1 tablespoon tomato paste
  • 1 clove garlic
  • 1 sprig of thyme
  • 1 bay leaf
  • 1/2 teaspoon coriander seeds
  • 1/4 teaspoon black peppercorns
  • Salt to taste

Instructions

  1. Clean the mushrooms by removing any untidy bits.
  2. Quarter the mushrooms if they are too large.
  3. If the mushrooms are not fresh, peel them to remove the skin.
  4. Prepare a small diffuser bag by wrapping a piece of cheesecloth around a clove of garlic, a fragment of bay leaf, coriander seeds, and black peppercorns.
  5. Tie the diffuser bag with a string.
  6. Heat a saucepan over medium heat and add a small amount of olive oil.
  7. Add the diced onions to the pan and cook gently for a few minutes, avoiding any browning.
  8. Add the quartered mushrooms to the pan and toss them with the onions.
  9. Add the lemon juice, white wine, and a pinch of salt to the pan and mix well.
  10. Once the mixture starts to simmer, add the tomato paste and stir to combine.
  11. Bury the diffuser bag under the mushrooms.
  12. Bring the mixture to a gentle boil and cook for 15 minutes, allowing the flavors to infuse.
  13. Turn off the heat and let the mushrooms cool down completely.
  14. To enhance the flavors, drizzle with olive oil and store in a porcelain dish in the refrigerator overnight.
  15. Serve the mushrooms cold or at room temperature on a grazing plate with bread, or alongside grilled meat or fish.

green_beans_two_ways.txt - Green Beans Two Ways

Objectives

  • Learn to prepare green beans in two ways: cold salad and pan-fried.
  • Master the French technique for making a vinaigrette.
  • Discover a simple and versatile side dish for any meal.

Ingredients

  • Green beans
  • Parsley
  • Garlic
  • Shallots
  • Onion
  • Salt
  • Pepper
  • Red wine vinegar
  • Olive oil
  • Butter

Instructions

  1. Trim the ends of the green beans.
  2. Boil water in a pot and add 1 teaspoon of rock salt.
  3. Once the water is boiling, add the green beans and cook for 20 minutes.
  4. Drain the green beans and rinse them under cold water.
  5. For the vinaigrette:
  6. Combine 1 pinch of salt, 1 pinch of pepper, 2 tablespoons of red wine vinegar, 1/2 teaspoon of garlic, and 1 tablespoon of chopped shallots in a jar.
  7. Shake the jar to dissolve the salt and start the aroma.
  8. Add 5 tablespoons of olive oil.
  9. Shake the jar again to mix all ingredients.
  10. For the cold green bean salad:
  11. Cut the cooked green beans in half.
  12. Pour the vinaigrette over the green beans and toss to combine.
  13. Garnish with fresh parsley.
  14. For the pan-fried green beans:
  15. Melt 20 grams of butter in a pan over medium heat.
  16. Add sliced onion and cook until golden brown (about 5 minutes).
  17. Add the cooked green beans to the pan.
  18. Season with salt and pepper.
  19. Turn the heat to high and toss the green beans to coat them in butter and onions.
  20. Remove the green beans from the pan and set aside.
  21. Add 1 tablespoon of vinegar to the pan and heat over high heat to deglaze the pan.
  22. Pour the vinegar over the green beans.
  23. Garnish with fresh parsley.
  24. Serve the cold green bean salad and pan-fried green beans.

ham_and_cheese_croquette.txt - Ham and Cheese Croquette

Objectives

  • Learn to make a classic ham and cheese croquette recipe.
  • Understand how to make a bechamel sauce and flavor it with ham and cheese.
  • Learn the proper breading technique for croquettes.

Ingredients

  • 2 tablespoons of butter
  • 2 tablespoons of flour
  • 1 cup of milk
  • 1 bay leaf
  • 1 sprig of thyme
  • 1/2 onion
  • 1 clove
  • 2 mushrooms, cut into quarters
  • 1/4 teaspoon of salt
  • 1/4 teaspoon of pepper
  • 1/4 cup of cream
  • 1 cup of grated cheese (cottage cheese and cheddar)
  • 1/2 cup of chopped ham
  • 1 cup of flour for breading
  • 2 eggs for breading
  • 1 cup of breadcrumbs for breading
  • Oil for deep frying

Instructions

  1. Melt the butter in a saucepan over medium heat.
  2. Whisk in the flour and cook for 3 minutes, stirring constantly.
  3. Remove from heat and set aside to cool.
  4. Heat the milk in a saucepan over medium heat.
  5. Add the bay leaf, thyme, onion, clove, mushrooms, salt, and pepper to the milk.
  6. Bring the milk to a simmer and cook for 5 minutes.
  7. Remove from heat and strain the milk through a sieve.
  8. Gradually whisk the warm milk into the cooled roux, stirring constantly.
  9. Cook over medium heat, stirring constantly, until the sauce thickens.
  10. Stir in the cream.
  11. Reduce heat to low and stir in the cheese until melted and smooth.
  12. Divide the bechamel sauce in half.
  13. Add the chopped ham to one half of the bechamel sauce and mix well.
  14. Pour each bechamel mixture into separate trays and spread evenly.
  15. Cover with plastic wrap, pressing it onto the surface of the bechamel to prevent a crust from forming.
  16. Refrigerate for at least 15 minutes, or until firm.
  17. Once the bechamel is firm, use a spoon or knife to portion out the desired amount of bechamel.
  18. Shape the bechamel into small, oval-shaped croquettes.
  19. Roll the croquettes in flour.
  20. Dip the croquettes in the beaten eggs.
  21. Roll the croquettes in breadcrumbs, ensuring they are fully coated.
  22. Heat the oil in a deep fryer or saucepan to 350°F (180°C).
  23. Carefully add the croquettes to the hot oil and fry for about 1 minute, or until golden brown.
  24. Remove the croquettes from the oil and drain on paper towels.
  25. Serve the croquettes hot, garnished with deep-fried parsley.

hanger_steak_with_shallot_sauce.txt - Hanger Steak with Shallot Sauce

Objectives

  • Learn to prepare and cook a hanger steak, a lesser-known but delicious cut of beef.
  • Understand the importance of proper meat trimming and separation.
  • Master the technique of creating a flavorful shallot sauce to accompany the steak.

Ingredients

  • 1 hanger steak
  • Salt and pepper
  • 1 tablespoon of oil (sunflower oil recommended)
  • 2-3 tablespoons of butter
  • 1 shallot, thinly sliced
  • 3-4 tablespoons of red wine vinegar
  • Fresh parsley, chopped
  • Salad (optional)

Instructions

  1. Trim the hanger steak, removing any excess skin, fat, and tendons.
  2. Separate the hanger steak into two pieces, one for the steak and one for the shallot sauce.
  3. Preheat the oven to 100 degrees Celsius (90 degrees Celsius is acceptable).
  4. Heat a frying pan over medium heat.
  5. Add 1-2 tablespoons of oil to the pan and wait until it shimmers.
  6. Place the hanger steak in the pan and cook for 2.5 minutes per side, or until a nice coloration appears.
  7. Transfer the steak to a tray, cover with foil, and place in the preheated oven.
  8. Reduce the heat under the frying pan and add the butter.
  9. Once the butter is melted, add the sliced shallots and cook for 3-4 minutes.
  10. Add the red wine vinegar to the pan and let it reduce by half.
  11. Season with salt and add the chopped parsley.
  12. Remove the steak from the oven and add the juices from the tray to the shallot sauce.
  13. Serve the hanger steak on a plate, topped with the shallot sauce and a sprinkle of parsley.
  14. Garnish with a salad if desired.

herb_butter.txt - Herb Butter

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a classic French herb butter, known as "Mètre" butter.
  • Understand the traditional use of herb butter for grilled meats and fish.
  • Master the technique of softening butter and incorporating ingredients for a smooth, spreadable consistency.

Ingredients

  • 1 stick of high-quality butter (unsalted)
  • 1/4 cup fresh parsley, finely chopped
  • 1/2 teaspoon salt
  • 1/4 teaspoon black pepper
  • 1/4 lemon, juiced

Instructions

  1. Cut the butter into small pieces and place in a clean container.
  2. Allow the butter to soften at room temperature until it's easily spreadable.
  3. While the butter softens, chop the parsley finely.
  4. Combine the salt, pepper, and lemon juice in a small bowl.
  5. Once the butter is soft, transfer it to a mixing bowl.
  6. Add the chopped parsley, salt, pepper, and lemon juice to the butter.
  7. Gently mix the ingredients together using a spatula or a spoon until the butter is evenly blended and has a creamy, paste-like consistency.
  8. If needed, add more parsley to achieve a desired ratio of green to yellow.
  9. Transfer the herb butter mixture to a piping bag.
  10. Pipe the herb butter into small, decorative puffs on a plate or serving dish.
  11. Refrigerate the herb butter until ready to serve.

hollandaise_sauce.txt - Hollandaise Sauce

Objectives

  • Learn to make a traditional Hollandaise sauce.
  • Master the technique of emulsifying egg yolks and butter.
  • Understand the importance of temperature control for a smooth, creamy sauce.

Ingredients

  • 2 egg yolks
  • 1 tablespoon cold water
  • 1/4 teaspoon salt
  • 1 tablespoon lemon juice
  • 1/2 cup clarified butter

Instructions

  1. Set the stovetop to the lowest heat setting.
  2. Place a saucepan on the stove.
  3. Add two egg yolks and one tablespoon of cold water to the saucepan.
  4. Whisk the egg yolks and water together.
  5. Continuously whisk the mixture while monitoring the temperature.
  6. Ensure the temperature remains below 60 degrees Celsius.
  7. Use your hand to check the temperature of the saucepan.
  8. If the saucepan is too hot, remove it from the heat and continue whisking until it cools down.
  9. Continue whisking until the mixture becomes thick and creamy.
  10. Add a pinch of salt and a tablespoon of lemon juice.
  11. Slowly drizzle in the clarified butter, whisking continuously.
  12. Continue adding butter until the sauce reaches desired consistency.
  13. Remove the saucepan from the heat.
  14. Serve the hollandaise sauce immediately over poached eggs, asparagus, or smoked salmon.
  15. Garnish with chives and cayenne pepper for added flavor.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_a4sio7ix-w

home_style_demi_glace.txt - Home-Style Demi-Glace

Objectives

  • Learn to make a flavorful demi-glace from store-bought stock.
  • Understand the difference between pan sauces and classic sauces.
  • Discover a quick and easy way to elevate your cooking with a homemade sauce base.

Ingredients

  • 500 ml store-bought stock (veal, beef, chicken or lamb)
  • 1 tablespoon onion, chopped
  • 1 tablespoon carrot, chopped
  • 1 bay leaf
  • 1 sprig of thyme
  • 1 teaspoon tomato paste
  • 1 tablespoon toasted flour
  • Peppercorns
  • 50 ml white wine (optional)
  • Chicken carcass and wings, chopped

Instructions

  1. Heat a pan over medium-high heat.
  2. Add the chopped chicken carcass and wings to the pan and sear for 10-12 minutes until well-browned.
  3. Remove the chicken pieces and set aside.
  4. Add the chopped onion and carrot to the pan and cook for a minute or two to absorb the leftover oil.
  5. Stir in the tomato paste and cook until the acidity is removed.
  6. Deglaze the pan with the white wine (optional).
  7. Reduce the wine until there are just a few teaspoons left.
  8. Return the chicken pieces to the pan.
  9. Stir in the toasted flour.
  10. Add the store-bought stock, peppercorns, thyme, bay leaf, and a pinch of salt.
  11. Bring the mixture to a simmer and reduce by half.
  12. Simmer for 20 minutes, or until the desired consistency is reached.
  13. Strain the demi-glace through a fine-mesh sieve.
  14. Serve immediately or store in the fridge for up to 3 days or freeze for up to 3 months.

hula_confit.txt - Roulade Confit

Objectives

  • Learn to make a simple and quick French dessert called Roulade Confit
  • Understand the steps involved in separating eggs, making meringue, and baking a sponge cake
  • Learn how to assemble and roll the Roulade Confit with jam

Ingredients

  • 80g white sugar
  • 40g corn starch
  • 2 eggs
  • 1 dash of salt
  • Raspberry jam
  • Icing sugar

Instructions

  1. Separate the egg yolks from the egg whites.
  2. Add 80 grams of white sugar to the egg yolks and mix until they become pale and watery.
  3. Add 40 grams of corn starch to the egg yolks and mix well.
  4. Whisk the egg whites with a pinch of salt until they form stiff peaks.
  5. Gradually fold the meringue into the egg yolk mixture, starting with a small amount and mixing well before adding the rest.
  6. Pour the mixture onto a baking tray and spread it evenly to create a flat layer.
  7. Bake in a preheated oven at 215-220 degrees Celsius for 10 minutes.
  8. While the sponge cake is baking, prepare a sheet of baking paper by sprinkling it with flour.
  9. Once the sponge cake is cooked, immediately invert it onto the floured baking paper to prevent sticking.
  10. Carefully peel off the baking paper from the bottom of the sponge cake while it's still warm.
  11. Spread a layer of raspberry jam evenly over the warm sponge cake.
  12. Immediately roll the sponge cake up with the jam inside to form a log shape.
  13. Transfer the rolled Roulade Confit to a serving tray and dust it with icing sugar.
  14. Allow the Roulade Confit to cool completely before slicing and serving.

instant_salted_chicken.txt - Poulet Sauté à la Minute

Objectives

  • Learn to make a simple, flavorful French chicken recipe.
  • Understand the importance of pan-frying chicken for optimal flavor.
  • Discover how to create a quick and delicious sauce using pan juices.

Ingredients

  • 1 tablespoon olive oil
  • 1 tablespoon butter
  • Chicken pieces (pre-seasoned with salt)
  • 1 tablespoon shallots, diced
  • 50 ml white wine
  • 1/2 lemon, juiced
  • Fresh parsley, chopped
  • Salt and pepper to taste
  • Optional: Thyme sprigs

Instructions

  1. Heat a cast iron pan over medium to medium-high heat.
  2. Add olive oil and butter to the pan, allowing the butter to melt.
  3. Place the pre-seasoned chicken pieces in the pan.
  4. Cook the chicken for 10-12 minutes on the first side, or until well-browned.
  5. Flip the chicken and continue cooking until the internal temperature reaches 165°F (74°C), about 23 minutes total.
  6. Transfer the cooked chicken to a tray and cover with foil.
  7. Add diced shallots to the pan and cook over medium-high heat until softened.
  8. Deglaze the pan with white wine, scraping up any browned bits from the bottom.
  9. Add lemon juice and stir to combine.
  10. Pour the sauce over the chicken, sprinkle with chopped parsley, and serve.

japanese_knife_tips.txt - Japanese Knife Tips

Objectives

  • Learn how to use a Japanese chef's knife correctly
  • Understand the importance of slicing and chopping techniques
  • Avoid common mistakes made by beginners

Instructions

  1. Use a continuous slicing motion instead of a rocking motion.
  2. Move the knife in a single direction, either forward or backward.
  3. Avoid chopping with a Japanese knife, as the thin blade can get caught on the chopping board.
  4. Practice slicing and chopping techniques until you feel comfortable and confident.
  5. Research your specific type of Japanese knife online for additional tips and techniques.

Objectives

  • Understand the importance of knife maintenance.
  • Learn the differences between carbon steel and stainless steel knife maintenance.
  • Recognize the trade-off between maintenance time and sharpness.

Instructions

  1. After using a carbon steel knife, clean it with soap and water.
  2. Dry the knife thoroughly.
  3. Oil the knife to prevent rust.
  4. Stainless steel knives do not require oiling.
  5. Wash and dry stainless steel knives after use.
  6. Store all knives safely.

knives_french_cooking.txt - Knives for French Cooking

Objectives

  • Learn about essential knives for French cooking
  • Understand the importance of choosing the right knives
  • Discover ergonomic considerations for knife handles

Instructions

  1. Choose a paring knife: This is the most versatile knife and is essential for everyday tasks.
  2. Invest in a boning knife: This sturdy knife is useful for cutting around bones and chicken carcasses.
  3. Get a chef's knife: A chef's knife is the most important knife for all-around cooking, making it a crucial addition to your kitchen.
  4. Consider a bread knife: While not essential, a bread knife can be a helpful addition for cutting through tough items like tomatoes and cauliflower.
  5. Avoid buying a full set of knives: When starting out, focus on getting the essential knives and avoid buying a full set that might contain unnecessary tools.
  6. Choose a mid-range brand: Opt for a good quality brand that offers decent knives without breaking the bank.
  7. Prioritize ergonomics: Look for knives with comfortable handles that fit your hand well, as you will be using them frequently.
  8. Avoid thin handles: Thin handles can be uncomfortable and difficult to grip, even on expensive knives.
  9. Test the knife before purchasing: Try holding the knife in your hand to assess its balance, weight, and feel.
  10. Consider the brand's reputation: Ensure the brand is known for quality and durability to ensure your knives stay sharp and last a long time.

korean_vegetable_prep.txt - Korean Vegetable Preparation

Objectives

  • Learn basic Korean vegetable preparation terms and techniques.
  • Understand the importance of proper peeling and washing techniques.
  • Discover a practical workstation setup for vegetable preparation at home.

Ingredients

  • Onions
  • Cauliflower
  • Carrots
  • Potatoes
  • Peas
  • Green beans
  • Parsley
  • Tomatoes

Instructions

  1. Apprécier: Remove external leaves from vegetables like onions and cauliflower.
  2. Épépiner: Peel vegetables using a peeler, holding the vegetable firmly with your hand and using your thumb as a guide.
  3. Écosser: Remove the outer shell of peas by opening them gently.
  4. Fileter: Remove strings from green beans by breaking off the end and pulling the string.
  5. Équeuter: Remove the stems and florets of parsley by hand.
  6. Monda: Remove the skins of tomatoes by making a small cross at the top, removing the peduncle, and plunging the tomato in boiling water for 10-15 seconds.
  7. After boiling, plunge the tomato in cold water to facilitate skin removal.
  8. Wash salad: Clean your sink and fill it with a small amount of water.
  9. Add vinegar to the water and submerge the salad for 5 minutes.
  10. Remove the salad and spin dry in a salad spinner.
  11. Wash garden salad: Rinse the salad twice to remove any dirt or debris.

lady_fingers_biscuit.txt - Ladyfingers Biscuit

Objectives

  • Learn to make ladyfingers, a key ingredient for classic French desserts.
  • Master the technique of incorporating egg whites and flour for a light and airy texture.
  • Explore the versatility of ladyfingers in various desserts, including souffles, charlottes, and tiramisus.

Ingredients

  • 4 eggs (separated)
  • 100g white sugar
  • 100g confectionary sugar
  • 100g flour

Instructions

  1. Separate the egg whites from the yolks.
  2. Place the egg whites in a bowl at room temperature and add a small amount of sugar.
  3. Beat the egg whites on low speed until foamy.
  4. Gradually increase the speed and add more sugar as the mixture starts to foam.
  5. Beat the egg whites until stiff and shiny, forming peaks.
  6. Beat the egg yolks separately until they resemble an omelet.
  7. Add the beaten egg yolks to the meringue on low speed for 10 seconds.
  8. Fold the remaining egg yolk mixture into the meringue by hand.
  9. Sift a quarter or half of the flour into the mixture and fold it in gently.
  10. Repeat the process with the remaining flour, folding it into the mixture until it is fully incorporated.
  11. Transfer the mixture into a piping bag.
  12. Line a baking sheet with parchment paper.
  13. Pipe the mixture onto the parchment paper, forming 10-centimeter-long fingers.
  14. Sprinkle confectionary sugar generously over the ladyfingers.
  15. Preheat the oven to 180°C (355°F).
  16. Bake the ladyfingers for 12-15 minutes, until lightly golden brown.
  17. Place the ladyfingers on a cooling rack to prevent them from becoming soggy.
  18. Store the ladyfingers in an airtight container lined with parchment paper for up to two weeks.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=H_qUF4YLqbA

lamb_braised_7_hours.txt - 7 Hour Braised Lamb

Objectives

  • Learn how to braise a leg of lamb for a melt-in-your-mouth texture
  • Understand the importance of searing meat before braising
  • Master the art of making a delicious lamb sauce

Ingredients

  • 1/2 leg of lamb
  • 1 tablespoon of oil
  • 1/2 liter chicken stock
  • 1/2 cup Madeira wine
  • 1/4 cup orange juice
  • 1 large onion, roughly chopped
  • 2 carrots, roughly chopped
  • 2 shallots, roughly chopped
  • 4 cloves garlic, unpeeled
  • 1 sprig rosemary
  • 1 sprig thyme
  • Salt and pepper to taste
  • Maple syrup (optional)

Instructions

  1. Season the lamb with salt and pepper.
  2. Sear the lamb on all sides in a large pot over medium-high heat.
  3. Remove the lamb from the pot and set aside.
  4. Add the onion, carrots, shallots, and garlic to the pot and cook until softened, about 5 minutes.
  5. Add the Madeira wine and orange juice to the pot and bring to a simmer.
  6. Add the chicken stock, rosemary, and thyme to the pot.
  7. Return the lamb to the pot.
  8. Preheat the oven to 120 degrees Celsius (248 degrees Fahrenheit).
  9. Cover the pot with parchment paper and a lid.
  10. Place the pot in the oven and braise for 5-7 hours, checking every 2-3 hours to ensure there is enough liquid.
  11. Once the lamb is cooked, remove it from the pot and shred with a fork.
  12. Strain the braising liquid into a saucepan.
  13. Reduce the braising liquid over medium heat until thickened.
  14. Optional: glaze the lamb with a mixture of maple syrup and orange juice.
  15. Serve the shredded lamb with the reduced braising sauce and mashed potatoes.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=EXZ-sNnjreE

lamb_cutlets_hazelnut_coating.txt - Crammed Lamb Cutlets with Hazelnut Coating and Sauce

Objectives

  • Create a flavorful, gourmet lamb dish with a hazelnut coating and sauce.
  • Learn to make a lamb jus using simple ingredients.
  • Perfect the technique for pan-frying lamb cutlets.

Ingredients

  • Lamb cutlets (with bone)
  • Hazelnut (skin removed)
  • Flour
  • Eggs
  • Breadcrumbs
  • Butter
  • Salt and pepper
  • Carrots
  • Onion
  • Shallot
  • Thyme
  • Bay leaf
  • Rosemary
  • Water
  • Cream
  • Fennel (roasted)
  • Cherry tomatoes (roasted)

Instructions

  1. Clean the lamb cutlets, removing any excess fat or trimmings.
  2. Preheat oven to 180°C and roast the hazelnuts for 10 minutes until the skin cracks.
  3. Rub the hazelnuts with a tea towel to remove the skin.
  4. Chop the hazelnuts finely using a food processor or the back of a spoon.
  5. In a pan, brown the lamb trimmings over high heat without any added fat.
  6. Add the carrots, onion, shallots, thyme, bay leaf, and rosemary to the pan and sweat for 2-3 minutes.
  7. Deglaze the pan with water, scraping up any browned bits.
  8. Bring the mixture to a boil, then reduce the heat and simmer for 15-20 minutes, adding water as needed.
  9. Reduce the cream in a separate pan.
  10. Pour the concentrated lamb jus into the reduced cream, add roasted hazelnuts, and continue to reduce until thickened.
  11. Season the lamb cutlets with salt and pepper.
  12. Dredge the cutlets in flour, then dip in egg, and finally coat in a mixture of breadcrumbs and chopped hazelnuts.
  13. Heat butter in a pan over medium heat.
  14. Pan-fry the cutlets for 5 minutes on each side until cooked through.
  15. Plate the lamb cutlets with roasted fennel, cherry tomatoes, and a drizzle of the hazelnut sauce.
  16. Garnish with fresh rosemary.
