pom_bania.txt - Pom Bania (Wet Bread)

Objectives

  • Learn how to make the classic Provençal sandwich, Pom Bania.
  • Understand the importance of fresh ingredients and a flavorful dressing.
  • Discover the authentic recipe and regional traditions of the sandwich.

Ingredients

  • 1 loaf of fresh, soft bread
  • 1 pinch of salt
  • 3-4 anchovy fillets, thinly chopped
  • 1 tablespoon red wine vinegar
  • 3-4 tablespoons olive oil
  • 2-3 slices of tomato
  • 1/2 onion, thinly sliced
  • 1/4 red bell pepper, thinly sliced
  • 2-3 hard-boiled eggs, sliced
  • 1 chiffonade of celery leaves
  • Black olives, to taste
  • Extra virgin olive oil, for drizzling

Instructions

  1. Prepare the dressing:
  2. Combine the salt, anchovy fillets, and red wine vinegar in a jar.
  3. Stir well to dissolve the salt and anchovies.
  4. Add the olive oil and shake the jar vigorously until the dressing is emulsified.
  5. Prepare the bread:
  6. Cut the bread in half lengthwise.
  7. Pour the dressing over each half of the bread, ensuring it is thoroughly soaked.
  8. Assemble the sandwich:
  9. Layer the ingredients on the bread in the following order:
    • Tomatoes
    • Onions
    • Red bell pepper
    • Hard-boiled eggs
    • Celery leaves
    • Black olives
  10. Drizzle with extra virgin olive oil.
  11. Close the sandwich:
  12. Place the top half of the bread on top of the ingredients.
  13. Gently press down on the sandwich to ensure the dressing is evenly distributed and all the ingredients are well-combined.
  14. Enjoy your Pom Bania!

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=9dz9Q-LRj-Y

pommes_de_terre_a_la_lardonne.txt - Pommes de terre à la lardonne

Objectives

  • Learn to make a simple and delicious French potato dish with bacon and onion.
  • Understand how to create a flavorful stock using chicken wings or stock cubes.
  • Master the technique of braising potatoes in the oven for a tender and flavorful result.

Ingredients

  • 1 kg waxy potatoes, peeled and cubed
  • 200g smoked bacon, cut into chunks
  • 1 onion, chopped
  • 2 chicken wings (optional)
  • 2 cups water
  • 1 sprig of thyme
  • 1 bay leaf
  • 1/2 vegetable stock cube (optional)
  • 2 tablespoons oil
  • Salt and pepper to taste
  • Parsley for garnish

Instructions

  1. Preheat oven to 200°C (390°F).
  2. Make the stock:
  3. Heat 2 tablespoons of oil in a pan over medium heat.
  4. Add the chicken wings and cook until lightly browned on all sides.
  5. Pour in 2 cups of water and bring to a boil.
  6. Add the thyme, bay leaf, and 1/2 vegetable stock cube (optional).
  7. Reduce heat to low and simmer for 25 minutes.
  8. If you don't have chicken wings:
  9. Boil 2 cups of water.
  10. Add the bacon and simmer for 10 minutes.
  11. Strain the bacon water and use it as your stock.
  12. Prepare the bacon and onions:
  13. Heat a cast iron pot over medium heat.
  14. Add a small amount of oil and lightly brown the bacon.
  15. Add the chopped onion and cook until softened.
  16. Add the potatoes:
  17. Drain the potatoes and dry them with a clean towel.
  18. Add the potatoes to the pot with the bacon and onion.
  19. Stir gently to combine.
  20. Add the stock and seasonings:
  21. Pour in the chicken broth or bacon water (about 1 cup).
  22. Add thyme, bay leaf, and pepper.
  23. Stir gently.
  24. Cook in the oven:
  25. Cover the pot with a lid.
  26. Bake in the preheated oven for 20-25 minutes, or until the potatoes are tender.
  27. Optional: Brown the potatoes:
  28. Remove the lid and turn on the oven grill.
  29. Bake for a few more minutes to brown the potatoes and concentrate the flavors.
  30. Serve:
  31. Transfer the potatoes to a serving dish.
  32. Sprinkle with parsley and serve immediately.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=by11pQrtprQ

pomodo_duchess_potato.txt - Pomodo (Duchess Potatoes with Cheese)

Objectives

  • Learn to make a classic Pomodo, a Duchess potato variation with cheese.
  • Master the technique for creating potato rosettes, nests, and croquettes.
  • Discover versatile side dish options for a festive Christmas meal.

Ingredients

  • 4 starchy potatoes (e.g., floury, waxy)
  • 4 egg yolks
  • Good quality butter
  • Gruyere cheese (or Comte, cheddar if unavailable)
  • Salt
  • Pepper
  • Grated nutmeg
  • Flour
  • Breadcrumbs
  • 1 egg

Instructions

  1. Peel and cut potatoes into halves.
  2. Place potatoes in a pot with cold water and 2 tablespoons of coarse salt.
  3. Bring to a boil and cook for 10-15 minutes until tender but not mushy.
  4. Drain potatoes for 3-4 minutes.
  5. Transfer potatoes to a baking tray and bake at 200 degrees Celsius for 3 minutes.
  6. While potatoes are baking, heat a vegetable mill over medium heat.
  7. Once potatoes are baked, pass them through the vegetable mill.
  8. Continue heating the potatoes in the mill for 4-5 minutes, stirring gently to remove excess moisture.
  9. Season potatoes with salt, pepper, and nutmeg.
  10. Add 30 grams of butter to the potatoes and mix until melted.
  11. Add 70 grams of cheese and melt.
  12. Turn off heat and add egg yolks one tablespoon at a time, mixing well after each addition.
  13. Add a little more salt, pepper, and butter if needed.
  14. Transfer the mixture to a shallow tray, cover with plastic wrap, and cool until lukewarm.
  15. Fill a piping bag with the cooled potato mixture.
  16. To make rosettes, pipe the mixture onto a baking sheet in a spiral shape.
  17. To make nests, pipe two circles of mixture, one on top of the other, and create an opening in the center using a knife.
  18. Bake rosettes and nests at 200 degrees Celsius for 15 minutes until golden brown.
  19. For potato croquettes, transfer the remaining potato mixture to the freezer to chill.
  20. Once chilled, roll the potato mixture into balls and coat in flour, egg, and breadcrumbs.
  21. Deep fry the croquettes in oil at 180 degrees Celsius for 3-4 minutes until golden brown.
  22. Serve the Pomodo rosettes, nests, and croquettes as side dishes for your Christmas meal.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=QYIPGqB5Ph0

pom_saute.txt - Pomme Sautée

Objectives

  • Learn how to sautée potatoes without pre-cooking
  • Discover the benefits of using a carbon steel sauté pan
  • Master the technique of Pomme Sautée, a southwest French potato dish

Ingredients

  • Duck fat (1-2 tablespoons)
  • Waxy potatoes (about 1 pound)
  • 1 onion, sliced
  • 1/2 cup diced Serrano ham
  • 1/4 cup sliced mushrooms (optional)
  • 1/4 cup chopped parsley
  • 1 clove garlic, pressed
  • Salt
  • Black pepper
  • Olive oil

Instructions

  1. Dry the potatoes thoroughly. They should be completely dry before adding to the pan.
  2. Heat a carbon steel sauté pan over high heat.
  3. Add 1-2 tablespoons of duck fat to the pan and let it melt.
  4. Swirl the fat to coat the entire pan.
  5. Add the potatoes to the hot pan and toss them around frequently.
  6. Sauté the potatoes for 10-12 minutes, or until they start to brown.
  7. Add the sliced onion, diced Serrano ham, and optional mushrooms to the pan.
  8. Continue to sauté for 1-2 minutes, tossing frequently.
  9. Add a pinch of black pepper.
  10. Reduce the heat to medium-low, cover the pan, and cook for 20 minutes, tossing occasionally.
  11. After 20 minutes, check if the potatoes are cooked through by inserting a knife. They should be soft and melt effortlessly.
  12. Turn off the heat and set aside.
  13. When ready to serve, heat the potatoes over medium-high heat.
  14. Add the chopped parsley and pressed garlic to the pan.
  15. Toss and sauté briefly until fragrant.
  16. Serve immediately.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=YZzFmB1acyE

pookuc_chicken_vinegar_sauce.txt - Pooku Style Chicken and Vinegar Sauce

Objectives

  • Learn to cook chicken in the Pooku style, using a slow, low-temperature approach.
  • Understand the importance of high-quality ingredients and the use of a copper sauté pan.
  • Master the technique of creating a thick, tangy vinegar sauce using butter, shallots, and red wine vinegar.

Ingredients

  • 1 chicken breast (or whole chicken)
  • 250 ml red wine vinegar (aged in oak barrel)
  • 1 shallot
  • 1 bay leaf
  • 2 sprigs of thyme
  • 250g unsalted butter
  • Salt and pepper to taste

Instructions

  1. Preheat oven to 200°C (400°F).
  2. Melt butter in a copper sauté pan over medium heat.
  3. Place the chicken breast in the pan and lightly color on all sides for 5 minutes, turning every 2-3 minutes.
  4. Add the thyme and bay leaf to the pan.
  5. Transfer the pan to the oven, cover with a lid, and cook for 20 minutes.
  6. While the chicken is cooking, prepare the sauce ingredients: shallots, butter, and red wine vinegar.
  7. Remove the chicken from the oven and reserve in a tray lined with foil. Cover with a bit of the cooking juices and keep warm in the oven.
  8. Turn the heat to high and bring the pan with the cooking juices to a boil.
  9. Reduce the heat to medium and simmer until the liquid has reduced by half.
  10. Remove the pan from the heat and add the shallots. Cook gently for 5 minutes, or until softened.
  11. Pour the red wine vinegar into the pan and bring to a boil over high heat.
  12. Reduce the vinegar by half.
  13. Turn off the heat.
  14. Add the butter in pieces, stirring until melted and incorporated.
  15. Season the sauce with salt and pepper to taste.
  16. Pour the sauce over the chicken and serve.
  17. For a milder flavor, you can add a bit of the chicken cooking juices to the sauce.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=t9uMuS22Qv0

poor_parisian_pork_cutlet.txt - Poor Parisian Pork Cutlet

Objectives

  • Learn to make a simple, pantry-friendly French pork cutlet recipe.
  • Understand the importance of proper onion cooking and heat control.
  • Create a flavorful sauce using cream, onion, garlic, and mushrooms.

Ingredients

  • 1 pork cutlet (or chicken breast)
  • 1 onion, thinly sliced
  • 1 clove garlic, minced
  • 1/2 cup mushrooms, sliced
  • 3-4 tablespoons creme fraiche (or heavy cream)
  • Salt and pepper to taste
  • Fresh parsley, for garnish

Instructions

  1. Thinly slice the onion and cook over medium heat for 4-5 minutes until softened.
  2. Season the pork cutlet with salt and pepper.
  3. Add the pork cutlet to the pan and cook for 2-3 minutes per side, browning it slightly.
  4. Add the garlic and mushrooms to the pan and cook for a few minutes until softened.
  5. Add the creme fraiche to the pan and stir to combine.
  6. Simmer the sauce for a few minutes until it thickens.
  7. Season the sauce with salt and pepper to taste.
  8. Garnish with fresh parsley and serve immediately.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=SKihmJJeLy8

pork_chops_caramelized_onions.txt - Pork Chops with Caramelized Onions

Objectives

  • Cook pork chops with a caramelized onion topping
  • Utilize a French technique for caramelizing onions
  • Create a moist, flavorful pork chop dish

Ingredients

  • 4 pork loin chops or cutlets
  • 8 onions, chopped
  • 1 tablespoon butter
  • 1-2 tablespoons grapeseed oil (or other oil with high smoking point)
  • Salt and pepper
  • Fresh sage, chopped
  • Garlic cloves, minced
  • Fresh thyme (optional)

Instructions

  1. Season the pork chops with salt and pepper.
  2. Heat a large non-stick pan over medium-high heat.
  3. Add butter and grapeseed oil to the pan.
  4. Sear the pork chops on each side for 5 minutes, or until well browned.
  5. Transfer the pork chops to a roasting pan.
  6. Add the chopped onions to the pan with the remaining butter and oil.
  7. Cook the onions over high heat for 15-20 minutes, stirring occasionally, until caramelized.
  8. Season the onions with salt and pepper.
  9. Cover the pork chops with the caramelized onions.
  10. Add a half clove of minced garlic to each chop.
  11. Sprinkle chopped fresh sage over the onions.
  12. Add a pat of butter to each chop.
  13. Sprinkle thyme on top of the chops (optional).
  14. Preheat oven to 170°C (340°F) or 180°C (355°F) for a fan-forced oven.
  15. Cover the roasting pan with baking paper or aluminum foil to prevent dryness.
  16. Bake for 30 minutes.
  17. Remove from oven and serve.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=OYYhfOXhbRs

pork_chop_with_cheese.txt - Pork Chop with Gruyere Cheese

Objectives

  • Learn how to prepare a classic French dish called "côte de porc au Gruyère"
  • Discover the importance of using the right type of cheese for this recipe
  • Explore various cooking techniques for pork chops, including grilling and broiling

Ingredients

  • 1 thick pork chop
  • Salt
  • Thick cream
  • Gruyere cheese
  • Mustard
  • Grapeseed oil

Instructions

  1. Remove the pork chop from the refrigerator 10-15 minutes before cooking to avoid cold spots.
  2. Discard the pork rind if present.
  3. Season the pork chop with salt on both sides.
  4. Heat a cast iron grill pan over medium-high heat.
  5. Brush the pork chop with grapeseed oil on all sides.
  6. Grill the pork chop for 10-12 minutes, ensuring a nice coloring on all sides.
  7. Check the internal temperature of the pork chop with a food thermometer, aiming for 65°C.
  8. While the pork chop is grilling, prepare the mixture by combining thick cream, mustard, and Gruyere cheese in a bowl.
  9. Mix the ingredients well to create a thick, spreadable consistency.
  10. Coat one side of the cooked pork chop with the cheesy mustard mixture.
  11. Transfer the pork chop to a baking dish.
  12. Add a bit of black pepper and additional Gruyere cheese on top of the mixture.
  13. Broil the pork chop for 5 minutes, placing the dish one notch down from the highest setting to prevent burning.
  14. Serve immediately.

pork_medallion_mushroom_port_sauce.txt - Pork Medallion with Mushroom and Port Sauce

Objectives

  • Learn to cook pork medallions with a creamy mushroom and Port sauce.
  • Master the technique of pan-frying mushrooms and reducing cream.
  • Create a flavorful sauce using deglazing and stock.

Ingredients

  • Pork Fillet
  • Flour
  • Butter
  • Mushrooms
  • Salt and Pepper
  • Port Wine
  • Pure Cream
  • Chicken Stock

Instructions

  1. Slice mushrooms thinly, about half a millimeter thick.
  2. Heat butter in a pan over medium-high heat.
  3. Add sliced mushrooms and pan-fry until they release water and become golden brown.
  4. Reduce heat and continue cooking until the water evaporates and mushrooms are nicely colored.
  5. Remove mushrooms from the pan and set aside.
  6. Cut pork fillet into 2-inch (5 cm) medallions.
  7. Season pork medallions with salt and pepper.
  8. Dredge each medallion in flour, tapping off excess.
  9. Heat butter and oil in a pan over medium-high heat.
  10. Sear pork medallions for 3 minutes on each side, ensuring they develop a nice brown crust.
  11. While pork medallions cook, heat cream in a separate pan over medium heat and reduce by a quarter.
  12. Warm chicken stock in a small pan over low heat.
  13. After searing, transfer pork medallions to a preheated oven at 150°C (250°F) for 1 minute on each side to ensure they are cooked through.
  14. Deglaze the pan where the medallions were seared with Port wine.
  15. Add a portion of the reduced cream to the pan and stir to incorporate.
  16. Add the remaining cream and gently cook, reducing the sauce slightly.
  17. Add warmed chicken stock to the sauce and reduce until it reaches the desired consistency.
  18. Season the sauce with salt and pepper to taste.
  19. Strain the sauce through a fine-mesh sieve to remove any impurities.
  20. Add the reserved mushrooms to the sauce and let them infuse.
  21. To plate, arrange cooked pork medallions on a plate with yellow rice on the side.
  22. Pour the mushroom and Port sauce over the medallions.
  23. Serve and enjoy!

pork_rillette_in_veloute_sauce.txt - Pork Rillette in Veloute Sauce

Objectives

  • Learn how to poach meat and create a veloute sauce.
  • Master the technique of making pork rillette.
  • Prepare a flavorful and elegant dish with pork, mushrooms, and carrots.

Ingredients

  • 1 tablespoon of butter
  • 1 tablespoon of oil
  • 2 cloves of garlic
  • 100g pancetta, diced
  • 500g pork, diced
  • 1 tablespoon of plain flour
  • 100ml dry white wine
  • 500ml veal stock (optional, can use water)
  • 1 carrot, diced
  • 1 small onion, studded with cloves
  • 1 stock cube
  • 1 bouquet garni
  • 200g mushrooms, sliced
  • 10g butter
  • 10g plain flour (for thickening)
  • 100ml cream
  • 1/2 lemon, juiced
  • 1 tablespoon capers

Instructions

  1. Heat butter and oil in a pot over medium heat.
  2. Add garlic and pancetta, cook until softened.
  3. Add diced pork, season with salt and pepper.
  4. Cook for a few minutes, until the pork is slightly browned.
  5. Add flour to the pot and stir to coat the meat.
  6. Cook the flour for 2 minutes.
  7. Slowly add cold white wine and stock (or water).
  8. Add carrot, onion, stock cube, and bouquet garni to the pot.
  9. Bring to a boil, then reduce heat and simmer for 1.5 hours.
  10. Remove the meat from the pot and set aside.
  11. Discard the bouquet garni.
  12. Increase heat to medium and bring the sauce to a boil.
  13. Add sliced mushrooms to the sauce and simmer for 5-10 minutes until cooked.
  14. If the sauce is too thin, thicken it by adding a mixture of butter and flour (10g each) to the boiling sauce.
  15. Stir until the sauce thickens.
  16. Add cream and lemon juice to the sauce and whisk until smooth.
  17. Return the cooked pork to the sauce and heat through.
  18. Stir in capers.
  19. Serve the pork rillette in veloute sauce with rice or potatoes.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=vgc9XatBhgY

  • Welcome back to the channel after a 10-month hiatus.
  • Provide an update on the channel's future, including the resumption of regular recipes.
  • Announce a live Q&A session on Saturday to address viewer questions.

Instructions

  1. Preheat oven to 350 degrees F (175 degrees C).
  2. Season the pork shoulder with salt, pepper, and any other desired spices.
  3. Place the pork shoulder in a large Dutch oven or oven-safe pot.
  4. Pour in the milk, ensuring it covers the pork shoulder.
  5. Add any additional ingredients you desire, such as onions, garlic, or herbs.
  6. Cover the pot tightly with a lid and place in the preheated oven.
  7. Braise the pork shoulder for 3-4 hours, or until it is tender and easily pulls apart.

pork_shoulder_in_milk.txt - Pork Shoulder in Milk

Objectives

  • Learn how to braise a pork shoulder in milk and cream for a tender and flavorful result.
  • Understand the importance of gently browning the meat before braising.
  • Discover how to make a bread sauce to accompany the roast pork.

Ingredients

  • 1 pork shoulder (approx. 2-3 lbs)
  • 1 tablespoon grapeseed oil
  • 1 knob of butter
  • 1 teaspoon black peppercorns
  • 2 bay leaves
  • 4 cloves garlic
  • 300 ml heavy whipping cream
  • 700 ml milk
  • Freshly grated nutmeg
  • 50 grams white bread, fresh
  • Parsley stalks

Instructions

  1. Season the pork shoulder with salt and pepper.
  2. Heat the grapeseed oil and butter in a cast iron pot over medium heat.
  3. Add the pork shoulder to the pot and cook for 3-4 minutes on each side, until lightly browned.
  4. Add the garlic, bay leaves, and peppercorns to the pot.
  5. Pour in the heavy whipping cream and let it simmer for a few minutes, stirring to deglaze the bottom of the pot.
  6. Add the milk and bring to a simmer.
  7. Sprinkle the pork with freshly grated nutmeg and mix it into the sauce.
  8. Preheat the oven to 320 degrees Fahrenheit (160 degrees Celsius).
  9. Cover the pot with a lid and place it in the oven.
  10. Cook for 1.5 hours, turning the roast every 30 minutes.
  11. Remove the roast from the oven and let it rest while you make the sauce.
  12. To make the sauce:
    • Strain the braising liquid through a sieve, discarding the garlic and bay leaves.
    • Press the garlic cloves through the sieve to extract their juices.
    • Add the white bread to the sauce and let it soak for a few minutes.
    • Use a stick blender to blend the sauce until smooth.
    • Strain the sauce again through a sieve to remove any remaining bread pieces.
    • Adjust the seasoning with salt and pepper to taste.
  13. Serve the roast pork with the bread sauce and roasted potatoes.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_ZBgiEmDanI

portion_size_and_tools.txt - Portion Size and Tools

Objectives

  • Understand the importance of portion size in French cooking.
  • Learn about essential cookware and tools for French cuisine.
  • Explore different types of knives and their specific uses.

Instructions

  1. Portion size is crucial for health, diet regulation, budgeting, and avoiding food waste.
  2. For fish, aim for 200-300 grams per person.
  3. For trout, serve one piece per person.
  4. For mixed salads, use 200 grams of ingredients per person.
  5. When combining ingredients, divide the total weight evenly among the components.
  6. Food preparation trays are essential for organizing ingredients and setting up a mobile station.
  7. Preparation bowls are vital for mixing, chopping, and storing ingredients.
  8. Food storage canisters are useful for storing liquids, soups, and cleaning utensils.
  9. Saute pans are versatile and ideal for cooking meats.
  10. Fish pans are specifically designed for cooking fish and prawns.
  11. Copper saucepans are great for making caramel, melting butter, and small sauces.
  12. Frying pans are essential for various cooking tasks.
  13. Cooking pots are fundamental for boiling, simmering, and stewing.
  14. Roasting pans are ideal for cooking large pieces of meat and fish.
  15. Demary knives are a set of specialized knives for different tasks.
  16. Paring knives are used for peeling, shaping, and trimming vegetables.
  17. Boning knives are essential for butchering and removing bones from meat.
  18. Filleting knives are used for removing the fillets from fish.
  19. Chef's knives are versatile and used for chopping vegetables, slicing meat, and other tasks.

potage_dubar.txt - Potage Dubar

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a classic French cauliflower and potato soup
  • Understand the importance of using the correct ratio of cauliflower and potatoes
  • Master the technique of blending the soup for a smooth and creamy consistency

Ingredients

  • 500g cauliflower
  • 125g potatoes
  • 250ml milk
  • 2 cups chicken stock
  • Salt
  • White pepper
  • Double cream (for finishing)
  • Croutons (optional)
  • Parsley (optional)
  • Chives (optional)
  • Mini florets of cauliflower (optional)

Instructions

  1. Peel and quarter the potatoes. Place them in a bowl of cold water.
  2. Bring a pot of salted water to a boil. Add the cauliflower florets and cook for 15-20 minutes, or until tender.
  3. Drain the potatoes and add them to a clean pot. Mash them with a fork or potato masher.
  4. Drain the cauliflower and rinse the pot.
  5. Warm the milk and chicken stock in a saucepan.
  6. Combine the cooked cauliflower and the milk/stock mixture in a blender. Blend until smooth.
  7. Add the mashed potatoes to the cauliflower mixture and blend again until smooth.
  8. Season with salt and white pepper to taste.
  9. Transfer the soup to a clean saucepan. Warm it over low heat.
  10. Stir in the double cream.
  11. Serve hot, garnished with croutons, parsley, chives, or mini cauliflower florets.

potage_saint_germain.txt - Potage Saint Germain

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a classic French green pea soup
  • Understand the importance of proper blanching and blending techniques
  • Master the art of creating a smooth, velvety soup texture

Ingredients

  • 1 cup green split peas (aka puerci in French)
  • 2 tablespoons carrots, finely diced
  • 2 tablespoons onions, finely diced
  • 1 leek, green parts only, finely chopped
  • 1 bouquet garni (thyme, bay leaf, parsley)
  • 1 clove garlic, smashed
  • 2 smoked pork cutlets
  • 1 liter cold water (about 4 cups)
  • 1 tablespoon butter
  • 12 grams salt
  • 1 organic chicken stock cube (optional)
  • Cream or butter (for finishing)
  • Croutons (for serving)
  • Fresh parsley (for garnish)

Instructions

  1. Wash, peel, and chop all vegetables.
  2. Blanch the split peas in boiling water for a few minutes, then drain and rinse.
  3. Melt butter in a saucepan over medium heat.
  4. Add the smoked pork cutlets and cook for 3 minutes.
  5. Add the carrots, onions, and leeks to the pan and cook for another 2-3 minutes.
  6. Add the blanched split peas to the pan.
  7. Pour in 1 liter of cold water and bring to a boil.
  8. Skim off any foam from the surface of the soup.
  9. Add the garlic clove, bouquet garni, and pork bone to the soup.
  10. Cook for 30 minutes, then add salt and continue cooking for another 10-15 minutes.
  11. Remove the bouquet garni and bone from the soup.
  12. Blend the soup with an immersion blender until smooth.
  13. Pass the soup through a sieve to remove any remaining solids.
  14. Stir in a tablespoon of butter to add richness and silkiness to the soup (do not use cream as it will make the soup too pale).
  15. Warm the soup gently over low heat.
  16. Serve the soup hot with croutons and fresh parsley.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VHsF-bK9xsg

potato_crepe.txt - Potato Crepe

Objectives

  • Make gluten-free potato crepes
  • Prepare a simple salad to accompany the potato crepes
  • Utilize a food processor for grating potatoes

Ingredients

  • Potatoes (Royal Blue variety)
  • 1 egg
  • Salt
  • Pepper
  • Olive oil
  • Farmhouse goat cheese
  • Lettuce
  • French vinaigrette
  • Pine nuts
  • Basil

Instructions

  1. Prepare ingredients: Peel and keep potatoes in cold water until ready to grate. Wash lettuce.
  2. Roast pine nuts: Heat a pan over high heat, add pine nuts, and cook until lightly browned.
  3. Grate potatoes: Use a food processor with a large grating attachment to grate potatoes.
  4. Season potatoes: Add salt, pepper, and one egg to the grated potatoes. Mix gently.
  5. Cook potato crepes: Heat a pan over high heat with 2-3 tablespoons of olive oil. Add potato mixture to the pan, forming a circle. Cook for 7-8 minutes without touching, until the bottom is browned.
  6. Flip potato crepes: Use a plate to flip the crepe over, or flip it like a pancake.
  7. Assemble salad: Combine lettuce, French vinaigrette, and roasted pine nuts. Top with farmhouse goat cheese and basil.
  8. Serve: Slice potato crepes and serve with salad.

potato_croquettes.txt - Potato Croquettes

Objectives

  • Learn how to make delicious potato croquettes.
  • Understand the key ingredients and steps involved.
  • Explore the history and origins of potato croquettes.

Ingredients

  • 10 potatoes (Duchess potatoes are recommended)
  • 1/2 cup milk
  • 1/4 cup butter
  • 1/4 cup flour
  • 1 egg
  • Breadcrumbs
  • Salt and pepper to taste
  • Oil for frying

Instructions

  1. Peel and dice the potatoes.
  2. Boil the potatoes until tender.
  3. Drain the potatoes and mash them.
  4. Add the milk, butter, and flour to the mashed potatoes.
  5. Mix well until smooth.
  6. Shape the potato mixture into small croquettes.
  7. Dip each croquette in the beaten egg, then coat with breadcrumbs.
  8. Heat oil in a frying pan over medium heat.
  9. Fry the croquettes until golden brown and crispy.
  10. Remove the croquettes from the pan and drain on paper towels.
  11. Season with salt and pepper to taste.
  12. Serve hot.

potato_croquette.txt - Potato Croquettes

Objectives

  • Learn how to make potato croquettes, a classic French recipe.
  • Understand the importance of a dry potato mash for successful croquettes.
  • Master the technique of deep-frying croquettes for a crispy exterior and fluffy interior.

Ingredients

  • Potatoes
  • Salt
  • Pepper
  • Nutmeg
  • Butter
  • Eggs (egg yolks only)
  • Breadcrumbs
  • Canola oil (or grapeseed oil)

Instructions

  1. Place potatoes in a pot of cold water and add a pinch of salt.
  2. Bring to a boil over high heat and cook for 20 minutes.
  3. Drain the potatoes and return them to the pot. Let them dry out for a few minutes.
  4. Press the potatoes through a food mill to create a smooth mash.
  5. Season the mash with salt, pepper, and grated nutmeg.
  6. Heat the mash over low heat and stir until it is dry and slightly sticky.
  7. Incorporate butter into the mash, mixing gently until combined.
  8. Remove the mash from the heat and add the egg yolks, mixing gently until incorporated.
  9. Return the mash to the heat for 1-2 minutes, stirring constantly to cook the eggs slightly and bind the mixture together.
  10. Spread the mash onto a tray and let it cool completely.
  11. Once the mash is cold, transfer it to a piping bag (without a tip) and pipe out logs or balls.
  12. Prepare a breading station with three bowls: one with flour, one with beaten egg whites, and one with breadcrumbs.
  13. Gently roll each croquette in flour, then dip in egg whites, and finally coat in breadcrumbs.
  14. Place the breaded croquettes on a tray and refrigerate for 5-10 minutes to firm up.
  15. Heat oil to 170 degrees Celsius (338 degrees Fahrenheit).
  16. Carefully add the croquettes to the hot oil, a few at a time, and fry until golden brown.
  17. Remove the croquettes from the oil and drain on paper towels.
  18. Serve hot with your favorite dipping sauce.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=JJ29b53kxEw

pot_au_feu.txt - Pot-au-Feu

Objectives

  • Learn the history of the Pot-au-Feu, a classic French soup.
  • Master the traditional technique for preparing a rich, flavorful broth.
  • Discover modern plating and serving ideas for this timeless dish.

Ingredients

  • 4 liters of water (approximately 1 gallon)
  • 1.5 kg beef bones (about 3.3 lbs)
  • 1 kg beef (about 2.2 lbs), various cuts (ribs, blade, shoulder)
  • 2 large carrots
  • 2 celery stalks
  • 1 parsnip
  • 1 large onion
  • 4 cloves
  • 1 large turnip
  • 1 leek
  • Salt and peppercorns
  • 1 tablespoon of oil
  • 1/2 cup water
  • 1/2 cup beef broth (optional)
  • 1/4 cup mayonnaise (optional)
  • Gherkins
  • Mustard
  • Parsley (optional)

Instructions

  1. Place the beef bones in a large stockpot.
  2. Surround the bones with the pieces of beef.
  3. Pour 3 liters of cold water over the meat and bones.
  4. Bring the water to a boil over high heat.
  5. Skim off any impurities that rise to the surface.
  6. Add 300 ml (1 cup) of cold water to the pot.
  7. Bring the mixture to a boil again and skim off any additional impurities.
  8. Repeat steps 6 and 7 two more times, until you reach a total of 4 liters of water.
  9. Add the carrots, celery, parsnip, onion with cloves, and turnip to the pot.
  10. Bring the mixture to a boil one last time and skim off any remaining impurities.
  11. Reduce the heat to a simmer, ensuring the broth is gently bubbling.
  12. Cover the pot with a lid, leaving a small opening for steam to escape.
  13. Simmer for 3 hours, or until the meat is cooked through.
  14. Remove and discard the vegetables after 1 hour of cooking.
  15. Continue simmering the meat for an additional 1.5 hours.
  16. Once the meat is cooked, turn off the heat and let the broth rest.
  17. While the broth is resting, prepare the vegetables for serving:
    • Boil potatoes in salted water for 20 minutes, or until tender.
    • Boil carrots, turnips, and leeks in a mixture of beef broth and water for 15-20 minutes, or until tender.
  18. Once the vegetables are cooked, remove them from the heat and set aside.
  19. To serve, arrange the vegetables and meat on a platter.
  20. Serve the broth in a separate bowl.
  21. Add condiments such as gherkins, mustard, mayonnaise, and parsley as desired.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=QNh_KMM3I6Q

poulet_a_la_creme_de_morilles.txt - Poulet à la Crème de Morilles

Objectives

  • Learn to cook a classic French dish, Poulet à la Crème de Morilles
  • Master the preparation of Morel mushrooms
  • Create a rich and flavorful sauce with cherry wine and double cream

Ingredients

  • 4 pieces of chicken (about 4 chicken breasts)
  • 40-50 grams of dried Morel mushrooms
  • 1 tablespoon of butter
  • 2 shallots
  • 120 ml of dry sherry wine
  • 1 tablespoon of chicken stock
  • 1/2 liter of cream
  • Salt and pepper to taste
  • Parsley for garnish (optional)

Instructions

  1. Soak the dried Morel mushrooms in hot water for at least 1 hour, up to 2 hours.
  2. Strain the mushrooms, reserving the soaking liquid.
  3. Rinse the mushrooms thoroughly under running water to remove any sand or particles.
  4. Strain the mushroom soaking liquid through a fine sieve to remove any sediment.
  5. Cut the Morel mushrooms into uniform sizes for even cooking.
  6. Season the chicken pieces with salt and pepper.
  7. Cut and sharpen the shallots lengthwise.
  8. Bring the cherry wine to a boil for about 30 seconds to evaporate excess alcohol.
  9. Melt butter in a cast iron pan over low heat.
  10. Add the chicken pieces to the pan and cook for 3-4 minutes on each side to brown.
  11. Remove the chicken from the pan and set aside.
  12. Add the shallots to the pan and sweat for 1-2 minutes.
  13. Add the Morel mushrooms to the pan and cook for 1-2 minutes.
  14. Add the cherry wine to the pan and reduce by half.
  15. Gradually add the reserved mushroom soaking liquid to the pan.
  16. Reduce the liquid slightly before adding the cream.
  17. Season the sauce with salt and a pinch of chicken stock.
  18. Add the cream to the pan, barely covering the Morel mushrooms.
  19. Bring the sauce to a boil and reduce until it thickens.
  20. Return the chicken to the pan and cook for 10-15 minutes, or until tender.
  21. Serve the chicken with the sauce and garnish with parsley, if desired.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=1J6ADe12VwI

poulet_a_la_gaston_gerard.txt - Poulet à la Gaston Gérard

Objectives

  • Learn the history of Poulet à la Gaston Gérard.
  • Prepare a simple, classic French chicken dish.
  • Master the art of making a rich, flavorful sauce.

Ingredients

  • 1 free-range chicken, cut into pieces
  • 2 tablespoons paprika
  • 100 grams Comté cheese or Gruyère cheese
  • 1/2 cup heavy cream
  • 2 tablespoons Dijon mustard
  • 1 glass dry white wine (Muscadet or Burgundy)
  • 1 tablespoon oil
  • 1 knob of butter
  • Salt and pepper to taste
  • Breadcrumbs

Instructions

  1. Heat a cast iron pan over medium heat.
  2. Add 1 tablespoon of oil and a knob of butter to the pan.
  3. Season chicken pieces with salt and pepper.
  4. Place chicken pieces in the pan and cook for 3-4 minutes per side, until lightly golden.
  5. Remove chicken pieces from the pan and set aside.
  6. Add the chicken carcass to the pan and cook for a few minutes.
  7. Reduce heat to medium-low.
  8. Arrange chicken pieces and chicken carcass in the pan.
  9. Sprinkle paprika over the chicken.
  10. Cover the pan and cook for 35-40 minutes on low heat.
  11. Remove the chicken pieces and keep them warm in a preheated oven at 60°C.
  12. Discard the chicken carcass.
  13. Increase heat to high.
  14. Bring the cooking juices to a boil for 1-2 minutes.
  15. Add 100 grams of grated cheese to the pan.
  16. Stir until the cheese melts and forms a fondue.
  17. Pour in a glass of dry white wine and bring to a boil again.
  18. Add 1/2 cup of heavy cream and bring to a boil.
  19. Reduce the sauce for 5-6 minutes until it coats the back of a spoon.
  20. Turn off the heat.
  21. Stir in 1-2 tablespoons of Dijon mustard.
  22. Taste and adjust seasoning.
  23. Pour the sauce over the chicken in an oven-safe dish.
  24. Grate the remaining cheese over the chicken.
  25. Sprinkle breadcrumbs over the cheese.
  26. Broil in the oven until the cheese and breadcrumbs are golden brown.
  27. Serve immediately.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=bFHe6hpoQGM

poulet_basque.txt - Poulet Basque

Objectives

  • Learn to prepare a traditional Basque Country chicken dish.
  • Master the technique of making a rich, flavorful chicken stock.
  • Understand the importance of low-heat simmering for confit preparations.

Ingredients

For the stock: - 7-8 chicken wings - 1/2 onion - 1/2 carrot - 1 tablespoon tomato paste - 1 tablespoon oil (peanut oil preferred) - Bouquet garni (bay leaf, thyme, parsley) - 2 cups chicken stock - 1/2 tablespoon dried thyme - 1 bay leaf

For the confit: - 1 tablespoon olive oil - 1/2 onion - 2 garlic cloves - 1 bell pepper - 1 can cherry tomatoes - Bouquet garni (bay leaf, thyme, parsley)

For the chicken: - Chicken thighs - Salt and pepper - White wine

Other: - Prosciutto ham (diced) - Water

Instructions

  1. Prepare the chicken stock:
  2. Heat oil in a pan over high heat.
  3. Add chicken wings and brown on all sides.
  4. Add garlic, carrot, and onion.
  5. Cook for 5 minutes.
  6. Stir in tomato paste and cook for another minute.
  7. Add chicken stock, dried thyme, and bay leaf.
  8. Reduce heat to low and simmer for 30 minutes.
  9. Blanch the prosciutto:
  10. Dice prosciutto into small pieces.
  11. Add cold water to a pot and bring to a boil.
  12. Add prosciutto and cook until the water boils again.
  13. Drain the prosciutto and rinse with cold water.
  14. Make the confit:
  15. Heat olive oil in a pan over low heat.
  16. Add blanched prosciutto and cook for 1 minute.
  17. Add onion and cook for a few minutes.
  18. Add garlic and cook for another few minutes.
  19. Add bell pepper and cook until fragrant.
  20. Add bouquet garni and cherry tomatoes.
  21. Add a little water or tomato sauce if needed.
  22. Cover and simmer over very low heat for 15-20 minutes, or until most of the liquid is gone.
  23. Prepare the chicken:
  24. Preheat oven to 360°F (200°C).
  25. Season chicken thighs with salt and pepper.
  26. Heat a cast-iron pan over medium heat.
  27. Add chicken thighs and brown on both sides.
  28. Transfer chicken to the oven and bake for 10 minutes, covered.
  29. Make the sauce:
  30. Remove chicken from oven and set aside.
  31. Increase heat to medium-high.
  32. Reduce any remaining juices in the pan until caramelized.
  33. Deglaze the pan with white wine, scraping up any browned bits.
  34. Reduce the wine until almost gone.
  35. Add chicken stock and reduce until it reaches a nappage consistency.
  36. Assemble the dish:
  37. Add the confit vegetables to the sauce.
  38. Return the chicken to the sauce.
  39. Cook gently for 5 minutes.
  40. Serve immediately.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=GjBciv1otuE

pule_a_labriillard.txt - Pule à la Brilliard

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a traditional French dish with cider, cream, and mustard
  • Understand the history and origin of the Pule à la Brilliard
  • Master the technique of creating a flavorful sauce with a spoon coating consistency

Ingredients

  • Old-fashioned mustard (1-2 tablespoons)
  • Cider (sweet or medium dry)
  • Good quality cream
  • Whole chicken (cut into pieces)
  • Carrot (1 medium, chopped)
  • Shallot (1 medium, chopped)
  • Parsley (for garnish)
  • Oyster mushrooms (optional, for garnish)
  • Butter (for browning)
  • Oil (for browning)

Instructions

  1. Melt butter and oil in a pan over medium heat.
  2. Brown the chicken offcuts to create a flavorful stock.
  3. Discard the offcuts and add the chicken pieces to the pan.
  4. Brown the chicken on all sides, about 5 minutes per side.
  5. Remove the chicken and set aside.
  6. Add the shallots and carrots to the pan and cook for a few minutes.
  7. Deglaze the pan with cider, scraping up the caramelized bits.
  8. Reduce the cider until almost dry.
  9. Add the chicken offcuts back to the pan to create the stock base.
  10. Return the chicken pieces to the pan, cover with cider, and cook for 25-30 minutes.
  11. Remove the chicken breasts after 15 minutes to prevent overcooking.
  12. Once the chicken is cooked, discard the offcuts and strain the sauce through a sieve.
  13. Return the strained sauce to the pan and add the cream.
  14. Bring the sauce to a simmer and reduce until it coats the back of a spoon.
  15. Remove from heat and stir in the mustard.
  16. Add a tablespoon of chicken juices to the sauce.
  17. Pour the sauce over the chicken and garnish with mushrooms and parsley.
  18. Serve immediately.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=PZ7xivGvpEM

pule_alice_chicken.txt - Pule Alice Chicken

Objectives

  • Learn to cook a simple yet elegant chicken dish with a creamy mushroom sauce.
  • Master the technique of deglazing a pan for a flavorful sauce.
  • Understand the importance of slow cooking and proper heat control for tender chicken.

Ingredients

  • 4 chicken pieces (2 breasts, 2 thighs)
  • 1 tablespoon butter
  • 1 tablespoon olive oil
  • Salt and pepper
  • 4 mushrooms
  • 100 ml brown chicken stock
  • 100 ml white wine
  • 1 tablespoon cognac
  • 100 ml cream
  • 1 shallot
  • Parsley (optional)

Instructions

  1. Season the chicken pieces with salt.
  2. Heat the butter and olive oil in a cast iron pot over medium heat.
  3. Add the chicken pieces, skin side down, and cook for 25 minutes, turning the heat to medium.
  4. While the chicken cooks, quarter the mushrooms and sauté them in a separate pan with olive oil, salt, and pepper.
  5. Reduce the chicken stock over high heat for 15 minutes to concentrate its flavor.
  6. After 25 minutes, turn the chicken pieces over and continue cooking for another 8-10 minutes.
  7. Remove the chicken from the pot and set aside on a tray.
  8. Remove excess fat from the pot, leaving the caramelized juices.
  9. Add the shallots and sautéed mushrooms to the pot.
  10. Deglaze the pan with the white wine and cognac, bringing the mixture to a boil and reducing by half.
  11. Add the reduced chicken stock and reduce again by half.
  12. Stir in the cream and season with pepper.
  13. Return the chicken pieces to the pot and braise for 10 minutes.
  14. Remove the chicken from the pot and keep warm.
  15. Reduce the sauce to desired thickness.
  16. Plate the chicken with the sauce and mushrooms, garnishing with parsley if desired.
  17. Serve immediately.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=I6vs2HkMt6o

rabbit_mustard_sauce.txt - Rabbit in Mustard Sauce

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a classic French rabbit dish with mustard sauce
  • Understand the importance of creating a white stock for the sauce
  • Master the techniques for glazing onions and cooking mushrooms for a white-themed dish

Ingredients

  • 1 rabbit, cut into pieces
  • 1 tablespoon flour
  • 1 onion, peeled and sliced
  • 2 tablespoons mustard
  • 2 tablespoons cream (optional)
  • 1/2 tablespoon fresh tarragon
  • 1/2 cup chicken stock
  • 1 cup water
  • 1 cup rabbit stock (made with rabbit bones, chicken bones, celery, carrots, leeks, bouquet garni, onions, and cloves)
  • 1/2 cup mushrooms, sliced
  • 1/4 cup butter
  • 1/2 lemon
  • 1/2 cup white wine (optional)
  • 1/2 teaspoon sugar
  • Salt and pepper to taste
  • Parsley for garnish

Instructions

  1. Make a white stock by blanching rabbit and chicken bones, then simmering with celery, carrots, leeks, bouquet garni, onions, and cloves in water and chicken stock for 45 minutes.
  2. While the stock simmers, cook the mushrooms in water, butter, and lemon juice until tender, about 10 minutes.
  3. Glaze the onions by simmering them in water, sugar, and butter until the water evaporates and the onions are translucent.
  4. Filter the white stock and set aside.
  5. Brown the rabbit pieces in a pan over medium heat.
  6. Remove the rabbit from the pan and set aside.
  7. Sweat the onion in the same pan over low heat for 5 minutes.
  8. Sprinkle in flour and cook for a few minutes, stirring constantly, to create a roux.
  9. Gradually whisk in the white stock, bringing to a boil and simmering until thickened.
  10. Add cream and reduce by a quarter.
  11. Add the rabbit pieces to the sauce and simmer for 40-45 minutes, or until cooked through.
  12. Remove the rabbit from the sauce and stir in mustard, tarragon, and additional cream (optional).
  13. Return the rabbit pieces to the sauce.
  14. Serve the rabbit in mustard sauce with tagliatelle, white-cooked mushrooms, glazed onions, and a sprinkle of parsley.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=U2keZyMtCoY

rack_of_lamb_venis.txt - Rack of Lamb Cooked in the Style of Venis

Objectives

  • Learn the pan-roasting technique for a rack of lamb
  • Prepare a delicious rack of lamb with simple vegetables
  • Master the art of pre-cooking and browning vegetables for a flavorful dish

Ingredients

  • 1 rack of lamb
  • 1 1/2 tbsp olive oil
  • 1 tbsp sunflower oil
  • 1/2 courgette, diced
  • 1 potato, diced
  • 1/2 cup cherry tomatoes, halved
  • 1 bay leaf
  • 1 sprig lemon thyme
  • 2-3 garlic cloves
  • 1/4 cup black olives
  • Salt and pepper to taste

Instructions

  1. Preheat oven to 210°C (410°F) with fan.
  2. Dice courgette, potato, and tomatoes into small cubes.
  3. Heat 1 1/2 tbsp olive oil in a non-stick pan over medium heat.
  4. Add courgette to the pan and season with salt and pepper.
  5. Cook for a few minutes, browning lightly.
  6. Repeat steps 3-5 with the diced potatoes in a separate pan.
  7. Briefly sauté the tomatoes in a pan with a little oil and salt and pepper.
  8. Season the rack of lamb with salt.
  9. Heat 1 tbsp sunflower oil in a cast iron pot over medium-high heat.
  10. Brown the rack of lamb on all sides, ensuring the fat side is seared first.
  11. Remove the rack of lamb from the pot and set aside.
  12. Wipe out any excess grease from the pot.
  13. Return the rack of lamb to the pot.
  14. Arrange the pre-cooked vegetables, bay leaf, thyme, and garlic cloves around the lamb.
  15. Place the lid on the pot and bake for 20 minutes.
  16. Remove from oven and check the internal temperature of the lamb, aiming for 145°F (62°C).
  17. Garnish with black olives.
  18. Serve immediately.

raspberry_tablet.txt - Raspberry Tablet

Objectives

  • Learn to make a delicious raspberry tablet using French techniques.
  • Understand how to create a smooth and creamy pastry cream.
  • Master the art of assembling a beautiful and flavorful raspberry tablet.

Ingredients

Pastry Cream: - 2 egg yolks - 1/4 cup sugar - 2 tablespoons corn flour - 1 cup milk - 2 tablespoons butter - 1 teaspoon vanilla extract

Raspberry Cream: - 1 cup raspberries - 1/4 cup sugar - 1 tablespoon lemon juice

Assembly: - 1 package of tartlets - Fresh strawberries - Mint leaves

Instructions

  1. Make the pastry cream:
  2. In a saucepan, whisk together the egg yolks, sugar, and corn flour until smooth.
  3. Gradually whisk in the milk until fully combined.
  4. Cook over medium heat, stirring constantly, until the mixture thickens.
  5. Remove from heat and stir in the butter and vanilla extract until smooth.
  6. Transfer to a bowl and cover with plastic wrap, pressing the wrap directly onto the surface of the cream to prevent a skin fromblocked: candidate: FinishReasonRecitation

raspberry_vanilla_slice.txt - Raspberry Vanilla Slice

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a delicious raspberry vanilla slice.
  • Understand the difference between the French version (mille-feuille) and this version.
  • Master the techniques for making pastry cream and mousseline cream.

Ingredients

  • Corn flour
  • 4 eggs (yolks only)
  • Whole milk
  • Pure cream
  • Fresh raspberries
  • Sugar
  • Butter
  • Fresh vanilla bean

Instructions

  1. Preheat the oven to 200 degrees Celsius (400 degrees Fahrenheit).
  2. Make the pastry cream:
  3. Heat milk in a pan over low to medium heat.
  4. Split the vanilla bean, scrape out the seeds, and add both to the milk.
  5. Whisk the egg yolks with 40 grams of sugar for 2-3 minutes until pale and thick.
  6. Once the milk is warming up, add the remaining sugar.
  7. Bring the milk to a boil, then immediately turn off the heat and whisk gently.
  8. Add corn flour to the egg yolk mixture, whisking to combine.
  9. Slowly add the hot milk to the egg yolk mixture, whisking continuously.
  10. Return the mixture to the pan and cook over medium heat, whisking constantly, until the cream thickens.
  11. Remove from heat and transfer to a clean metal container.
  12. Cool the cream by placing the container in a bowl of ice water.
  13. Prepare the puff pastry:
  14. Place the puff pastry on a baking tray lined with a silicon mat.
  15. Cover the pastry with parchment paper and weigh it down to prevent it from rising.
  16. Bake in the preheated oven for 20 minutes.
  17. Finish the pastry cream:
  18. Once the pastry cream is lukewarm, add the butter and whisk until combined.
  19. Cover the cream with plastic wrap, ensuring the wrap touches the surface, and refrigerate until cold.
  20. Make the whipped cream:
  21. Chill a bowl and whisk.
  22. Add 100 ml of pure cream to the chilled bowl and whisk until slightly thickened.
  23. Add 10 grams of caster sugar and continue whisking until the cream is whipped.
  24. Assemble the mousseline cream:
  25. Add a tablespoon of rum to the chilled pastry cream.
  26. Gently fold in the whipped cream until combined.
  27. Assemble the vanilla slice:
  28. Cut a piece of puff pastry in half.
  29. Spread a layer of mousseline cream on one half.
  30. Top with fresh raspberries.
  31. Spread another layer of mousseline cream on top of the raspberries.
  32. Place the other half of the puff pastry on top and press gently.
  33. Trim the edges of the slice as desired.
  34. Dust with powdered sugar.
  35. Serve immediately.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MGOncCRTl-Q

red_onion_tart.txt - Red Onion Tart

Objectives

  • Create a delicious and easy onion tart using pre-made puff pastry
  • Caramelize red onions with red wine for a sweet and savory flavor
  • Assemble and bake the tart for a simple yet impressive appetizer

Ingredients

  • 1 kg red onions
  • 50-60g butter
  • 1-2 tablespoons sugar
  • 50 ml red wine
  • Salt and pepper to taste
  • 1 teaspoon thyme (fresh or dried)
  • 1/2 tablespoon cherry vinegar or balsamic vinegar
  • 1 sheet of puff pastry (defrosted)
  • Soft goat cheese
  • Toasted pine nuts
  • Chives (for garnish)

Instructions

  1. Peel and thinly slice the red onions. Discard the root.
  2. Melt butter in a medium saucepan over medium heat.
  3. Add sliced onions, salt, and pepper. Cook for 5 minutes, stirring occasionally.
  4. Add sugar and red wine. Continue cooking for 15 minutes, stirring occasionally, until the onions are soft and caramelized.
  5. Add thyme and vinegar. Increase heat to high and cook for a few minutes, stirring constantly, until the onions are slightly sticky.
  6. Transfer the caramelized onions to a bowl and let cool.
  7. Preheat oven to 200 degrees Celsius (400 degrees Fahrenheit).
  8. Place a sheet of parchment paper on a baking sheet.
  9. Unfold the puff pastry on the baking sheet.
  10. Spread the cooled caramelized onion mixture evenly over the pastry, leaving a small border.
  11. Bake for 25 minutes, or until the pastry is golden brown and puffed.
  12. Let the tart cool slightly before garnishing with soft goat cheese, toasted pine nuts, and chives.
  13. Serve warm.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=CMheetDyG3U

red_wine_butter_sauce.txt - Red Wine Butter Sauce (Bur Rouge)

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a red wine butter sauce (Bur Rouge)
  • Understand the techniques to achieve a deep red color
  • Discover how to balance the acidity and flavor of the sauce

Ingredients

  • 400 ml French red wine (full bodied, inexpensive)
  • 1 tablespoon Ruby Port (optional)
  • 1 shallot, chopped
  • 100 g mushrooms, chopped
  • 1 carrot, chopped
  • 1 clove garlic, crushed
  • 1 tablespoon tomato paste
  • 1 sprig of thyme
  • 1 bay leaf
  • 1 tablespoon parsley stalks
  • 1 teaspoon juniper berries
  • 1 teaspoon peppercorns
  • 150 g cold butter, cubed
  • Salt and pepper to taste

Instructions

  1. Combine the wine, port (optional), shallot, mushrooms, carrot, garlic, tomato paste, thyme, bay leaf, parsley stalks, juniper berries, and peppercorns in a large saucepan.
  2. Bring the mixture to a low boil and reduce by half, about 10-15 minutes.
  3. Strain the reduction through a fine-mesh sieve into a clean saucepan, pressing on the solids to extract all the liquid.
  4. Return the strained reduction to the saucepan and reduce over medium-low heat until it reaches a syrupy consistency, about 2-3 tablespoons remaining.
  5. Reduce the heat to very low. Add the cold butter cubes, a few at a time, whisking continuously until the butter melts and the sauce emulsifies.
  6. Season with salt and pepper to taste.
  7. Keep the sauce warm in a double boiler until ready to serve.
  8. Serve the sauce over grilled fish or meat.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=1meW2BLrb7I

red_wine_butter.txt - Red Wine Butter

Objectives

  • Learn to make red wine butter for steaks
  • Understand the importance of using high-fat content butter
  • Discover a new technique for incorporating sauce into butter

Ingredients

  • 82% fat content butter, softened
  • Red wine
  • Beef stock
  • Thyme
  • Shallots
  • Bay leaf
  • Lemon
  • Parsley

Instructions

  1. Soften the butter in the microwave until it is very soft and can be easily mixed.
  2. Reduce the beef stock over medium heat until it is a thick glaze.
  3. Thinly slice shallots and add them to a pan with a bay leaf, thyme, and red wine.
  4. Bring the wine to a light boil and reduce by half.
  5. Optional: Add black pepper to the wine reduction.
  6. Discard the aromatics from the wine reduction and set aside to cool.
  7. Combine the beef glaze, parsley, a tablespoon of lemon juice, and the wine reduction in a bowl.
  8. Add the parsley to the softened butter and whisk until combined.
  9. Gradually add half of the wine reduction mixture to the butter, whisking constantly until incorporated.
  10. Continue adding the wine reduction mixture in small amounts, whisking until fully combined.
  11. Adjust the seasoning with salt and pepper to taste.
  12. Transfer the butter mixture to a piece of plastic wrap and roll into a log.
  13. Refrigerate the butter log for at least 4 hours or overnight to allow the flavors to infuse.
  14. Slice the butter onto steaks and serve.

ribeye_steak_red_wine_sauce.txt - Ribeye Steak with Red Wine Sauce

Objectives

  • Learn to make a simple and delicious red wine sauce.
  • Cook a ribeye steak to medium-rare perfection.
  • Prepare a classic French bistro-style side dish of fried potatoes.

Ingredients

  • 1 ribeye steak (thick)
  • 4 tbsp groundnut oil
  • 1 tbsp butter
  • 1 shallot, chopped
  • 1 tbsp flour
  • 120 ml red wine
  • 1 pinch sugar
  • Salt and pepper to taste
  • Fresh parsley (for garnish)
  • Potatoes (for garnish)
  • Garlic (for garnish)

Instructions

  1. Heat a frying pan over high heat.
  2. Add 4 tbsp groundnut oil to the pan and heat until smoking.
  3. Sear the ribeye steak for 2 minutes on each side.
  4. Reduce heat to low and cook the steak for an additional 8 minutes, turning occasionally, to reach medium-rare.
  5. Remove the steak from the pan and place it on a warm tray to rest.
  6. In a separate non-stick pan, melt 1 tbsp butter over low heat.
  7. Add the chopped shallots and cook until softened, about 5 minutes.
  8. Add 1 tbsp flour to the pan and cook for 1 minute, stirring constantly.
  9. Pour in 120 ml of red wine and bring to a boil.
  10. Reduce the sauce over medium heat until it thickens, about 10 minutes.
  11. Add a pinch of sugar, salt, and pepper to taste.
  12. Remove the sauce from heat and stir in a small amount of fresh parsley and a knob of butter.
  13. While the steak is resting, prepare the potatoes. Heat a steel pan over medium heat and add a generous amount of oil.
  14. Add the potatoes to the pan and fry until golden brown, tossing occasionally.
  15. Add a bit of garlic and parsley to the potatoes towards the end of cooking.
  16. Once the steak has rested, transfer it to a serving dish and pour the red wine sauce over top.
  17. Serve the steak with the fried potatoes and enjoy.

rice_pudding.txt - Rice Pudding

Objectives

  • Learn how to make rice pudding using a pastry chef's recipe.
  • Understand the difference between a cook's and a pastry chef's approach to rice pudding.
  • Discover the secret ingredient that elevates the rice pudding to a custard-like texture.

Ingredients

  • Full cream milk
  • Sugar
  • 2 egg yolks
  • Arborio rice (round grain rice)
  • Fresh vanilla pod
  • Butter

Instructions

  1. Bring a small pan of water to a boil.
  2. In a large saucepan, combine the full cream milk, sugar, and vanilla pod (sliced open with seeds removed).
  3. Heat the milk mixture over medium heat, slowly bringing it almost to a boil.
  4. While the milk is warming, rinse the arborio rice under cold water.
  5. Add the rinsed rice to the boiling water and cook for 2 minutes.
  6. Drain the rice and add it to the warm milk mixture.
  7. Reduce heat to a very low simmer and cook for 30-45 minutes, stirring occasionally.
  8. Turn off the heat and remove the vanilla pod.
  9. Add 30 grams of cold butter to the cooked rice pudding and stir until melted.
  10. Gradually whisk in 2-3 egg yolks, stirring constantly to prevent them from cooking.
  11. Pour the rice pudding into a metal tray and cool rapidly in the refrigerator or freezer.
  12. Serve chilled.

Instructions

roasted_quails_with_grapes.txt - Roasted Quails with Grapes

Objectives

  • Learn to prepare and roast quails with grapes.
  • Master the technique of barding quails with bacon.
  • Discover the classic French recipe for roasted quails.

Ingredients

  • 3 quails
  • 1 piece of grape per quail
  • Rock salt
  • 1 piece of bacon per quail
  • Butcher string
  • White grapes
  • Cognac
  • Shallots
  • Garlic
  • Parsley
  • Butter
  • Oil
  • 100 ml of chicken stock
  • Salt and pepper

Instructions

  1. Prepare the quails for cooking.
  2. Stuff each quail with a piece of grape.
  3. Season the inside of each quail with a pinch of rock salt.
  4. Tie the legs of each quail together using butcher string.
  5. Wrap each quail with a piece of bacon, securing it with string.
  6. Refrigerate the prepared quails.
  7. Prepare the grapes.
  8. Place the grapes in a bowl and rinse with clear water.
  9. Blanch the grapes in boiling water for 10 seconds.
  10. Immediately plunge the grapes into cold water.
  11. Peel the skin off each grape.
  12. Prepare the mushrooms.
  13. Trim the stems of the mushrooms.
  14. Lightly rinse and brush the mushrooms.
  15. Marinate the grapes in cognac.
  16. Place the peeled grapes in a container and pour cognac over them.
  17. Allow the grapes to macerate in cognac.
  18. Prepare the stock.
  19. Combine 100 ml of chicken stock with shallots, garlic, and parsley.
  20. Roast the quails.
  21. Heat a saute pan over medium to high heat.
  22. Add a mix of butter and oil to the pan.
  23. Place the quails in the pan and cook for 4 minutes per side.
  24. Reduce the heat to low and continue cooking until the quails are golden brown.
  25. Transfer the quails to a preheated oven at 200 degrees Celsius (400 degrees Fahrenheit) and cook for 10-15 minutes.
  26. Pan-fry the mushrooms.
  27. Heat a pan over high heat.
  28. Add the mushrooms to the pan and season with salt and pepper.
  29. Cook until the mushrooms are tender and slightly browned.
  30. Add garlic to the pan and continue cooking, tossing the mushrooms until they are evenly cooked.
  31. Remove the pan from heat and add parsley.
  32. Prepare the sauce.
  33. Remove the quails from the oven and set aside.
  34. Remove the excess fat from the pan.
  35. Add shallots to the pan and cook until caramelized.
  36. Deglaze the pan with cognac.
  37. Reduce the cognac until almost dry.
  38. Add the chicken stock to the pan.
  39. Reduce the stock until it thickens.
  40. Add the marinated grapes to the pan and cook until they are slightly caramelized.
  41. Remove the grapes from the pan and set aside.
  42. Add the mushroom stock to the pan.
  43. Reduce the sauce until it becomes a glaze.
  44. Assemble and serve.
  45. Pour the sauce over the roasted quails.
  46. Arrange the quails on a plate with the grapes and mushrooms.
  47. Garnish with parsley.
  48. Serve immediately.

routier_roast_sauce_governor.txt - Routier Roast with Sauce Governor

Objectives

  • Learn to make a classic French routier roast with sauce governor.
  • Understand the importance of marinating the venison meat for at least 12 hours.
  • Master the art of making a rich, peppery sauce with cranberry marmalade.

Ingredients

  • 1 piece of venison, pre-marinated in red wine for at least 12 hours
  • 1 liter of beef stock
  • 1 tablespoon of red wine marinade
  • 1 tablespoon of red wine marinade garnish (including juniper berries, cloves, thyme, bay leaf, peppercorns)
  • 1 teaspoon of tomato paste
  • 1 tablespoon of vinegar
  • 30 grams of pork belly
  • 1 tablespoon of butter
  • 1 tablespoon of flour
  • 1 tablespoon of butter
  • 2 cups of beef stock
  • 1 teaspoon of cranberry jelly
  • 200 ml of cream (optional)
  • 1 cup of chestnuts, precooked
  • 1 tablespoon of butter
  • Salt and pepper to taste
  • 1 cup of forest mushrooms
  • Oil

Instructions

  1. Prepare the sauce:
  2. Strain the red wine marinade, separating the liquid from the garnish.
  3. Bring the marinade liquid to a boil and reduce by half.
  4. Bring the beef stock to a boil and reduce for 10 minutes.
  5. Combine 1 tablespoon of butter and 1 tablespoon of flour, whisk together, and add to the reduced beef stock.
  6. Bring the stock mixture to a boil and thicken.
  7. Sauté the pork belly:
  8. Heat a sauté pan over medium heat.
  9. Add 1 tablespoon of butter and 30 grams of pork belly.
  10. Cook for 1-2 minutes.
  11. Combine the sauce ingredients:
  12. Add the red wine marinade garnish, thyme, bay leaf, peppercorns, and tomato paste to the sauté pan.
  13. Cook for a few minutes.
  14. Make the gastrique:
  15. In a separate pan, combine 1 tablespoon of vinegar and 1 tablespoon of red wine marinade.
  16. Reduce the mixture until almost dry.
  17. Add the stock:
  18. Add the thickened beef stock to the gastrique.
  19. Cook the sauce:
  20. Simmer the sauce for 15-20 minutes on low heat.
  21. Make the chestnut puree:
  22. Heat 1 tablespoon of butter in a pan over medium-low heat.
  23. Add the precooked chestnuts and warm them up.
  24. Mash the chestnuts with a potato ricer or manual tool.
  25. Gradually add 200 ml of cream and warm the mixture.
  26. Press the mixture further to create a smooth puree.
  27. Season with salt and pepper.
  28. Cook the venison:
  29. Pat the venison dry with paper towels.
  30. Season with salt and pepper.
  31. Heat a pan with a little oil over medium-high heat.
  32. Sear the venison on all sides until browned.
  33. Transfer the venison to a baking dish.
  34. Add the remaining marinade vegetables to the baking dish.
  35. Bake in a preheated oven at 180 degrees Celsius (350 degrees Fahrenheit) for 15-20 minutes.
  36. Cook the mushrooms:
  37. Heat a pan with oil over high heat.
  38. Add the forest mushrooms and cook until they release their water and become browned.
  39. Finish the sauce:
  40. Strain the sauce through a sieve.
  41. Add 1 teaspoon of cranberry jelly to the sauce.
  42. Blend the sauce to combine.
  43. Plate the dish:
  44. Arrange the chestnut puree on the plate.
  45. Add slices of venison.
  46. Drizzle the sauce over the venison and puree.
  47. Garnish with cooked mushrooms.
  48. Enjoy!

salad_leones.txt - Salad Lyonnaise

Objectives

  • Learn to make a classic French salad, Salad Lyonnaise
  • Understand the importance of quality ingredients
  • Master the technique of medium boiled eggs

Ingredients

  • 1 piece smoked bacon
  • 1 piece bread
  • 1 head frisee lettuce
  • 4 eggs
  • 2 tablespoons walnut oil
  • 1 tablespoon vinegar
  • Salt and pepper
  • 1 clove garlic
  • Parsley

Instructions

  1. Trim the rind off the smoked bacon and slice it into lardons.
  2. Cut the bread into thin slices.
  3. Wash the frisee lettuce twice in a bowl of water, scooping it out to prevent water from seeping back into the lettuce.
  4. Bring a pot of water to a boil and gently add the eggs to the boiling water.
  5. Once the water returns to a boil, start a timer for six minutes.
  6. After six minutes, drain the water and immediately pour cold water over the eggs.
  7. Heat a steel pan over medium heat and add the bacon lardons.
  8. Cook the lardons for 2-3 minutes until crispy and browned.
  9. Remove the lardons from the pan and set aside on paper towels to absorb excess fat.
  10. Add butter to the same pan and warm it up.
  11. Add the slices of bread to the pan and cook for 2 minutes on each side until golden brown.
  12. Remove the croutons from the pan and set aside on paper towels to absorb excess fat.
  13. In a bowl, whisk together the walnut oil, vinegar, salt, and pepper.
  14. Rub a clove of garlic on both sides of each crouton.
  15. Place the frisee lettuce in a bowl and pour the dressing over it.
  16. Toss the lettuce to coat it in the dressing.
  17. Place the dressed lettuce in a serving dish.
  18. Add the croutons to the serving dish.
  19. Peel the medium boiled eggs and add them to the serving dish.
  20. Sprinkle with chopped parsley.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2n38O9VF7to

salmon_cider_veloute.txt - Salmon with Cider Velouté

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a simple, elegant cider velouté sauce.
  • Poach salmon using a parchment paper lid to prevent drying.
  • Create a flavorful and easy pan sauce for fish.

Ingredients

  • Salmon fillet (approx. 150g)
  • 1 tablespoon butter
  • 1 tablespoon flour
  • 1/2 cup cider
  • 1 shallot, thinly diced
  • 1 bay leaf
  • Salt and pepper to taste
  • 1/4 cup heavy cream
  • 1 teaspoon lemon juice

Instructions

  1. Melt the butter in a saucepan over medium heat.
  2. Whisk in the flour and cook for 2-3 minutes, stirring constantly, until the roux is golden brown.
  3. Pour in the cider and bring to a simmer.
  4. Season with salt and pepper.
  5. Add the diced shallots and bay leaf.
  6. Place the salmon fillet in the pan.
  7. Cover the pan with a piece of parchment paper that has been buttered on one side.
  8. Simmer for 8-10 minutes, or until the salmon is cooked through.
  9. Remove the salmon and set aside.
  10. Strain the cooking juices from the pan into a bowl.
  11. Whisk the hot cooking juices into the roux, stirring constantly.
  12. Reduce the heat to medium-high and thicken the sauce.
  13. Stir in the heavy cream and lemon juice.
  14. Taste and adjust seasoning.
  15. Pour the sauce over the salmon and serve immediately.

salmon_tartar.txt - Salmon Tartar

Objectives

  • Learn to make a classic salmon tartar recipe
  • Understand the importance of using fresh, high-quality ingredients
  • Master the technique of making a mayonnaise-based sauce

Ingredients

  • 1 piece of fresh king salmon
  • 1 tablespoon of olive oil
  • 1 dash of Tabasco
  • 1 dash of English sauce
  • 1 tablespoon of good quality capers
  • 1 shallot
  • 1 egg yolk
  • Salt and pepper to taste
  • Dijon mustard
  • Parsley
  • Chives
  • Lemon juice

Instructions

  1. Remove the skin from the salmon.
  2. Place the salmon in the freezer for a short time to firm it up.
  3. Chop the salmon into very small cubes using a knife.
  4. Prepare the Mison Plus:
  5. Measure out the olive oil, Tabasco, English sauce, capers, shallots, egg yolk, salt, pepper, and Dijon mustard.
  6. Finely chop the parsley and chives.
  7. Make the mayonnaise:
  8. Combine the egg yolk, mustard, salt, and pepper in a bowl.
  9. Slowly whisk in the olive oil until the mixture thickens and emulsifies.
  10. Add lemon juice to lighten the color and consistency.
  11. Flavor the mayonnaise:
  12. Add the chopped shallots, parsley, chives, Tabasco, and English sauce to the mayonnaise.
  13. Mix well to combine.
  14. Combine the salmon and mayonnaise:
  15. Add the chopped salmon to the flavored mayonnaise.
  16. Mix gently to coat the salmon.
  17. Marinate the salmon:
  18. Cover the salmon mixture with plastic wrap and refrigerate for 10-15 minutes.
  19. Plate the salmon tartar:
  20. Use a food ring to create a neat presentation.
  21. Fill the ring with the salmon mixture and press down to flatten.
  22. Carefully remove the ring.
  23. Garnish with additional capers, parsley, lemon slices, and a drizzle of olive oil.
  24. Serve with bread or biscuits.

salted_chicken_with_onion_garlic_and_tomatoes.txt - Salted Chicken with Onion, Garlic, and Tomatoes

Objectives

  • Learn to cook a simple, flavorful chicken dish with tomatoes.
  • Understand the importance of slow cooking onions for optimal flavor.
  • Create a delicious sauce using reduced wine and chicken stock.

Ingredients

  • 2 chicken breasts
  • 2 chicken thighs
  • Salt and pepper
  • Flour
  • 1 can chopped tomatoes
  • 1 onion
  • Garlic
  • Bay leaf
  • Thyme
  • Butter
  • White wine
  • Chicken stock (optional)
  • Olive oil

Instructions

  1. Salt and pepper the chicken breasts and thighs.
  2. Coat the chicken in flour to create a crispy skin.
  3. Heat olive oil and butter in a cast iron saute pan over medium heat.
  4. Place the chicken skin-side down in the pan and cook for 5 minutes per side.
  5. Remove the chicken and set aside.
  6. Add thyme and a bruised bay leaf to the pan.
  7. Reduce the heat to medium and add the onions.
  8. Cook the onions for 8-10 minutes until softened.
  9. Add the garlic and cook for 1 minute.
  10. Increase heat to high and deglaze the pan with white wine.
  11. Reduce the wine until almost completely evaporated.
  12. Add the chicken stock (optional) and reduce by half.
  13. Add the chopped tomatoes, fresh thyme, and cook for 2-3 minutes.
  14. Season the sauce with salt, pepper, and a pinch of sugar.
  15. Return the chicken to the pan, skin-side up.
  16. Baste the chicken with the sauce.
  17. Cover the pan and cook for 20 minutes.
  18. While the chicken is cooking, grill halved tomatoes for 5 minutes per side.
  19. Drizzle the grilled tomatoes with olive oil and sprinkle with oregano.
  20. Remove the chicken from the pan and set aside.
  21. Continue cooking the chicken thighs for an additional 10 minutes.
  22. Add a tablespoon of olive oil to the sauce to give it shine.
  23. Plate the chicken and tomatoes.
  24. Serve with bread, rice, or pasta.
